may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c771"><span class="c237">TRADE AND COOPERATION AGREEMENT BETWEEN THE EUROPEAN UNION AND THE &nbsp;EUROPEAN ATOMIC ENERGY COMMUNITY, OF THE ONE PART, AND THE UNITED KINGDOM &nbsp;OF GREAT BRITAIN AND NORTHERN IRELAND, OF THE OTHER PART </span></p><p class="c590"><span class="c27">PREAMBLE </span></p><p class="c854"><span class="c0">THE EUROPEAN UNION AND THE EUROPEAN ATOMIC ENERGY COMMUNITY &nbsp;AND &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c753"><span class="c0">THE UNITED KINGDOM OF GREAT BRITAIN AND NORTHERN IRELAND, </span></p><p class="c405"><span class="c27">REAFFIRMING their commitment to democratic principles, to the rule of law, to human rights, to &nbsp;countering proliferation of weapons of mass destruction and to the fight against climate change, which &nbsp;constitute essential elements of this and supplementing agreements, </span></p><p class="c117"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the importance of global cooperation to address issues of shared interest, </span></p><p class="c296"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the importance of transparency in international trade and investment to the benefit of &nbsp;all stakeholders, &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c416"><span class="c27">SEEKING to establish clear and mutually advantageous rules governing trade and investment between &nbsp;the Parties, </span></p><p class="c462"><span class="c27">CONSIDERING that in order to guarantee the efficient management and correct interpretation and &nbsp;application of this Agreement and any supplementing agreement as well as compliance with the &nbsp;obligations under those agreements, it is essential to establish provisions ensuring overall governance, &nbsp;in particular dispute settlement and enforcement rules that fully respect the autonomy of the &nbsp;respective legal orders of the Union and of the United Kingdom, as well as the United Kingdom&rsquo;s status &nbsp;as a country outside the European Union, </span></p><p class="c569"><span class="c27">BUILDING upon their respective rights and obligations under the Marrakesh Agreement Establishing &nbsp;the World Trade Organization, done on 15 April 1994, and other multilateral and bilateral instruments &nbsp;of cooperation, </span></p><p class="c92"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the Parties&rsquo; respective autonomy and rights to regulate within their territories in order &nbsp;to achieve legitimate public policy objectives such as the protection and promotion of public health, &nbsp;social services, public education, safety, the environment including climate change, public morals, &nbsp;social or consumer protection, animal welfare, privacy and data protection and the promotion and &nbsp;protection of cultural diversity, while striving to improve their respective high levels of protection, </span></p><p class="c797"><span class="c27">BELIEVING in the benefits of a predictable commercial environment that fosters trade and investment &nbsp;between them and prevents distortion of trade and unfair competitive advantages, in a manner &nbsp;conducive to sustainable development in its economic, social and environmental dimensions, </span></p><p class="c445"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the need for an ambitious, wide-ranging and balanced economic partnership to be &nbsp;underpinned by a level playing field for open and fair competition and sustainable development, &nbsp;through effective and robust frameworks for subsidies and competition and a commitment to uphold &nbsp;their respective high levels of protection in the areas of labour and social standards, environment, the &nbsp;fight against climate change, and taxation, </span></p><p class="c361"><span class="c0">6 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c58"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the need to ensure an open and secure market for businesses, including medium-sized enterprises, and their goods and services through addressing unjustified barriers to trade and &nbsp;investment, </span></p><p class="c156"><span class="c27">NOTING the importance of facilitating new opportunities for businesses and consumers through digital &nbsp;trade, and addressing unjustified barriers to data flows and trade enabled by electronic means, whilst &nbsp;respecting the Parties&#39; personal data protection rules, </span></p><p class="c403"><span class="c27">DESIRING that this Agreement contributes to consumer welfare through policies ensuring a high level &nbsp;of consumer protection and economic well-being, as well as encouraging cooperation between &nbsp;relevant authorities, </span></p><p class="c577"><span class="c27">CONSIDERING the importance of cross-border connectivity by air, by road and by sea, for passengers &nbsp;and for goods, and the need to ensure high standards in the provision of transportation services &nbsp;between the Parties, </span></p><p class="c359"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the benefits of trade and investment in energy and raw materials and the importance &nbsp;of supporting the delivery of cost efficient, clean and secure energy supplies to the Union and the &nbsp;United Kingdom, </span></p><p class="c850"><span class="c27">NOTING the interest of the Parties in establishing a framework to facilitate technical cooperation and &nbsp;develop new trading arrangements for interconnectors which deliver robust and efficient outcomes for &nbsp;all timeframes, </span></p><p class="c423"><span class="c27">NOTING that cooperation and trade between the Parties in these areas should be based on fair &nbsp;competition in energy markets and non-discriminatory access to networks, </span></p><p class="c584"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the benefits of sustainable energy, renewable energy, in particular offshore generation &nbsp;in the North Sea, and energy efficiency, </span></p><p class="c672"><span class="c27">DESIRING to promote the peaceful use of the waters adjacent to their coasts and the optimum and &nbsp;equitable utilisation of the marine living resources in those waters including the continued sustainable &nbsp;management of the shared stocks, </span></p><p class="c282"><span class="c27">NOTING that, the United Kingdom withdrew from the European Union and that with effect from 1 &nbsp;January 2021, the United Kingdom is an independent coastal State with corresponding rights and &nbsp;obligations under international law, </span></p><p class="c259"><span class="c27">AFFIRMING that the sovereign rights of the coastal States exercised by the Parties for the purpose of &nbsp;exploring, exploiting, conserving and managing the living resources in their waters should be &nbsp;conducted pursuant to and in accordance with the principles of international law, including the United &nbsp;Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea of 10 December 1982, </span></p><p class="c368"><span class="c27">RECOGNISING the importance of the coordination of social security rights enjoyed by persons moving &nbsp;between the Parties to work, to stay or to reside, as well as the rights enjoyed by their family members &nbsp;and survivors, &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c718"><span class="c27">CONSIDERING that cooperation in areas of shared interest, such as science, research and innovation, &nbsp;nuclear research or space, in the form of the participation of the United Kingdom in the corresponding &nbsp;Union programmes under fair and appropriate conditions will benefit both Parties,</span></p><p class="c377"><span class="c0">7 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c1"><span class="c27">CONSIDERING that cooperation between the United Kingdom and the Union relating to the prevention, &nbsp;investigation, detection or prosecution of criminal offences and to the execution of criminal penalties, &nbsp;including the safeguarding against and prevention of threats to public security, will enable the security &nbsp;of the United Kingdom and the Union to be strengthened, </span></p><p class="c470"><span class="c27">DESIRING that an agreement is concluded between the United Kingdom and the Union to provide a &nbsp;legal base for such cooperation, </span></p><p class="c128"><span class="c27">ACKNOWLEDGING that the Parties may supplement this Agreement with other agreements forming &nbsp;an integral part of their overall bilateral relations as governed by this Agreement and that the &nbsp;Agreement on Security Procedures for Exchanging and Protecting Classified Information is concluded &nbsp;as such a supplementing agreement, and enables the exchange of classified information between the &nbsp;Parties under this Agreement or any other supplementing agreement, </span></p><p class="c473"><span class="c0">HAVE AGREED AS FOLLOWS:</span></p><p class="c783"><span class="c0">8 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c24">PART ONE: COMMON AND INSTITUTIONAL PROVISIONS </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c27">TITLE I: GENERAL PROVISIONS </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article COMPROV.1: Purpose &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c599"><span class="c0">This Agreement establishes the basis for a broad relationship between the Parties, within an area of &nbsp;prosperity and good neighbourliness characterised by close and peaceful relations based on &nbsp;cooperation, respectful of the Parties&rsquo; autonomy and sovereignty. </span></p><p class="c582"><span class="c0">Article COMPROV.2: Supplementing agreements </span></p><p class="c539"><span class="c0">1. Where the Union and the United Kingdom conclude other bilateral agreements between &nbsp;them, such agreements shall constitute supplementing agreements to this Agreement, unless &nbsp;otherwise provided for in those agreements. Such supplementing agreements shall be an integral part &nbsp;of the overall bilateral relations as governed by this Agreement and shall form part of the overall &nbsp;framework. </span></p><p class="c63"><span class="c0">2. Paragraph 1 also applies to: </span></p><p class="c37"><span class="c0">(a) agreements between the Union and its Member States, of the one part, and the United &nbsp;Kingdom, of the other part; and </span></p><p class="c409"><span class="c0">(b) agreements between Euratom, of the one part, and the United Kingdom, of the other part. &nbsp;Article COMPROV.3: Good faith &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c631"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall, in full mutual respect and good faith, assist each other in carrying out tasks &nbsp;that flow from this Agreement and any supplementing agreement. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c744"><span class="c0">2. They shall take all appropriate measures, whether general or particular, to ensure the &nbsp;fulfilment of the obligations arising from this Agreement and from any supplementing agreement, and &nbsp;shall refrain from any measures which could jeopardise the attainment of the objectives of this &nbsp;Agreement or any supplementing agreement. </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c27">TITLE II: PRINCIPLES OF INTERPRETATION AND DEFINITIONS </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article COMPROV.13: Public international law &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c482"><span class="c0">1. The provisions of this Agreement and any supplementing agreement shall be interpreted in &nbsp;good faith in accordance with their ordinary meaning in their context and in light of the object and &nbsp;purpose of the agreement in accordance with customary rules of interpretation of public international &nbsp;law, including those codified in the Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties, done at Vienna on 23 &nbsp;May 1969. </span></p><p class="c244"><span class="c0">2. For greater certainty, neither this Agreement nor any supplementing agreement establishes &nbsp;an obligation to interpret their provisions in accordance with the domestic law of either Party. </span></p><p class="c341"><span class="c0">3. For greater certainty, an interpretation of this Agreement or any supplementing agreement &nbsp;given by the courts of either Party shall not be binding on the courts of the other Party.</span></p><p class="c776"><span class="c0">9 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article COMPROV.16: Private rights &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c199"><span class="c0">1. Without prejudice to Article MOBI.SSC.67 [Protection of individual rights] and with the &nbsp;exception, with regard to the Union, of Part Three [Law enforcement and judicial cooperation ], nothing in this Agreement or any supplementing agreement shall be construed as conferring rights or &nbsp;imposing obligations on persons other than those created between the Parties under public &nbsp;international law, nor as permitting this Agreement or any supplementing agreement to be directly &nbsp;invoked in the domestic legal systems of the Parties. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c722"><span class="c0">2. A Party shall not provide for a right of action under its law against the other Party on the &nbsp;ground that the other Party has acted in breach of this Agreement or any supplementing agreement. </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article COMPROV.17: Definitions </span></p><p class="c604"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of this Agreement and any supplementing agreement, and unless otherwise &nbsp;specified, the following definitions apply</span><span class="c24">: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c127"><span class="c0">(a) &ldquo;data subject&rdquo; means an identified or identifiable natural person; an identifiable person being &nbsp;a person who can be identified, directly or indirectly, in particular by reference to an identifier &nbsp;such as a name, an identification number, location data or an online identifier, or to one or &nbsp;more factors specific to the physical, physiological, genetic, mental, economic, cultural or social &nbsp;identity of that natural person; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) &ldquo;day&rdquo; means a calendar day; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) &ldquo;Member State&rdquo; means a Member State of the European Union; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(d) &ldquo;personal data&rdquo; means any information relating to a data subject; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(e) &ldquo;State&rdquo; means a Member State or the United Kingdom, as the context requires; </span></p><p class="c585"><span class="c0">(f) &ldquo;territory&rdquo; of a Party means in respect of each Party the territories to which the Agreement &nbsp;applies in accordance with Article FINPROV.1 [Territorial scope]; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c555"><span class="c0">(g) &ldquo;the transition period&rdquo; means the transition period provided for in Article 126 of the &nbsp;Withdrawal Agreement; and </span></p><p class="c334"><span class="c0">(h) &ldquo;Withdrawal Agreement&rdquo; means the Agreement on the withdrawal of the United Kingdom of &nbsp;Great Britain and Northern Ireland from the European Union and the European Atomic Energy &nbsp;Community, including its Protocols. </span></p><p class="c544"><span class="c0">2. Any reference to the &ldquo;Union&rdquo;, &ldquo;Party&rdquo; or &ldquo;Parties&rdquo; in this Agreement or any supplementing &nbsp;agreement shall be understood as not including the European Atomic Energy Community, unless &nbsp;otherwise specified or where the context otherwise requires. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c27">TITLE III: INSTITUTIONAL FRAMEWORK </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article INST.1: Partnership Council </span></p><p class="c360"><span class="c0">1. A Partnership Council is hereby established. It shall comprise representatives of the Union and &nbsp;of the United Kingdom. The Partnership Council may meet in different configurations depending on &nbsp;the matters under discussion. </span></p><p class="c26"><span class="c0">10 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c279"><span class="c0">2. The Partnership Council shall be co-chaired by a Member of the European Commission and a &nbsp;representative of the Government of the United Kingdom at ministerial level. It shall meet at the &nbsp;request of the Union or the United Kingdom, and, in any event, at least once a year, and shall set its &nbsp;meeting schedule and its agenda by mutual consent. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c424"><span class="c0">3. The Partnership Council shall oversee the attainment of the objectives of this Agreement and &nbsp;any supplementing agreement. It shall supervise and facilitate the implementation and application of &nbsp;this Agreement and of any supplementing agreement. Each Party may refer to the Partnership Council &nbsp;any issue relating to the implementation, application and interpretation of this Agreement or of any &nbsp;supplementing agreement. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c841"><span class="c0">4. The Partnership Council shall have the power to: </span></p><p class="c676"><span class="c0">(a) adopt decisions in respect of all matters where this Agreement or any supplementing &nbsp;agreement so provides; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c694"><span class="c0">(b) make recommendations to the Parties regarding the implementation and application of this &nbsp;Agreement or of any supplementing agreement; </span></p><p class="c321"><span class="c0">(c) adopt, by decision, amendments to this Agreement or to any supplementing agreement in the &nbsp;cases provided for in this Agreement or in any supplementing agreement; </span></p><p class="c263"><span class="c0">(d) except in relation to Title III [Institutional Framework] of Part One [Common and institutional &nbsp;provisions], until the end of the fourth year following the entry into force of this Agreement, &nbsp;adopt decisions amending this Agreement or any supplementing agreement, provided that such &nbsp;amendments are necessary to correct errors, or to address omissions or other deficiencies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c538"><span class="c0">(e) discuss any matter related to the areas covered by this Agreement or by any supplementing &nbsp;agreement; </span></p><p class="c104"><span class="c0">(f) delegate certain of its powers to the Trade Partnership Committee or to a Specialised &nbsp;Committee, except those powers and responsibilities referred to in point (g) of Article INST.1(4) &nbsp;[Partnership Council]; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c517"><span class="c0">(g) by decision, establish Trade Specialised Committees and Specialised Committees, other than &nbsp;those referred to in Article INST.2(1) [Committees], dissolve any Trade Specialised Committee &nbsp;or Specialised Committee, or change the tasks assigned to them; and </span></p><p class="c13"><span class="c0">(h) </span><span class="c91">make recommendations to the Parties regarding the transfer of personal data in </span><span class="c0">specific </span><span class="c91">areas &nbsp;covered by this Agreement or any supplementing agreement. </span></p><p class="c738"><span class="c0">5. The work of the Partnership Council shall be governed by the rules of procedure set out in &nbsp;ANNEX INST-1 [Rules of Procedure of the Partnership Council and Committees]. The Partnership &nbsp;Council may amend that Annex. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c589"><span class="c0">Article INST.2: Committees </span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0">1. The following Committees are hereby established: </span></p><p class="c100"><span class="c0">(a) the Trade Partnership Committee, which addresses matters covered by Titles I to VII, Chapter 4 &nbsp;[Energy goods and raw materials] of Title VIII, Titles IX to XII of Heading One [Trade] of Part Two, </span></p><p class="c328"><span class="c0">11 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c30"><span class="c0">Heading Six [Other provisions] of Part Two, and Annex ENER-2 [ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL &nbsp;SUBSIDIES]; </span></p><p class="c233"><span class="c0">(b) the Trade Specialised Committee on Goods which addresses matters covered by Chapter 1 of &nbsp;Title I of Heading One of Part Two and Chapter four [Energy goods and raw materials] of Title &nbsp;VIII of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c20"><span class="c0">(c) the Trade Specialised Committee on Customs Cooperation and Rules of Origin, which addresses &nbsp;matters covered by Chapters 2 and 5 of Title I of Heading One of Part Two, the Protocol on &nbsp;mutual administrative assistance in customs matters and the provisions on customs &nbsp;enforcement of intellectual property rights, fees and charges, customs valuation and repaired &nbsp;goods; </span></p><p class="c76"><span class="c0">(d) the Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures, which addresses &nbsp;matters covered by Chapter 3 of Title I of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c338"><span class="c0">(e) the Trade Specialised Committee on Technical Barriers to Trade, which addresses matters &nbsp;covered by Chapter 4 of Title I of Heading One of Part Two and Article ENER.25 [Cooperation on &nbsp;standards] of Title VIII [Energy] of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c713"><span class="c0">(f) the Trade Specialised Committee on Services, Investment and Digital Trade, which addresses &nbsp;matters covered by Titles II to IV of Heading One of Part Two and Chapter 4 [Energy Goods and &nbsp;Raw Materials] of Title VIII of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c670"><span class="c0">(g) the Trade Specialised Committee on Intellectual Property, which addresses matters covered by &nbsp;Title V of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c690"><span class="c0">(h) the Trade Specialised Committee on Public Procurement, which addresses matters covered by &nbsp;Title VI of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c426"><span class="c0">(i) the Trade Specialised Committee on Regulatory Cooperation, which addresses matters covered &nbsp;by Title X of Heading One of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c53"><span class="c0">(j) the Trade Specialised Committee on Level Playing Field for Open and Fair Competition and &nbsp;Sustainable Development, which addresses matters covered by Title XI of Heading One of Part &nbsp;Two and Annex ENER-2 [ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL SUBSIDIES]; </span></p><p class="c334"><span class="c0">(k) the Trade Specialised Committee on Administrative Cooperation in VAT and Recovery of Taxes &nbsp;and Duties, which addresses matters covered by the Protocol on administrative cooperation &nbsp;and combating fraud in the field of Value Added Tax and on mutual assistance for the recovery &nbsp;of claims relating to taxes and duties;] </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(l) the Specialised Committee on Energy, &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c501"><span class="c0">(i) which addresses matters covered by Title VIII of Heading One of Part Two, with the &nbsp;exception of Chapter 4 [Energy Goods and Raw Materials], Article ENER.25 &nbsp;[Cooperation on Standards] and Annex ENER-2 [ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL &nbsp;SUBSIDIES], and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c552"><span class="c0">(ii) which can discuss and provide expertise to the relevant Trade Specialised Committee &nbsp;on matters pertaining to Chapter four [Energy Goods and Raw Materials] and Article &nbsp;ENER.25 [Cooperation on Standards] of Title VIII of Heading One of Part Two;</span></p><p class="c257"><span class="c0">12 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c236"><span class="c0">(m) the Specialised Committee on Air Transport, which addresses matters covered by Title I of &nbsp;Heading Two of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c683"><span class="c0">(n) the Specialised Committee on Aviation Safety, which addresses matters covered by Title II of &nbsp;Heading Two of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c634"><span class="c0">(o) the Specialised Committee on Road Transport, which addresses matters covered by Heading &nbsp;Three [Road Transport] of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c847"><span class="c0">(p) the Specialised Committee on Social Security Coordination, which addresses matters covered &nbsp;by Heading Four of Part Two and the Protocol on Social Security Coordination; </span></p><p class="c531"><span class="c0">(q) the Specialised Committee on Fisheries, which addresses matters covered by Heading Five &nbsp;[Fisheries] of Part Two; </span></p><p class="c587"><span class="c0">(r) the Specialised Committee on Law Enforcement and Judicial Cooperation, which addresses &nbsp;matters covered by Part Three [Law enforcement and judicial cooperation in criminal matters]; &nbsp;and </span></p><p class="c734"><span class="c0">(s) the Specialised Committee on Participation in Union Programmes, which addresses matters &nbsp;covered by Part Five [Union programmes]. </span></p><p class="c551"><span class="c0">2. With respect to issues related to Titles I to VII, Chapter 4 [Energy goods and raw materials] of &nbsp;Title VIII, Titles IX to XII of Heading One [Trade] of Part Two, Heading Six [Other provisions] of Part Two &nbsp;and Annex ENER-2 [ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL SUBSIDIES], the Trade Partnership Committee &nbsp;referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article shall have the power to: </span></p><p class="c179"><span class="c0">(a) assist the Partnership Council in the performance of its tasks and, in particular, report to the &nbsp;Partnership Council and carry out any task assigned to it by the latter; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) supervise the implementation of this Agreement or any supplementing agreement; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c880"><span class="c0">(c) adopt decisions or make recommendations as provided for in this Agreement or any &nbsp;supplementing agreement or where such power has been delegated to it by the Partnership &nbsp;Council; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c120"><span class="c0">(d) supervise the work of the Trade Specialised Committees referred to in paragraph 1 of this &nbsp;Article; </span></p><p class="c191"><span class="c0">(e) explore the most appropriate way to prevent or solve any difficulty that may arise in relation to &nbsp;the interpretation and application of this Agreement or any supplementing agreement, without &nbsp;prejudice to Title I [Dispute settlement] of Part Six ; </span></p><p class="c574"><span class="c0">(f) exercise the powers delegated to it by the Partnership Council pursuant to point (f) of Article &nbsp;INST.1(4) [Partnership Council]; </span></p><p class="c229"><span class="c0">(g) establish, by decision, Trade Specialised Committees other than those referred to in paragraph &nbsp;1 of this Article, dissolve any such Trade Specialised Committee, or change the tasks assigned &nbsp;to them; and </span></p><p class="c224"><span class="c0">(h) establish, supervise, coordinate and dissolve Working Groups, or delegate their supervision to &nbsp;a Trade Specialised Committee.</span></p><p class="c299"><span class="c0">13 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c741"><span class="c0">3. With respect to issues related to their area of competence, Trade Specialised Committees &nbsp;shall have the power to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c211"><span class="c0">(a) monitor and review the implementation and ensure the proper functioning of this Agreement &nbsp;or any supplementing agreement; </span></p><p class="c102"><span class="c0">(b) assist the Trade Partnership Committee in the performance of its tasks and, in particular, report &nbsp;to the Trade Partnership Committee and carry out any task assigned to them by it; </span></p><p class="c404"><span class="c0">(c) conduct the preparatory technical work necessary to support the functions of the Partnership &nbsp;Council and the Trade Partnership Committee, including when those bodies have to adopt &nbsp;decisions or recommendations; </span></p><p class="c689"><span class="c0">(d) adopt decisions in respect of all matters where this Agreement or any supplementing &nbsp;agreement so provides; </span></p><p class="c558"><span class="c0">(e) discuss technical issues arising from the implementation of this Agreement or of any &nbsp;supplementing agreement, without prejudice to Title I [Dispute Settlement] of Part Six; and </span></p><p class="c371"><span class="c0">(f) provide a forum for the Parties to exchange information, discuss best practices and share &nbsp;implementation experience. </span></p><p class="c866"><span class="c0">4. With respect to issues related to their area of competence, Specialised Committees shall have &nbsp;the power to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c289"><span class="c0">(a) monitor and review the implementation and ensure the proper functioning of this Agreement &nbsp;or any supplementing agreement; </span></p><p class="c179"><span class="c0">(b) assist the Partnership Council in the performance of its tasks and, in particular, report to the &nbsp;Partnership Council and carry out any task assigned to them by it; </span></p><p class="c132"><span class="c0">(c) adopt decisions, including amendments, and recommendations in respect of all matters where &nbsp;this Agreement or any supplementing agreement so provides or for which the Partnership &nbsp;Council has delegated its powers to a Specialised Committee in accordance with point (f) of &nbsp;Article INST.1(4) [Partnership Council]; </span></p><p class="c663"><span class="c0">(d) discuss technical issues arising from the implementation of this Agreement or any &nbsp;supplementing agreement; </span></p><p class="c492"><span class="c0">(e) provide a forum for the Parties to exchange information, discuss best practices and share &nbsp;implementation experience; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(f) establish, supervise, coordinate and dissolve Working Groups; and </span></p><p class="c662"><span class="c0">(g) provide a forum for consultation pursuant to Article INST.13(7) [Consultations] of Title I [Dispute &nbsp;Settlement] of Part Six. </span></p><p class="c245"><span class="c0">5. Committees shall comprise representatives of each Party. Each Party shall ensure that its &nbsp;representatives on the Committees have the appropriate expertise with respect to the issues under &nbsp;discussion.</span></p><p class="c278"><span class="c0">14 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c340"><span class="c0">6. The Trade Partnership Committee shall be co-chaired by a senior representative of the Union &nbsp;and a representative of the United Kingdom with responsibility for trade-related matters, or their &nbsp;designees. It shall meet at the request of the Union or the United Kingdom, and, in any event, at least &nbsp;once a year, and shall set its meeting schedule and its agenda by mutual consent. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c605"><span class="c0">7. The Trade Specialised Committees and the Specialised Committees shall be co-chaired by a &nbsp;representative of the Union and a representative of the United Kingdom. Unless otherwise provided &nbsp;for in this Agreement, or unless the co-chairs decide otherwise, they shall meet at least once a year. </span></p><p class="c117"><span class="c0">8. Committees shall set their meeting schedule and agenda by mutual consent. </span></p><p class="c118"><span class="c0">9. The work of the Committees shall be governed by the rules of procedure set out in ANNEX &nbsp;INST-X [Rules of Procedure of the Partnership Council and Committees]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c305"><span class="c0">10. By derogation from paragraph 9, a Committee may adopt and subsequently amend its own &nbsp;rules that shall govern its work. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article INST.3: Working Groups </span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0">1. The following Working Groups are hereby established: </span></p><p class="c614"><span class="c0">(a) the Working Group on Organic Products, under the supervision of the Trade Specialised Committee &nbsp;on Technical Barriers to Trade; </span></p><p class="c324"><span class="c0">(b) the Working Group on Motor Vehicles and Parts, under the supervision of the Trade Specialised &nbsp;Committee on Technical Barriers to Trade; </span></p><p class="c610"><span class="c0">(c) the Working Group on Medicinal Products, under the supervision of the Trade Specialised &nbsp;Committee on Technical Barriers to Trade; </span></p><p class="c864"><span class="c0">(d) the Working Group on Social Security Coordination, under the supervision of the Specialised &nbsp;Committee on Social Security Coordination; </span></p><p class="c699"><span class="c0">2. Working Groups shall, under the supervision of Committees, assist Committees in the &nbsp;performance of their tasks and, in particular, prepare the work of Committees and carry out any task &nbsp;assigned to them by the latter. </span></p><p class="c175"><span class="c0">3. Working Groups shall comprise representatives of the Union and of the United Kingdom and &nbsp;shall be co-chaired by a representative of the Union and a representative of the United Kingdom. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c197"><span class="c0">4. Working Groups shall set their own rules of procedure, meeting schedule and agenda by &nbsp;mutual consent. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article INST.4: Decisions and recommendations </span></p><p class="c827"><span class="c0">1. The decisions adopted by the Partnership Council, or, as the case may be, by a Committee, &nbsp;shall be binding on the Parties and on all the bodies set up under this Agreement and under any &nbsp;supplementing agreement, including the arbitration tribunal referred to in Title I [Dispute settlement] &nbsp;of Part Six. Recommendations shall have no binding force. </span></p><p class="c80"><span class="c0">2. The Partnership Council or, as the case may be, a Committee, shall adopt decisions and make &nbsp;recommendations by mutual consent.</span></p><p class="c82"><span class="c0">15 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article INST.5: Parliamentary cooperation </span></p><p class="c454"><span class="c0">1. The European Parliament and the Parliament of the United Kingdom may establish a &nbsp;Parliamentary Partnership Assembly consisting of Members of the European Parliament and of &nbsp;Members of the Parliament of the United Kingdom, as a forum to exchange views on the partnership. </span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. Upon its establishment, the Parliamentary Partnership Assembly: </span></p><p class="c241"><span class="c0">(a) may request relevant information regarding the implementation of this Agreement and any &nbsp;supplementing agreement from the Partnership Council, which shall then supply that Assembly &nbsp;with the requested information; </span></p><p class="c887"><span class="c0">(b) shall be informed of the decisions and recommendations of the Partnership Council; and (c) may make recommendations to the Partnership Council. </span></p><p class="c395"><span class="c0">Article INST.6: Participation of civil society </span></p><p class="c36"><span class="c0">The Parties shall consult civil society on the implementation of this Agreement and any supplementing &nbsp;agreement, in particular through interaction with the domestic advisory groups and the Civil Society &nbsp;Forum referred to in Articles INST.7 [Domestic advisory groups] and INST.8 [Civil Society Forum]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article INST.7: Domestic advisory groups </span></p><p class="c396"><span class="c0 c108">1. Each Party shall consult on issues covered by this Agreement and any supplementing </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">agreement its newly created or existing domestic advisory group or groups comprising a </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">representation of independent civil society organisations including non-governmental organisations, </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">business and employers&#39; organisations, as well as trade unions, active in economic, sustainable </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">development, social, human rights, environmental and other matters. Each Party may convene its </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">domestic advisory group or groups in different configurations to discuss the implementation of </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;different provisions of this Agreement or of any supplementing agreement. </span></p><p class="c286"><span class="c0 c108">2. Each Party shall consider views or recommendations submitted by its domestic advisory group </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">or groups. Representatives of each Party shall aim to consult with their respective domestic advisory </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;group or groups at least once a year. Meetings may be held by virtual means. </span></p><p class="c762"><span class="c0 c108">3. In order to promote public awareness of the domestic advisory groups, each Party shall </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">endeavour to publish the list of organisations participating in its domestic advisory group or groups as </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;well as the contact point for that or those groups. </span></p><p class="c671"><span class="c0 c108">4. The Parties shall promote interaction between their respective domestic advisory groups, </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">including by exchanging where possible the contact details of members of their domestic advisory </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">groups.</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c494"><span class="c0">Article INST.8: Civil Society Forum </span></p><p class="c105"><span class="c0 c108">1. The Parties shall facilitate the organisation of a Civil Society Forum to conduct a dialogue on </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">the implementation of Part Two of this Agreement. The Partnership Council shall adopt operational </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;guidelines for the conduct of the Forum. </span></p><p class="c121"><span class="c0 c108">2. The Civil Society Forum shall meet at least once a year, unless otherwise agreed by the Parties. </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">The Civil Society Forum may meet by virtual means.</span></p><p class="c32"><span class="c0">16 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c821"><span class="c0">3. The Civil Society Forum shall be open for the participation of independent civil society &nbsp;organisations established in the territories of the Parties, including members of the domestic advisory &nbsp;groups referred to in Article INST.7 [Domestic advisory groups]. Each Party shall promote a balanced &nbsp;representation, including non-governmental organisations, business and employers&acute; organisations &nbsp;and trade unions, active in economic, sustainable development, social, human rights, environmental &nbsp;and other matters.</span></p><p class="c336"><span class="c0">17 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c24">PART TWO: TRADE, TRANSPORT, FISHERIES AND OTHER ARRANGEMENTS </span></p><p class="c859"><span class="c0">HEADING ONE: TRADE </span></p><p class="c381"><span class="c27">TITLE I: TRADE IN GOODS </span></p><p class="c97"><span class="c0">Chapter 1: National treatment and market access for goods (including trade remedies) Article GOODS.1: Objective </span></p><p class="c817"><span class="c0">The objective of this Chapter is to facilitate trade in goods between the Parties and to maintain &nbsp;liberalised trade in goods in accordance with the provisions of this Agreement. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.2: Scope </span></p><p class="c89"><span class="c0">Except as otherwise provided, this Chapter applies to trade in goods of a Party. Article GOODS.3: Definitions </span></p><p class="c497"><span class="c0">For the purposes of this Chapter, the following definitions apply: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c879"><span class="c0">(a) &ldquo;consular transactions&rdquo; means the procedure of obtaining from a consul of the importing Party &nbsp;in the territory of the exporting Party, or in the territory of a third party, a consular invoice or a &nbsp;consular visa for a commercial invoice, certificate of origin, manifest, shipper&rsquo;s export &nbsp;declaration or any other customs documentation in connection with the importation of the &nbsp;good; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c496"><span class="c0">(b) &ldquo;Customs Valuation Agreement&rdquo; means the Agreement on Implementation of Article VII of &nbsp;GATT 1994; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c33"><span class="c0">(c) &ldquo;export licensing procedure&rdquo; means an administrative procedure, whether or not referred to as &nbsp;licensing, used by a Party for the operation of export licensing regimes, requiring the submission &nbsp;of an application or other documentation, other than that generally required for customs &nbsp;clearance purposes, to the relevant administrative body as a prior condition for exportation &nbsp;from that Party; </span></p><p class="c453"><span class="c0">(d) &ldquo;import licensing procedure&rdquo; means an administrative procedure, whether or not referred to &nbsp;as licensing, used by a Party for the operation of import licensing regimes, requiring the &nbsp;submission of an application or other documentation, other than that generally required for &nbsp;customs clearance purposes, to the relevant administrative body or bodies as a prior condition &nbsp;for importation into the territory of the importing Party; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c13"><span class="c0">(e) &ldquo;originating goods&rdquo; means, unless otherwise provided, a good qualifying under the rules of &nbsp;origin set out in Chapter 2 [Rules of origin] of this Title; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(f) &ldquo;performance requirement&rdquo; means a requirement that: </span></p><p class="c78"><span class="c0">(i) a given quantity, value or percentage of goods be exported; </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">(ii) goods of the Party granting an import licence be substituted for imported goods; </span></p><p class="c437"><span class="c0">18 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c829"><span class="c0">(iii) a person benefiting from an import licence purchase other goods in the territory of the &nbsp;Party granting the import licence, or accord a preference to domestically produced &nbsp;goods; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c271"><span class="c0">(iv) a person benefiting from an import licence produce goods in the territory of the Party &nbsp;granting the import licence, with a given quantity, value or percentage of domestic &nbsp;content; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c886"><span class="c0">(v) relates in whatever form to the volume or value of imports, to the volume or value of &nbsp;exports or to the amount of foreign exchange flows; </span></p><p class="c867"><span class="c0">(g) &ldquo;remanufactured good&rdquo; means a good classified in HS Chapters 32, 40, 84 to 90, 94 or 95 that: &nbsp;(i) is entirely or partially composed of parts obtained from used goods; &nbsp;(ii) has similar life expectancy and performance compared with such goods, when new; and &nbsp;(iii) is given an equivalent warranty to as that applicable to such goods when new; and </span></p><p class="c586"><span class="c0">(h) &ldquo;repair&rdquo; means any processing operation undertaken on a good to remedy operating defects or &nbsp;material damage and entailing the re-establishment of the good to its original function or to &nbsp;ensure compliance with technical requirements for its use. Repair of a good includes restoration &nbsp;and maintenance, with a possible increase in the value of the good from restoring the original &nbsp;functionality of that good, but does not include an operation or process that: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c149"><span class="c0">(i) destroys the essential characteristics of a good, or creates a new or commercially &nbsp;different good; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c180"><span class="c0">(ii) transforms an unfinished good into a finished good; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c440"><span class="c0">(iii) is used to improve or upgrade the technical performance of a good. &nbsp;Article GOODS.3A: Classification of goods </span></p><p class="c836"><span class="c0">The classification of goods in trade between the Parties under this Agreement is set out in each Party&rsquo;s &nbsp;respective tariff nomenclature in conformity with the Harmonised System. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.4: National treatment on internal taxation and regulation </span></p><p class="c769"><span class="c0">Each Party shall accord national treatment to the goods of the other Party in accordance with Article &nbsp;III of GATT 1994 including its Notes and Supplementary Provisions. To this end, Article III of GATT 1994 &nbsp;and its Notes and Supplementary Provisions are incorporated into and made part of this Agreement, &nbsp;</span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.4A: Freedom of transit </span></p><p class="c642"><span class="c0">Each Party shall accord freedom of transit through its territory, via the routes most convenient for &nbsp;international transit, for traffic in transit to or from the territory of the other Party or of any other &nbsp;third country. To this end, Article V of GATT 1994 and its Notes and Supplementary Provisions are &nbsp;incorporated into and made part of this Agreement, </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. The Parties understand that &nbsp;Article V of GATT 1994 includes the movement of energy goods via </span><span class="c27">inter alia </span><span class="c0">pipelines or electricity &nbsp;grids. </span></p><p class="c82"><span class="c0">19 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.5: Prohibition of customs duties </span></p><p class="c793"><span class="c0">Except as otherwise provided for in this Agreement, customs duties on all goods originating in the &nbsp;other Party shall be prohibited. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.6: Export duties, taxes or other charges </span></p><p class="c540"><span class="c0">1. A Party may not adopt or maintain any duty, tax or other charge of any kind imposed on, or in &nbsp;connection with, the exportation of a good to the other Party; or any internal tax or other charge on &nbsp;a good exported to the other Party that is in excess of the tax or charge that would be imposed on like &nbsp;goods when destined for domestic consumption. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c69"><span class="c0">2. For the purpose of this Article, the term &lsquo;other charge of any kind&rsquo; does not include fees or &nbsp;other charges that are permitted under Article GOODS.7 [Fees and formalities]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.7: Fees and formalities </span></p><p class="c11"><span class="c0">1. Fees and other charges imposed by a Party on or in connection with importation or &nbsp;exportation of a good of the other Party shall be limited in amount to the approximate cost of the &nbsp;services rendered, and shall not represent an indirect protection to domestic goods or taxation of &nbsp;imports or exports for fiscal purposes. A Party shall not levy fees or other charges on or in connection &nbsp;with importation or exportation on an </span><span class="c27">ad valorem </span><span class="c0">basis. </span></p><p class="c872"><span class="c0">2. Each Party may impose charges or recover costs only where specific services are rendered, in &nbsp;particular, but not limited to, the following: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c253"><span class="c0">(a) attendance, where requested, by customs staff outside official office hours or at premises other &nbsp;than customs premises; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c223"><span class="c0">(b) analyses or expert reports on goods and postal fees for the return of goods to an applicant, &nbsp;particularly in respect of decisions relating to binding information or the provision of &nbsp;information concerning the application of the customs laws and regulations; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c150"><span class="c0">(c) the examination or sampling of goods for verification purposes, or the destruction of goods, &nbsp;where costs other than the cost of using customs staff are involved; and </span></p><p class="c281"><span class="c0">(d) exceptional control measures, if these are necessary due to the nature of the goods or to a &nbsp;potential risk. </span></p><p class="c29"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall promptly publish all fees and charges it imposes in connection with &nbsp;importation or exportation via an official website in such a manner as to enable governments, traders &nbsp;and other interested parties, to become acquainted with them. That information shall include the &nbsp;reason for the fee or charge for the service provided, the responsible authority, the fees and charges &nbsp;that will be applied, and when and how payment is to be made. New or amended fees and charges &nbsp;shall not be imposed until information in accordance with this paragraph has been published and &nbsp;made readily available. </span></p><p class="c47"><span class="c0">4. A Party shall not require consular transactions, including related fees and charges, in &nbsp;connection with the importation of any good of the other Party.</span></p><p class="c205"><span class="c0">20 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.8: Repaired goods </span></p><p class="c212"><span class="c0">1. A Party shall not apply a customs duty to a good, regardless of its origin, that re-enters the &nbsp;Party&rsquo;s territory after that good has been temporarily exported from its territory to the territory of &nbsp;the other Party for repair. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c708"><span class="c0">2. Paragraph 1 does not apply to a good imported in bond, into free trade zones, or in similar &nbsp;status, that is then exported for repair and is not re-imported in bond, into free trade zones, or in &nbsp;similar status. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c523"><span class="c0">3. A Party shall not apply a customs duty to a good, regardless of its origin, imported temporarily &nbsp;from the territory of the other Party for repair. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.9: Remanufactured goods </span></p><p class="c390"><span class="c0">1. A Party shall not accord to remanufactured goods of the other Party treatment that is less &nbsp;favourable than that which it accords to equivalent goods in new condition. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c491"><span class="c0">2. Article GOODS.10 [Import and export restrictions] applies to import and export prohibitions &nbsp;or restrictions on remanufactured goods. If a Party adopts or maintains import and export prohibitions &nbsp;or restrictions on used goods, it shall not apply those measures to remanufactured goods. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c760"><span class="c0">3. A Party may require that remanufactured goods be identified as such for distribution or sale &nbsp;in its territory and that they meet all applicable technical requirements that apply to equivalent goods &nbsp;in new condition. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.10: Import and export restrictions </span></p><p class="c252"><span class="c0">1. A Party shall not adopt or maintain any prohibition or restriction on the importation of any &nbsp;good of the other Party or on the exportation or sale for export of any good destined for the territory &nbsp;of the other Party, except in accordance with Article XI of GATT 1994, including its Notes and &nbsp;Supplementary Provisions. To this end, Article XI of GATT 1994 and its Notes and Supplementary &nbsp;Provisions are incorporated into and made part of this Agreement, </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. A Party shall not adopt or maintain: </span></p><p class="c583"><span class="c0">(a) export and import price requirements, except as permitted in enforcement of countervailing &nbsp;and anti-dumping duty orders and undertakings; or </span></p><p class="c720"><span class="c0">(b) import licensing conditioned on the fulfilment of a performance requirement. Article GOODS.11: Import and export monopolies </span></p><p class="c851"><span class="c0">A Party shall not designate or maintain an import or export monopoly. For the purposes of this Article, &nbsp;import or export monopoly means the exclusive right or grant of authority by a Party to an entity to &nbsp;import a good from, or export a good to, the other Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS. 13: Import licensing procedures </span></p><p class="c215"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall ensure that all import licensing procedures applicable to trade in goods &nbsp;between the Parties are neutral in application, and are administered in a fair, equitable, non discriminatory and transparent manner.</span></p><p class="c82"><span class="c0">21 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c553"><span class="c0">2. A Party shall only adopt or maintain licensing procedures as a condition for importation into &nbsp;its territory from the territory of the other Party, if other appropriate procedures to achieve an &nbsp;administrative purpose are not reasonably available. </span></p><p class="c34"><span class="c0">3. A Party shall not adopt or maintain any non-automatic import licensing procedure, unless it is &nbsp;necessary to implement a measure that is consistent with this Agreement. A Party adopting such non automatic import licensing procedure shall indicate clearly the measure being implemented through &nbsp;that procedure. </span></p><p class="c113"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall introduce and administer any import licensing procedure in accordance with &nbsp;Articles 1 to 3 of the WTO Agreement on Import Licensing Procedures (&lsquo;the Import Licensing &nbsp;Agreement&rsquo;). To this end, Articles 1 to 3 of the Import Licensing Agreement are incorporated into and &nbsp;made part of this Agreement </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. </span></p><p class="c302"><span class="c0">5. Any Party introducing or modifying any import licensing procedure shall make all relevant &nbsp;information available online on an official website. That information shall be made available, &nbsp;whenever practicable, at least 21 days prior to the date of the application of the new or modified &nbsp;licensing procedure and in any event no later than the date of application. That information shall &nbsp;contain the data required under Article 5 of the Import Licensing Agreement. </span></p><p class="c460"><span class="c0">6. At the request of the other Party, a Party shall promptly provide any relevant information &nbsp;regarding any import licensing procedures that it intends to adopt or that it maintains, including the &nbsp;information referred to in Articles 1 to 3 of the Import Licensing Agreement. </span></p><p class="c196"><span class="c0">7. For greater certainty, nothing in this Article requires a Party to grant an import licence, or &nbsp;prevents a Party from implementing its obligations or commitments under United Nations Security &nbsp;Council Resolutions or under multilateral non-proliferation regimes and import control arrangements. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS. 14: Export licensing procedures </span></p><p class="c554"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall publish any new export licensing procedure, or any modification to an existing &nbsp;export licensing procedure, in such a manner as to enable governments, traders and other interested &nbsp;parties to become acquainted with them. Such publication shall take place, whenever practicable, 45 &nbsp;days before the procedure or modification takes effect, and in any case no later than the date such &nbsp;procedure or modification takes effect and, where appropriate, publication shall take place on any &nbsp;relevant government websites. </span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. The publication of export licensing procedures shall include the following information: </span></p><p class="c456"><span class="c0">(a) the texts of its export licensing procedures, or of any modifications it makes to those &nbsp;procedures; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) the goods subject to each licensing procedure; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c542"><span class="c0">(c) for each procedure, a description of the process for applying for a licence and any criteria an &nbsp;applicant must meet to be eligible to apply for a licence, such as possessing an activity licence, &nbsp;establishing or maintaining an investment, or operating through a particular form of &nbsp;establishment in a Party&rsquo;s territory; </span></p><p class="c638"><span class="c0">(d) a contact point or points from which interested persons can obtain further information on the &nbsp;conditions for obtaining an export licence; </span></p><p class="c600"><span class="c0">22 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c375"><span class="c0">(e) the administrative body or bodies to which an application or other relevant documentation are &nbsp;to be submitted; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c891"><span class="c0">(f) a description of any measure or measures being implemented through the export licensing &nbsp;procedure; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c101"><span class="c0">(g) the period during which each export licensing procedure will be in effect, unless the procedure &nbsp;remains in effect until withdrawn or revised in a new publication; </span></p><p class="c463"><span class="c0">(h) if the Party intends to use a licensing procedure to administer an export quota, the overall &nbsp;quantity and, if applicable, the value of the quota and the opening and closing dates of the &nbsp;quota; and </span></p><p class="c159"><span class="c0">(i) any exemptions or exceptions that replace the requirement to obtain an export licence, how to &nbsp;request or use those exemptions or exceptions, and the criteria for granting them. </span></p><p class="c379"><span class="c0">3. Within 45 days after the date of entry into force of this Agreement, each Party shall notify the &nbsp;other Party of its existing export licensing procedures. Each Party shall notify to the other Party any &nbsp;new export licensing procedures and any modifications to existing export licensing procedures within &nbsp;60 days of publication. The notification shall include a reference to the sources where the information &nbsp;required pursuant to paragraph 2 is published and shall include, where appropriate, the address of &nbsp;the relevant government websites. </span></p><p class="c290"><span class="c0">4. For greater certainty, nothing in this Article requires a Party to grant an export licence, or &nbsp;prevents a Party from implementing its commitments under United Nations Security Council &nbsp;Resolutions as well as under multilateral non-proliferation regimes and export control arrangements including the Wassenaar Arrangement on Export Controls for Conventional Arms and Dual-Use Goods &nbsp;and Technologies, the Australia Group, the Nuclear Suppliers Group, and the Missile Technology &nbsp;Control Regime, or from adopting, maintaining or implementing independent sanctions regimes. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.15: Customs valuation </span></p><p class="c474"><span class="c0">Each Party shall determine the customs value of goods of the other Party imported into its territory in &nbsp;accordance with Article VII of GATT 1994 and the Customs Valuation Agreement. To this end, Article &nbsp;VII of GATT 1994 including its Notes and Supplementary Provisions, and Articles 1 to 17 of the Customs &nbsp;Valuation Agreement including its Interpretative Notes, are incorporated into and made part of this &nbsp;Agreement, </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.16: Preference utilisation </span></p><p class="c860"><span class="c0">1. For the purpose of monitoring the functioning of this Agreement and calculating preference &nbsp;utilisation rates, the Parties shall annually exchange import statistics for a 10 year-long period starting &nbsp;one year after the entry into force of this Agreement. Unless the Trade Partnership Committee decides &nbsp;otherwise, this period shall be automatically extended for five years, and thereafter the Trade &nbsp;Partnership Committee may decide to extend it further. </span></p><p class="c765"><span class="c0">2. The exchange of import statistics shall cover data pertaining to the most recent year available, &nbsp;including value and, where applicable, volume, at the tariff line level for imports of goods of the other &nbsp;Party benefitting from preferential duty treatment under this Agreement and for those that receive &nbsp;non-preferential treatment. </span></p><p class="c203"><span class="c0">23 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.17: Trade Remedies </span></p><p class="c212"><span class="c0">1. The Parties affirm their rights and obligations under Article VI of GATT 1994, the Anti-Dumping &nbsp;Agreement, the SCM Agreement, Article XIX of GATT 1994, the Safeguards Agreement, and Article 5 &nbsp;of the Agreement on Agriculture. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c593"><span class="c0">2. Chapter 2 [Rules of origin] of this Title does not apply to anti-dumping, countervailing and &nbsp;safeguard investigations and measures. </span></p><p class="c138"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall apply anti-dumping and countervailing measures in accordance with the &nbsp;requirements of the Anti-Dumping Agreement and the SCM Agreement, and pursuant to a fair and &nbsp;transparent process. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c242"><span class="c0">4. Provided it does not unnecessarily delay the conduct of the investigation, each interested &nbsp;party in an anti-dumping or countervailing investigation</span><span class="c134">1</span><span class="c0">shall be granted a full opportunity to defend &nbsp;its interests. </span></p><p class="c138"><span class="c0">5. Each Party&#39;s investigating authority may, in accordance with the Party&#39;s law, consider whether &nbsp;the amount of the anti-dumping duty to be imposed shall be the full margin of dumping or a lesser &nbsp;amount. </span></p><p class="c269"><span class="c0">6. Each Party&#39;s investigating authority shall, in accordance with the Party&rsquo;s law, consider &nbsp;information provided as to whether imposing an anti-dumping or a countervailing duty would not be &nbsp;in the public interest. </span></p><p class="c801"><span class="c0">7. A Party shall not apply or maintain, with respect to the same good, at the same time: (a) a measure pursuant to Article 5 of the Agreement on Agriculture; and &nbsp;(b) a measure pursuant to Article XIX of GATT 1994 and the Safeguards Agreement. 8. Title I [Dispute settlement] of Part Six does not apply to paragraphs 1 to 6 of this Article. Article GOODS.18: Use of existing WTO tariff rate quotas </span></p><p class="c804"><span class="c0">1. Products originating in one Party shall not be eligible to be imported into the other Party under &nbsp;existing WTO Tariff Rate Quotas (&lsquo;TRQs&rsquo;) as defined in paragraph 2. This shall include those TRQs as &nbsp;being apportioned between the Parties pursuant to Article XXVIII GATT negotiations initiated by the &nbsp;European Union in WTO document G/SECRET/42/Add.2 and by the UK in WTO document &nbsp;G/SECRET/44 and as set out in each Party&rsquo;s respective internal legislation. For the purposes of this &nbsp;Article, the originating status of the products shall be determined on the basis of non-preferential &nbsp;rules of origin applicable in the importing Party. </span></p><p class="c862"><span class="c0">2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, &lsquo;existing WTO TRQs&rsquo; means those tariff rate quotas which &nbsp;are WTO concessions of the European Union included in the draft EU28 schedule of concessions and &nbsp;commitments under GATT 1994 submitted to the WTO in document G/MA/TAR/RS/506 as amended &nbsp;by documents G/MA/TAR/RS/506/Add.1 and G/MA/TAR/RS/506/Add.2. </span></p><p class="c5"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c239"><span class="c81">1</span><span class="c77">For the purpose of this Article, interested parties shall be defined as per Article 6(11) of the Anti-dumping &nbsp;Agreement and Article 12.9 of the SCM Agreement.</span></p><p class="c562"><span class="c0">24 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.19: Measures in case of breaches or circumventions of customs legislation </span></p><p class="c476"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall co-operate in preventing, detecting and combating breaches or &nbsp;circumventions of customs legislation, in accordance with their obligations under Chapter 2 [Rules of &nbsp;origin] of this Title and the Protocol on mutual administrative assistance in customs matters. Each &nbsp;Party shall take appropriate and comparable measures to protect its own and the other Party&rsquo;s &nbsp;financial interests regarding the levying of duties on goods entering the customs territories of the &nbsp;United Kingdom or the Union. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c194"><span class="c0">2. Subject to the possibility of exemption for compliant traders under paragraph 7, a Party may &nbsp;temporarily suspend the relevant preferential treatment of the product or products concerned in &nbsp;accordance with the procedure laid down in paragraphs 3 and 4 if: </span></p><p class="c666"><span class="c0">(a) that Party has made a finding, based on objective, compelling and verifiable information, that &nbsp;systematic and large-scale breaches or circumventions of customs legislation have been &nbsp;committed, and; </span></p><p class="c232"><span class="c0">(b) the other Party repeatedly and unjustifiably refuses or otherwise fails to comply with the &nbsp;obligations referred to in paragraph 1. </span></p><p class="c391"><span class="c0">3. The Party which has made a finding as referred to in paragraph 2 shall notify the Trade &nbsp;Partnership Committee and shall enter into consultations with the other Party within the Trade &nbsp;Partnership Committee with a view to reaching a mutually acceptable solution. </span></p><p class="c845"><span class="c0">4. If the Parties fail to agree on a mutually acceptable solution within three months after the &nbsp;date of notification, the Party which has made the finding may decide to suspend temporarily the &nbsp;relevant preferential treatment of the product or products concerned. In this case, the Party which &nbsp;made the finding shall notify the temporary suspension, including the period during which it intends &nbsp;the temporary suspension to apply, to the Trade Partnership Committee without delay. </span></p><p class="c611"><span class="c0">5. The temporary suspension shall apply only for the period necessary to counteract the &nbsp;breaches or circumventions and to protect the financial interests of the Party concerned, and in any &nbsp;case not for longer than six months. The Party concerned shall keep the situation under review and, &nbsp;where it decides that the temporary suspension is no longer necessary, it shall bring it to an end before &nbsp;the end of the period notified to the Trade Partnership Committee. Where the conditions that gave &nbsp;rise to the suspension persist at the expiry of the period notified to the Trade Partnership Committee, &nbsp;the Party concerned may decide to renew the suspension. Any suspension shall be subject to periodic &nbsp;consultations within the Trade Partnership Committee. </span></p><p class="c481"><span class="c0">6. Each Party shall publish, in accordance with its internal procedures, notices to importers about &nbsp;any decision concerning temporary suspensions referred to in paragraphs 4 and 5. </span></p><p class="c566"><span class="c0">7. Notwithstanding paragraph 4, if an importer is able to satisfy the importing customs authority &nbsp;that such products are fully compliant with the importing Party&rsquo;s customs legislation, the &nbsp;requirements of this Agreement, and any other appropriate conditions related to the temporary &nbsp;suspension established by the importing Party in accordance with its laws and regulations, the &nbsp;importing Party shall allow the importer to apply for preferential treatment and recover any duties &nbsp;paid in excess of the applicable preferential tariff rates when the products were imported.</span></p><p class="c650"><span class="c0">25 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.20: Management of administrative errors </span></p><p class="c486"><span class="c0">In case of systematic errors by the competent authorities or issues concerning the proper &nbsp;management of the preferential system at export, concerning notably the application of the provisions &nbsp;of Chapter 2 of this Title or the application of the Protocol on Mutual Administrative Assistance in &nbsp;Customs Matters, and if these errors or issues lead to consequences in terms of import duties, the &nbsp;Party facing such consequences may request the Trade Partnership Committee to examine the &nbsp;possibility of adopting decisions, as appropriate, to resolve the situation. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article GOODS.21: Cultural property </span></p><p class="c608"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall cooperate in facilitating the return of cultural property illicitly removed from &nbsp;the territory of a Party, having regard to the principles enshrined in the UNESCO Convention on the &nbsp;Means of Prohibiting and Preventing the Illicit Import, Export and Transfer of Ownership of Cultural &nbsp;Property signed in Paris on 17 November 1970. </span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. For the purposes of this Article: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c651"><span class="c0">(a) &lsquo;cultural property&rsquo; means property classified or defined as being among the national treasures &nbsp;possessing artistic, historic or archaeological value under the respective rules and procedures &nbsp;of each Party; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c411"><span class="c0">(b) &lsquo;illicitly removed from the territory of a Party&rsquo; means: </span></p><p class="c401"><span class="c0">(i) removed from the territory of a Party on or after 1 January 1993 in breach of that Party&rsquo;s &nbsp;rules on the protection of national treasures or in breach of its rules on the export of &nbsp;cultural property; or </span></p><p class="c17"><span class="c0">(ii) not returned at the end of a period of lawful temporary removal or any breach of another &nbsp;condition governing such temporary removal, on or after 1 January 1993. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c353"><span class="c0">3. The competent authorities of the Parties shall cooperate with each other in particular by: </span></p><p class="c612"><span class="c0">(a) notifying the other Party where cultural property is found in their territory and there are &nbsp;reasonable grounds for believing that the cultural property has been illicitly removed &nbsp;from the territory of the other Party; </span></p><p class="c835"><span class="c0">(b) addressing requests of the other Party for the return of cultural property which has been &nbsp;illicitly removed from the territory of that Party; </span></p><p class="c800"><span class="c0">(c) preventing any actions to evade the return of such cultural property, by means of any &nbsp;necessary interim measures; and </span></p><p class="c417"><span class="c0">(d) taking any necessary measures for the physical preservation of cultural property which has &nbsp;been illicitly removed from the territory of the other Party. </span></p><p class="c44"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall identify a contact point responsible for communicating with the contact point &nbsp;of the other Party with respect to any matters arising under this Article, including with respect to the &nbsp;notifications and requests referred to in points (a) and (b) of paragraph 3.</span></p><p class="c471"><span class="c0">26 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c195"><span class="c0">5. The envisaged cooperation between the Parties shall involve the customs authorities of the &nbsp;Parties responsible for managing export procedures for cultural property as appropriate and &nbsp;necessary. </span></p><p class="c353"><span class="c0">6.
