Title I [Dispute Settlement] of Part Six does not apply to this Article. </span></p><p class="c94"><span class="c0">Chapter 2: Rules of origin &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c27">Section 1: Rules of origin </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.1: Objective </span></p><p class="c632"><span class="c0">The objective of this Chapter is to lay down the provisions determining the origin of goods for the &nbsp;purpose of application of preferential tariff treatment under this Agreement, and setting out related &nbsp;origin procedures. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.2: Definitions </span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0 c108">For the purposes of this Chapter, the following definitions apply:</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c298"><span class="c0">(a) &quot;classification&quot; means the classification of a product or material under a particular chapter, &nbsp;heading, or sub-heading of the Harmonised System; </span></p><p class="c354"><span class="c0">(b) &quot;consignment&quot; means products which are either sent simultaneously from one exporter to one &nbsp;consignee or covered by a single transport document covering their shipment from the exporter &nbsp;to the consignee or, in the absence of such a document, by a single invoice; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c266"><span class="c0">(c) &quot;exporter&quot; means a person, located in a Party, who, in accordance with the requirements laid &nbsp;down in the laws and regulations of that Party, exports or produces the originating product and &nbsp;makes out a statement on origin; </span></p><p class="c319"><span class="c0">(d) &quot;importer&quot; means a person who imports the originating product and claims preferential tariff &nbsp;treatment for it; </span></p><p class="c93"><span class="c0">(e) &quot;material&quot; means any substance used in the production of a product, including any components, &nbsp;ingredients, raw materials, or parts; </span></p><p class="c480"><span class="c0">(f) &quot;non-originating material&quot; means a material which does not qualify as originating under this &nbsp;Chapter, including a material whose originating status cannot be determined; </span></p><p class="c856"><span class="c0">(g) &quot;product&quot; means the product resulting from the production, even if it is intended for use as a &nbsp;material in the production of another product; </span></p><p class="c607"><span class="c0">(h) &quot;production&quot; means any kind of working or processing including assembly. Article ORIG.3: General requirements </span></p><p class="c750"><span class="c0 c108">1. For the </span><span class="c0">purposes</span><span class="c0 c108">&nbsp;of applying the preferential tariff treatment by a Party to the originating </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">good of the other Party in accordance with this Agreement, </span><span class="c0">provided that the products satisfy all other &nbsp;applicable requirements of this Chapter, </span><span class="c0 c108">the following products shall be considered as originating in </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">the other Party:</span></p><p class="c217"><span class="c0">27 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c822"><span class="c0">(a) products wholly obtained in that Party within the meaning of Article ORIG.5 [Wholly obtained products]; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) products produced in that Party exclusively from originating materials in that Party; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c717"><span class="c0">(c) products produced in that Party incorporating non-originating materials provided they satisfy &nbsp;the requirements set out in ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules of origin]. </span></p><p class="c710"><span class="c0">2. If a product has acquired originating status, the non-originating materials used in the &nbsp;production of that product shall not be considered as non-originating when that product is &nbsp;incorporated as a material in another product. </span></p><p class="c322"><span class="c0">3. The acquisition of originating status shall be fulfilled without interruption in the United &nbsp;Kingdom or the Union. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.4: Cumulation of origin </span></p><p class="c393"><span class="c0">1. A product originating in a Party shall be considered as originating in the other Party if that &nbsp;product is used as a material in the production of another product in that other Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c115"><span class="c0">2. Production carried out in a Party on a non-originating material may be taken into account for &nbsp;the purpose of determining whether a product is originating in the other Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c173"><span class="c0">3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply if the production carried out in the other Party does not go &nbsp;beyond the operations referred to in Article ORIG.7 [Insufficient production]. </span></p><p class="c19"><span class="c0">4. In order for an exporter to complete the statement on origin referred to in point (a) of Article &nbsp;ORIG.18(2) [Claim for preferential tariff treatment] for a product referred to in paragraph 2 of this &nbsp;Article, the exporter shall obtain from its supplier a supplier&rsquo;s declaration as provided for in Annex &nbsp;ORIG-3 [Supplier&rsquo;s declaration] or an equivalent document that contains the same information &nbsp;describing the non-originating materials concerned in sufficient detail to enable them to be identified. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.5: Wholly obtained products </span></p><p class="c490"><span class="c0">1. The following products shall be considered as wholly obtained in a Party: (a) mineral products extracted or taken from its soil or from its seabed; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c230"><span class="c0">(b) plants and vegetable products grown or harvested there; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) live animals born and raised there; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(d) products obtained from live animals raised there; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(e) products obtained from slaughtered animals born and raised there; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(f) products obtained by hunting or fishing conducted there; </span></p><p class="c352"><span class="c0">(g) products obtained from aquaculture there if aquatic organisms, including fish, molluscs, &nbsp;crustaceans, other aquatic invertebrates and aquatic plants are born or raised from seed stock &nbsp;such as eggs, roes, fry, fingerlings, larvae, parr, smolts or other immature fish at a post-larval &nbsp;stage by intervention in the rearing or growth processes to enhance production such as regular &nbsp;stocking, feeding or protection from predators;</span></p><p class="c217"><span class="c0">28 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c110"><span class="c0">(h) products of sea fishing and other products taken from the sea outside any territorial sea by a &nbsp;vessel of a Party; </span></p><p class="c564"><span class="c0">(i) products made aboard of a factory ship of a Party exclusively from products referred to in point &nbsp;(h); </span></p><p class="c140"><span class="c0">(j) products extracted from the seabed or subsoil outside any territorial sea provided that they &nbsp;have rights to exploit or work such seabed or subsoil; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(k) waste and scrap resulting from production operations conducted there; </span></p><p class="c68"><span class="c0">(l) waste and scrap derived from used products collected there, provided that those products are &nbsp;fit only for the recovery of raw materials; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(m) products produced there exclusively from the products specified in points (a) to (l). </span></p><p class="c367"><span class="c0">2. The terms &ldquo;vessel of a Party&rdquo; and &ldquo;factory ship of a Party&rdquo; in points (h) and (i) of paragraph 1 &nbsp;mean a vessel and factory ship which: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) is registered in a Member State or in the United Kingdom; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) sails under the flag of a Member State or of the United Kingdom; and </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) meets one of the following conditions: </span></p><p class="c176"><span class="c0">(i) it is at least 50% owned by nationals of a Member State or of the United Kingdom; or (ii) it is owned by legal persons which each: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c272"><span class="c0">(A) have their head office and main place of business in the Union or the United &nbsp;Kingdom; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c256"><span class="c0">(B) are at least 50% owned by public entities, nationals or legal persons of a Member &nbsp;State or the United Kingdom. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.6: Tolerances </span></p><p class="c28"><span class="c0">1. If a product does not satisfy the requirements set out in ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules &nbsp;of origin] due to the use of a non-originating material in its production, that product shall nevertheless &nbsp;be considered as originating in a Party, provided that: </span></p><p class="c704"><span class="c0">(a) the total weight of non-originating materials used in the production of products classified under &nbsp;Chapters 2 and 4 to 24 of the Harmonised System, other than processed fishery products of &nbsp;Chapter 16, does not exceed 15% of the weight of the product; </span></p><p class="c235"><span class="c0">(b) the total value of non-originating materials for all other products, except for products classified &nbsp;under Chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonised System does not exceed 10% of the ex-works price &nbsp;of the product; or </span></p><p class="c770"><span class="c0">(c) for a product classified under Chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonised System, the tolerances set &nbsp;out in Note 7 and 8 of ANNEX ORIG-1 [Introductory Notes to the Product-Specific Rules of &nbsp;Origin] apply.</span></p><p class="c356"><span class="c0">29 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c192"><span class="c0">2. Paragraph 1 does not apply if the value or weight of non-originating materials used in the &nbsp;production of a product exceeds any of the percentages for the maximum value or weight of non originating materials as specified in the requirements set out in ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules &nbsp;of origin]. </span></p><p class="c335"><span class="c0">3. Paragraph 1 of this Article does not apply to products wholly obtained in a Party within the &nbsp;meaning of Article ORIG.5 [Wholly obtained products]. If ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules of &nbsp;origin] requires that the materials used in the production of a product are wholly obtained, paragraphs &nbsp;1 and 2 of this Article apply. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.7: Insufficient Production </span></p><p class="c222"><span class="c0">1. Notwithstanding point (c) of Article ORIG.3(1) [General requirements], a product shall not be &nbsp;considered as originating in a Party if the production of the product in a Party consists only of one or &nbsp;more of the following operations conducted on non-originating materials: </span></p><p class="c512"><span class="c0">(a) preserving operations such as drying, freezing, keeping in brine and other similar operations &nbsp;where their sole purpose is to ensure that the products remain in good condition during &nbsp;transport and storage;</span><span class="c134">2</span><span class="c532">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(b) breaking-up or assembly of packages; </span></p><p class="c643"><span class="c0">(c) washing, cleaning; removal of dust, oxide, oil, paint or other coverings; (d) ironing or pressing of textiles and textile articles; </span></p><p class="c858"><span class="c0">(e) simple painting and polishing operations; </span></p><p class="c298"><span class="c0">(f) husking and partial or total milling of rice; polishing and glazing of cereals and rice; bleaching of &nbsp;rice; </span></p><p class="c172"><span class="c0">(g) operations to colour or flavour sugar or form sugar lumps; partial or total milling of sugar in &nbsp;solid form; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(h) peeling, stoning and shelling, of fruits, nuts and vegetables; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(i) sharpening, simple grinding or simple cutting; </span></p><p class="c254"><span class="c0">(j) sifting, screening, sorting, classifying, grading, matching including the making-up of sets of &nbsp;articles; </span></p><p class="c513"><span class="c0">(k) simple placing in bottles, cans, flasks, bags, cases, boxes, fixing on cards or boards and all other &nbsp;simple packaging operations; </span></p><p class="c668"><span class="c0">(l) affixing or printing marks, labels, logos and other like distinguishing signs on products or their &nbsp;packaging; </span></p><p class="c425"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c270"><span class="c81">2 </span><span class="c77">Preserving operations such as chilling, freezing or ventilating are considered insufficient within the meaning of &nbsp;point (a), whereas operations such as pickling, drying or smoking that are intended to give a product special or &nbsp;different characteristics are not considered insufficient.</span></p><p class="c103"><span class="c0">30 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">(m) simple mixing of products, whether or not of different kinds; mixing of sugar with any material; </span></p><p class="c568"><span class="c0">(n) simple addition of water or dilution with water or another substance that does not materially &nbsp;alter the characteristics of the product, or dehydration or denaturation of products; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c392"><span class="c0">(o) simple assembly of parts of articles to constitute a complete article or disassembly of products &nbsp;into parts; </span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(p) slaughter of animals. </span></p><p class="c420"><span class="c0">2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, operations shall be considered simple if neither special skills &nbsp;nor machines, apparatus or equipment especially produced or installed are needed for carrying out &nbsp;those operations. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.8: Unit of qualification </span></p><p class="c792"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of this Chapter, the unit of qualification shall be the particular product which &nbsp;is considered as the basic unit when classifying the product under the Harmonised System. </span></p><p class="c190"><span class="c0">2. For a consignment consisting of a number of identical products classified under the same heading &nbsp;of the Harmonised System, each individual product shall be taken into account when applying the &nbsp;provisions of this Chapter. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.9: Packing materials and containers for shipment </span></p><p class="c394"><span class="c0">Packing materials and containers for shipment that are used to protect a product during &nbsp;transportation shall be disregarded in determining whether a product is originating. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.10: Packaging materials and containers for retail sale &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c124"><span class="c0">Packaging materials and containers in which the product is packaged for retail sale, if classified with &nbsp;the product, shall be disregarded in determining the origin of the product, except for the purposes of &nbsp;calculating the value of non-originating materials if the product is subject to a maximum value of non originating materials in accordance with ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules of origin]. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.11: Accessories, spare parts and tools </span></p><p class="c310"><span class="c0">1. Accessories, spare parts, tools and instructional or other information materials shall be &nbsp;regarded as one product with the piece of equipment, machine, apparatus or vehicle in question if &nbsp;they: </span></p><p class="c667"><span class="c0">(a) are classified and delivered with, but not invoiced separately from, the product; and (b) are of the types, quantities and value which are customary for that product. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c399"><span class="c0">2. Accessories, spare parts, tools and instructional or other information materials referred to in &nbsp;paragraph 1 shall be disregarded in determining the origin of the product except for the purposes of &nbsp;calculating the value of non-originating materials if a product is subject to a maximum value of non originating materials as set out in ANNEX ORIG-2 [Product-specific rules of origin]. </span></p><p class="c129"><span class="c0">31 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.12: Sets </span></p><p class="c213"><span class="c0">Sets, as defined in General Rule 3 for the Interpretation of the Harmonised System, shall be considered &nbsp;as originating in a Party if all of their components are originating. If a set is composed of originating &nbsp;and non-originating components, the set as a whole shall be considered as originating in a Party, if the &nbsp;value of the non-originating components does not exceed 15 % of the ex-works price of the set. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.13: Neutral elements </span></p><p class="c22"><span class="c0">In order to determine whether a product is originating in a Party, it shall not be necessary to determine &nbsp;the origin of the following elements, which might be used in its production: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) fuel, energy, catalysts and solvents; </span></p><p class="c795"><span class="c0">(b) plant, equipment, spare parts and materials used in the maintenance of equipment and &nbsp;buildings; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(c) machines, tools, dies and moulds; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c711"><span class="c0">(d) lubricants, greases, compounding materials and other materials used in production or used to &nbsp;operate equipment and buildings; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(e) gloves, glasses, footwear, clothing, safety equipment and supplies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(f) equipment, devices and supplies used for testing or inspecting the product; and </span></p><p class="c855"><span class="c0">(g) other materials used in the production which are not incorporated into the product nor &nbsp;intended to be incorporated into the final composition of the product. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.14: Accounting segregation </span></p><p class="c143"><span class="c0">1. Originating and non-originating fungible materials or &quot;fungible products&quot; shall be physically &nbsp;segregated during storage in order to maintain their originating and non-originating status. </span></p><p class="c295"><span class="c0">2. For the purpose of paragraph 1, &lsquo;fungible materials&rsquo; or &quot;fungible products&quot; means materials &nbsp;or products that are of the same kind and commercial quality, with the same technical and physical &nbsp;characteristics, and that cannot be distinguished from one another for origin purposes. </span></p><p class="c225"><span class="c0">3. Notwithstanding paragraph 1, originating and non-originating fungible materials may be used &nbsp;in the production of a product without being physically segregated during storage if an accounting &nbsp;segregation method is used. </span></p><p class="c112"><span class="c0">4. Notwithstanding paragraph 1, originating and non-originating fungible products classified in &nbsp;Chapter 10, 15, 27, 28, 29, heading 32.01 to 32.07, or heading 39.01 to 39.14 of the Harmonised &nbsp;System may be stored in a Party before exportation to the other Party without being physically &nbsp;segregated provided that an accounting segregation method is used. </span></p><p class="c95"><span class="c0">5. The accounting segregation method referred to in paragraphs 3 and 4 shall be applied in &nbsp;conformity with a stock management method under accounting principles which are generally &nbsp;accepted in the Party. </span></p><p class="c691"><span class="c0">32 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c168"><span class="c0">6. The accounting segregation method shall be any method that ensures that at any time no &nbsp;more materials or products receive originating status than would be the case if the materials or &nbsp;products had been physically segregated. </span></p><p class="c721"><span class="c0">7. A Party may require, under conditions set out in its laws or regulations, that the use of an &nbsp;accounting segregation method is subject to prior authorisation by the customs authorities of that &nbsp;Party. The customs authorities of the Party shall monitor the use of such authorisations and may &nbsp;withdraw an authorisation if the holder makes improper use of the accounting segregation method or &nbsp;fails to fulfil any of the other conditions laid down in this Chapter. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.15: Returned products </span></p><p class="c300"><span class="c0">If a product originating in a Party exported from that Party to a third country returns to that Party, it &nbsp;shall be considered as a non-originating product unless it can be demonstrated to the satisfaction of &nbsp;the customs authority of that Party that the returning product: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) is the same as that exported; and </span></p><p class="c291"><span class="c0">(b) has not undergone any operation other than what was necessary to preserve it in good &nbsp;condition while in that third country or while being exported. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.16: Non-alteration </span></p><p class="c479"><span class="c0">1. An originating product declared for home use in the importing Party shall not, after &nbsp;exportation and prior to being declared for home use, have been altered, transformed in any way or &nbsp;subjected to operations other than to preserve it in good condition or than adding or affixing marks, &nbsp;labels, seals or any other documentation to ensure compliance with specific domestic requirements &nbsp;of the importing Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c655"><span class="c0">2. The storage or exhibition of a product may take place in a third country, provided that the &nbsp;product remains under customs supervision in that third country. </span></p><p class="c653"><span class="c0">3. The splitting of consignments may take place in a third country if it is carried out by the &nbsp;exporter or under the responsibility of the exporter, provided that the consignments remain under &nbsp;customs supervision in that third country. </span></p><p class="c637"><span class="c0">4. In the case of doubt as to whether the requirements provided for in paragraphs 1 to 3 are &nbsp;complied with, the customs authority of the importing Party may request the importer to provide &nbsp;evidence of compliance with those requirements, which may be given by any means, including &nbsp;contractual transport documents such as bills of lading or factual or concrete evidence based on the &nbsp;marking or numbering of packages or any evidence related to the product itself. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.17: Review of drawback of, or exemption from, customs duties &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c382"><span class="c0">Not earlier than 2 years from the entry into force of this Agreement, at the request of either Party, &nbsp;the Trade Specialised Committee on Customs Cooperation and Rules of Origin shall review the Parties&rsquo; &nbsp;respective duty drawback and inward-processing schemes. For this purpose, at the request of a Party, &nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">no later than 60 days from that request, the other Party shall provide the requesting Party with </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">available information and detailed statistics covering the period from the entry into force of this </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">Agreement, or the previous 5 years if that is shorter, on the operation of its duty-drawback and </span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0 c108">inward-processing scheme. I</span><span class="c0">n the light of this review, the Trade Specialised Committee on Customs &nbsp;Cooperation and Rules of Origin may make recommendations to the Partnership Council for the </span></p><p class="c257"><span class="c0">33 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c313"><span class="c0">amendment of the provisions of this Chapter and its Annexes, with a view to introducing limitations &nbsp;or restrictions with respect to drawback of or exemption from customs duties. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c27">Section 2: Origin procedures </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.18: Claim for preferential tariff treatment </span></p><p class="c726"><span class="c0">1. The importing Party, on importation, shall grant preferential tariff treatment to a product &nbsp;originating in the other Party within the meaning of this Chapter on the basis of a claim by the importer &nbsp;for preferential tariff treatment. The importer shall be responsible for the correctness of the claim for &nbsp;preferential tariff treatment and for compliance with the requirements provided for in this Chapter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. A claim for preferential tariff treatment shall be based on: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c701"><span class="c0">(a) a statement on origin that the product is originating made out by the exporter; or &nbsp;(b) the importer&rsquo;s knowledge that the product is originating. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c433"><span class="c0">3. The importer making the claim for preferential tariff treatment based on a statement on origin &nbsp;as referred to in point (a) of paragraph 2 shall keep the statement on origin and, when required by the &nbsp;customs authority of the importing Party, shall provide a copy thereof to that customs authority. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.18a: Time of the claim for preferential tariff treatment </span></p><p class="c301"><span class="c0">1. A claim for preferential tariff treatment and the basis for that claim as referred to in Article &nbsp;ORIG.18(2) [Claim for preferential tariff treatment] shall be included in the customs import declaration &nbsp;in accordance with the laws and regulations of the importing Party. </span></p><p class="c615"><span class="c0">2. By way of derogation from paragraph 1 of this Article, if the importer did not make a claim for &nbsp;preferential tariff treatment at the time of importation, the importing Party shall grant preferential &nbsp;tariff treatment and repay or remit any excess customs duty paid provided that: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c567"><span class="c0">(a) the claim for preferential tariff treatment is made no later than three years after the date of &nbsp;importation, or such longer time period as specified in the laws and regulations of the importing &nbsp;Party; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c170"><span class="c0">(b) the importer provides the basis for the claim as referred to in Article ORIG.18(2) [Claim for &nbsp;preferential tariff treatment]; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c896"><span class="c0">(c) the product would have been considered originating and would have satisfied all other &nbsp;applicable requirements within the meaning of Section 1 [Rules of origin] of this Chapter if it &nbsp;had been claimed by the importer at the time of importation. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c57"><span class="c0">The other obligations applicable to the importer under Article ORIG.18 [Claim for preferential tariff &nbsp;treatment] remain unchanged. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.19: Statement on origin </span></p><p class="c457"><span class="c0">1. A statement on origin shall be made out by an exporter of a product on the basis of &nbsp;information demonstrating that the product is originating, including information on the originating &nbsp;status of materials used in the production of the product. The exporter shall be responsible for the &nbsp;correctness of the statement on origin and the information provided. </span></p><p class="c82"><span class="c0">34 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c895"><span class="c0">2. A statement on origin shall be made out using one of the language versions set out in ANNEX &nbsp;ORIG-4 [Text of the statement on origin] in an invoice or on any other document that describes the &nbsp;originating product in sufficient detail to enable the identification of that product. The exporter shall &nbsp;be responsible for providing sufficient detail to allow the identification of the originating product. The &nbsp;importing Party shall not require the importer to submit a translation of the statement on origin. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c837"><span class="c0">3. A statement on origin shall be valid for 12 months from the date it was made out or for such &nbsp;longer period as provided by the Party of import up to a maximum of 24 months. </span></p><p class="c325"><span class="c0">4. A statement on origin may apply to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(a) a single shipment of one or more products imported into a Party; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c674"><span class="c0">(b) multiple shipments of identical products imported into a Party within the period specified in the &nbsp;statement on origin, which shall not exceed 12 months. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c46"><span class="c0">5. If, at the request of the importer, unassembled or disassembled products within the meaning &nbsp;of General Rule 2(a) for the Interpretation of the Harmonised System that fall within Sections XV to &nbsp;XXI of the Harmonised System are imported by instalments, a single statement on origin for such &nbsp;products may be used in accordance with the requirements laid down by the customs authority of the &nbsp;importing Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.20: Discrepancies </span></p><p class="c283"><span class="c0">The customs authority of the importing Party shall not reject a claim for preferential tariff treatment &nbsp;due to minor errors or discrepancies in the statement on origin, or for the sole reason that an invoice &nbsp;was issued in a third country. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.21: Importer&rsquo;s knowledge </span></p><p class="c432"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of a claim for preferential tariff treatment that is made under point (b) of &nbsp;Article ORIG.18(2) [Claim for preferential tariff treatment], the importer&rsquo;s knowledge that a product &nbsp;is originating in the exporting Party shall be based on information demonstrating that the product is &nbsp;originating and satisfies the requirements provided for in this Chapter. </span></p><p class="c261"><span class="c0">2. Before claiming the preferential treatment, in the event that an importer is unable to obtain &nbsp;the information referred to in paragraph 1 of this Article as a result of the exporter deeming it to be &nbsp;confidential information or for any other reason, the exporter may provide a statement on origin so &nbsp;that the importer may claim the preferential tariff treatment on the basis of point (a) of Article &nbsp;ORIG.18(2) [Claim for Preferential Tariff Treatment]. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.22: Record-keeping requirements </span></p><p class="c806"><span class="c0">1. For a minimum of three years after the date of importation of the product, an importer making &nbsp;a claim for preferential tariff treatment for a product imported into the importing Party shall keep: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c158"><span class="c0">(a) if the claim was based on a statement on origin, the statement on origin made out by the &nbsp;exporter; or </span></p><p class="c840"><span class="c0">(b) if the claim was based on the importer&#39;s knowledge, all records demonstrating that the product &nbsp;satisfies the requirements for obtaining originating status. </span></p><p class="c435"><span class="c0">35 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c737"><span class="c0">2. An exporter who has made out a statement on origin shall, for a minimum of four years after &nbsp;that statement on origin was made out, keep a copy of the statement on origin and all other records &nbsp;demonstrating that the product satisfies the requirements to obtain originating status. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c464"><span class="c0">3. The records to be kept in accordance with this Article may be held in electronic format. &nbsp;Article ORIG.23: Small consignments </span></p><p class="c343"><span class="c0">1. By way of derogation from Articles ORIG.18 [Claim for Preferential Tariff Treatment] to &nbsp;ORIG.21 [Importer&rsquo;s Knowledge], provided that the product has been declared as meeting the &nbsp;requirements of this Chapter and the customs authority of the importing Party has no doubts as to &nbsp;the veracity of that declaration, the importing Party shall grant preferential tariff treatment to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c630"><span class="c0">(a) a product sent in a small package from private persons to private persons; &nbsp;(b) a product forming part of a traveller&rsquo;s personal luggage; and </span></p><p class="c207"><span class="c0">(c) for the United Kingdom, in addition to points (a) and (b), other low value consignments. 2. The following products are excluded from the application of paragraph 1 of this Article: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c876"><span class="c0">(a) products, the importation of which forms part of a series of importations that may reasonably &nbsp;be considered to have been made separately for the purpose of avoiding the requirements of &nbsp;Article ORIG.18 [Claim for Preferential Tariff Treatment]; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c411"><span class="c0">(b) for the Union: </span></p><p class="c724"><span class="c0">(i) a product imported by way of trade; the imports which are occasional and consist solely &nbsp;of products for the personal use of the recipients or travellers or their families are not &nbsp;be considered as imports by way of trade if it is evident from the nature and quantity &nbsp;of the products that no commercial purpose is intended; and </span></p><p class="c785"><span class="c0">(ii) products, the total value of which exceeds EUR 500 in the case of products sent in small &nbsp;packages, or EUR 1 200 in the case of products forming part of a traveller&rsquo;s personal &nbsp;luggage. The amounts to be used in a given national currency shall be the equivalent in &nbsp;that currency of the amounts expressed in euro as at the first working day of October. The exchange rate amounts shall be those published for that day by the European &nbsp;Central Bank, unless a different amount is communicated to the European Commission &nbsp;by 15 October, and shall apply from 1 January the following year. The European &nbsp;Commission shall notify the United Kingdom of the relevant amounts. The Union may &nbsp;establish other limits which it will communicate to the United Kingdom; and </span></p><p class="c751"><span class="c0">(c) for the United Kingdom, products whose total value exceeds the limits set under the domestic &nbsp;law of the United Kingdom. The United Kingdom will communicate these limits to the Union. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c781"><span class="c0">3. The importer shall be responsible for the correctness of the declaration and for the &nbsp;compliance with the requirements provided for in this Chapter. The record-keeping requirements set &nbsp;out in Article ORIG.22 [Record-keeping requirements] shall not apply to the importer under this &nbsp;Article. </span></p><p class="c205"><span class="c0">36 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.24: Verification </span></p><p class="c344"><span class="c0">1. The customs authority of the importing Party may conduct a verification as to whether a &nbsp;product is originating or whether the other requirements of this Chapter are satisfied, on the basis of &nbsp;risk assessment methods, which may include random selection. Such verifications may be conducted &nbsp;by means of a request for information from the importer who made the claim referred to in Article &nbsp;ORIG.18 [Claim for Preferential Tariff Treatment], at the time the import declaration is submitted, &nbsp;before the release of the products, or after the release of the products. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c86"><span class="c0">2. The information requested pursuant to paragraph 1 shall cover no more than the following &nbsp;elements: </span></p><p class="c292"><span class="c0">(a) if the claim was based on a statement on origin, that statement on origin; and (b) information pertaining to the fulfilment of origin criteria, which is: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c255"><span class="c0">(i) where the origin criterion is &ldquo;wholly obtained&rdquo;, the applicable category (such as &nbsp;harvesting, mining, fishing) and the place of production; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c385"><span class="c0">(ii) where the origin criterion is based on change in tariff classification, a list of all the non originating materials, including their tariff classification (in 2, 4 or 6-digit format, &nbsp;depending on the origin criterion); &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c735"><span class="c0">(iii) where the origin criterion is based on a value method, the value of the final product as &nbsp;well as the value of all the non-originating materials used in the production of that &nbsp;product; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c446"><span class="c0">(iv) where the origin criterion is based on weight, the weight of the final product as well as &nbsp;the weight of the relevant non-originating materials used in the final product; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c448"><span class="c0">(v) where the origin criterion is based on a specific production process, a description of that &nbsp;specific process. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c60"><span class="c0">3. When providing the requested information, the importer may add any other information that &nbsp;it considers relevant for the purpose of verification. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c660"><span class="c0">4. If the claim for preferential tariff treatment is based on a statement on origin, the importer &nbsp;shall provide that statement on origin but may reply to the customs authority of the importing Party &nbsp;that the importer is not in a position to provide the information referred to in point (b) of paragraph &nbsp;2. </span></p><p class="c739"><span class="c0">5. If the claim for preferential tariff treatment is based on the importer&rsquo;s knowledge, after having &nbsp;first requested information in accordance with paragraph 1, the customs authority of the importing &nbsp;Party conducting the verification may request the importer to provide additional information if that &nbsp;customs authority considers that additional information is necessary in order to verify the originating &nbsp;status of the product or whether the other requirements of this Chapter are met. The customs &nbsp;authority of the importing Party may request the importer for specific documentation and &nbsp;information, if appropriate. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c333"><span class="c0">6. If the customs authority of the importing Party decides to suspend the granting of preferential &nbsp;tariff treatment to the product concerned while awaiting the results of the verification, the release of &nbsp;the products shall be offered to the importer subject to appropriate precautionary measures including </span></p><p class="c328"><span class="c0">37 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c351"><span class="c0">guarantees. Any suspension of preferential tariff treatment shall be terminated as soon as possible &nbsp;after the customs authority of the importing Party has ascertained the originating status of the &nbsp;products concerned, or the fulfilment of the other requirements of this Chapter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.25: Administrative cooperation </span></p><p class="c18"><span class="c0">1. In order to ensure the proper application of this Chapter, the Parties shall cooperate, through &nbsp;the customs authority of each Party, in verifying whether a product is originating and is in compliance &nbsp;with the other requirements provided for in this Chapter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c386"><span class="c0">2. If the claim for preferential tariff treatment was based on a statement on origin, as &nbsp;appropriate after having first requested information in accordance with Article ORIG.24(1) &nbsp;[Verification] and based on the reply from the importer, the customs authority of the importing Party &nbsp;conducting the verification may also request information from the customs authority of the exporting &nbsp;Party within a period of two years after the importation of the products, or from the moment the &nbsp;claim is made pursuant to point (a) of Article ORIG.18a(2) [Time of the claim for preferential &nbsp;treatment], if the customs authority of the importing Party conducting the verification considers that &nbsp;additional information is necessary in order to verify the originating status of the product or to verify &nbsp;that the other requirements provided for in this Chapter have been met. The request for information &nbsp;shall include the following elements: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) the statement on origin; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) the identity of the customs authority issuing the request; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) the name of the exporter; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(d) the subject and scope of the verification; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(e) any relevant documentation. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c418"><span class="c0">In addition, the customs authority of the importing Party may request the customs authority of the &nbsp;exporting Party to provide specific documentation and information, where appropriate. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c164"><span class="c0">3. The customs authority of the exporting Party may, in accordance with its laws and regulations, &nbsp;request documentation or examination by calling for any evidence, or by visiting the premises of the &nbsp;exporter, to review records and observe the facilities used in the production of the product. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c697"><span class="c0">4. Without prejudice to paragraph 5, the customs authority of the exporting Party receiving the &nbsp;request referred to in paragraph 2 shall provide the customs authority of the importing Party with the &nbsp;following information: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) the requested documentation, where available; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) an opinion on the originating status of the product; </span></p><p class="c8"><span class="c0">(c) the description of the product that is subject to examination and the tariff classification relevant &nbsp;to the application of this Chapter; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c757"><span class="c0">(d) a description and explanation of the production process that is sufficient to support the &nbsp;originating status of the product; </span></p><p class="c636"><span class="c0">38 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c119"><span class="c0">(e) information on the manner in which the examination of the product was conducted; and &nbsp;(f) supporting documentation, where appropriate. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c620"><span class="c0">5. The customs authority of the exporting Party shall not provide the information referred to in &nbsp;points (a), (d) and (f) of paragraph 4 to the customs authority of the importing Party if that information &nbsp;is deemed confidential by the exporter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c794"><span class="c0">6. Each Party shall notify the other Party of the contact details of the customs authorities and &nbsp;shall notify the other Party of any change to those contact details within 30 days after the date of the &nbsp;change. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.26: Denial of preferential tariff treatment </span></p><p class="c182"><span class="c0">1. Without prejudice to paragraph 3, the customs authority of the importing Party may deny &nbsp;preferential tariff treatment, if: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c520"><span class="c0">(a) within three months after the date of a request for information pursuant to Article ORIG.24(1) &nbsp;[Verification]: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c434"><span class="c0">(i) no reply has been provided by the importer; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c624"><span class="c0">(ii) where the claim for preferential tariff treatment was based on a statement on origin, &nbsp;no statement on origin has been provided; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c184"><span class="c0">(iii) where the claim for preferential tariff treatment was based on the importer&rsquo;s &nbsp;knowledge, the information provided by the importer is inadequate to confirm that the &nbsp;product is originating; </span></p><p class="c846"><span class="c0">(b) within three months after the date of a request for additional information pursuant to Article &nbsp;ORIG.24(5) [Verification]: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c500"><span class="c0">(i) no reply has been provided by the importer; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c832"><span class="c0">(ii) the information provided by the importer is inadequate to confirm that the product is &nbsp;originating; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c883"><span class="c0">(c) within 10 months</span><span class="c134">3 </span><span class="c0">after the date of a request for information pursuant to Article ORIG.25(2) &nbsp;[Administrative Cooperation]: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c500"><span class="c0">(i) no reply has been provided by the customs authority of the exporting Party; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c374"><span class="c0">(ii) the information provided by the customs authority of the exporting Party is inadequate to &nbsp;confirm that the product is originating. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c178"><span class="c0">2. The customs authority of the importing Party may deny preferential tariff treatment to a &nbsp;product for which an importer claims preferential tariff treatment where the importer fails to comply &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c570"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c787"><span class="c81">3 </span><span class="c77">The period will be of 12 months for requests of information pursuant to Article ORIG.25(2) [Administrative &nbsp;cooperation] addressed to the customs authority of the exporting Party during the first three months of the &nbsp;application of this Agreement.</span></p><p class="c103"><span class="c0">39 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c431"><span class="c0">with requirements under this Chapter other than those relating to the originating status of the &nbsp;products. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c579"><span class="c0">3. If the customs authority of the importing Party has sufficient justification to deny preferential &nbsp;tariff treatment under paragraph 1 of this Article, in cases where the customs authority of the &nbsp;exporting Party has provided an opinion pursuant to point (b) of Article ORIG.25(4) [Administrative &nbsp;cooperation] confirming the originating status of the products, the customs authority of the importing &nbsp;Party shall notify the customs authority of the exporting Party of its intention to deny the preferential &nbsp;tariff treatment within two months after the date of receipt of that opinion. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c18"><span class="c0">If such notification is made, consultations shall be held at the request of either Party, within three &nbsp;months after the date of the notification. The period for consultation may be extended on a case-by case basis by mutual agreement between the customs authorities of the Parties. The consultation may &nbsp;take place in accordance with the procedure set by the Trade Specialised Committee on Customs &nbsp;Cooperation and Rules of Origin. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c318"><span class="c0">Upon the expiry of the period for consultation, if the customs authority of the importing Party cannot &nbsp;confirm that the product is originating, it may deny the preferential tariff treatment if it has a sufficient &nbsp;justification for doing so and after having granted the importer the right to be heard. However, when &nbsp;the customs authority of the exporting Party confirms the originating status of the products and &nbsp;provides justification for such conclusion, the customs authority of the importing Party shall not deny &nbsp;preferential tariff treatment to a product on the sole ground that Article ORIG.25(5) [Administrative &nbsp;cooperation] has been applied. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c641"><span class="c0">4. In all cases, the settlement of differences between the importer and the customs authority of &nbsp;the Party of import shall be under the law of the Party of import. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.27: Confidentiality </span></p><p class="c565"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall maintain, in accordance with its laws and regulations, the confidentiality of &nbsp;any information provided to it by the other Party, pursuant to this Chapter, and shall protect that &nbsp;information from disclosure. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c59"><span class="c0">2. Where, notwithstanding Article ORIG.25(5) [Administrative cooperation], confidential &nbsp;business information has been obtained from the exporter by the customs authority of the exporting &nbsp;Party or importing Party through the application of Articles ORIG.24 [Verification] and ORIG.25 &nbsp;[Administrative cooperation], that information shall not be disclosed. </span></p><p class="c90"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall ensure that confidential information collected pursuant to this Chapter shall &nbsp;not be used for purposes other than the administration and enforcement of decisions and &nbsp;determinations relating to origin and to customs matters, except with the permission of the person or &nbsp;Party who provided the confidential information. </span></p><p class="c712"><span class="c0">4. Notwithstanding paragraph 3, a Party may allow information collected pursuant to this &nbsp;Chapter to be used in any administrative, judicial, or quasi-judicial proceedings instituted for failure &nbsp;to comply with customs-related laws implementing this Chapter. A Party shall notify the person or &nbsp;Party who provided the information in advance of such use. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.28: Administrative measures and sanctions </span></p><p class="c727"><span class="c0">Each Party shall ensure the effective enforcement of this Chapter. Each Party shall ensure that the &nbsp;competent authorities are able to impose administrative measures, and, where appropriate, </span></p><p class="c65"><span class="c0">40 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c39"><span class="c0">sanctions, in accordance with its laws and regulations, on any person who draws up a document, or &nbsp;causes a document to be drawn up, which contains incorrect information that was provided for the &nbsp;purpose of obtaining a preferential tariff treatment for a product, who does not comply with the &nbsp;requirements set out in Article ORIG.22 [Record-keeping requirements], or who does not provide the &nbsp;evidence, or refuses to submit to a visit, as referred to in Article ORIG.25(3) [Administrative &nbsp;cooperation]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c27">Section 3: Other Provisions </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.29: Ceuta and Melilla </span></p><p class="c428"><span class="c0">1. For purposes of this Chapter, in the case of the Union, the term &ldquo;Party&rdquo; does not include Ceuta &nbsp;and Melilla. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c706"><span class="c0">2. Products originating in the United Kingdom, when imported into Ceuta and Melilla, shall in all &nbsp;respects be subject to the same customs treatment under this Agreement, as that which is applied to &nbsp;products originating in the customs territory of the Union under Protocol 2 of the Act of Accession of &nbsp;the Kingdom of Spain and the Portuguese Republic to the European Union. The United Kingdom shall &nbsp;grant to imports of products covered by this Agreement and originating in Ceuta and Melilla the same &nbsp;customs treatment as that which is granted to products imported from and originating in the Union. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c502"><span class="c0">3. The rules of origin and origin procedures referred to in this Chapter apply mutatis mutandis &nbsp;to products exported from the United Kingdom to Ceuta and Melilla and to products exported from &nbsp;Ceuta and Melilla to the United Kingdom. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c325"><span class="c0">4. Ceuta and Melilla shall be considered as a single territory. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c563"><span class="c0">5. Article ORIG.4 [Cumulation of origin] applies to import and exports of products between the &nbsp;Union, the United Kingdom and Ceuta and Melilla. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c703"><span class="c0">6. The exporters shall enter &ldquo;the United Kingdom&rdquo; or &ldquo;Ceuta and Melilla&rdquo; in field 3 of the text of &nbsp;the statement on origin, depending on the origin of the product. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c503"><span class="c0">7. The customs authority of the Kingdom of Spain shall be responsible for the application and &nbsp;implementation of this Chapter in Ceuta and Melilla. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.30: Transitional provisions for products in transit or storage </span></p><p class="c658"><span class="c0">The provisions of this Agreement may be applied to products which comply with the provisions of this &nbsp;Chapter and which on the date of entry into force of this Agreement are either in transit from the &nbsp;exporting Party to the importing Party or under customs control in the importing Party without &nbsp;payment of import duties and taxes, subject to the making of a claim for preferential tariff treatment &nbsp;referred to in Article ORIG.18 [Claim for preferential tariff treatment] to the customs authority of the &nbsp;importing Party, within 12 months of that date. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article ORIG.31: Amendment to this chapter and its annexes </span></p><p class="c10"><span class="c0">The Partnership Council may amend this Chapter and its Annexes. </span></p><p class="c94"><span class="c0">Chapter 3: Sanitary and phytosanitary measures </span></p><p class="c659"><span class="c0">41 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article SPS.1: Objectives &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c10"><span class="c0">The objectives of this Chapter are to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c62"><span class="c0">(a) protect human, animal and plant life or health in the territories of the Parties while facilitating &nbsp;trade between the Parties; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) further the implementation of the SPS Agreement; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c326"><span class="c0">(c) ensure that the Parties&rsquo; sanitary and phytosanitary (&ldquo;SPS&rdquo;) measures do not create unnecessary &nbsp;barriers to trade; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">(d) promote greater transparency and understanding on the application of each Party&rsquo;s SPS measures; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c526"><span class="c0">(e) enhance cooperation between the Parties in the fight against antimicrobial resistance, promotion &nbsp;of sustainable food systems, protection of animal welfare, and on electronic certification; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c732"><span class="c0">(f) enhance cooperation in the relevant international organisations to develop international &nbsp;standards, guidelines and recommendations on animal health, food safety and plant health; and </span></p><p class="c181"><span class="c0">(g) promote implementation by each Party of international standards, guidelines and &nbsp;recommendations. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article SPS.2: Scope &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c873"><span class="c0">1. This Chapter applies to all SPS measures of a Party that may, directly or indirectly, affect trade &nbsp;between the Parties. </span></p><p class="c535"><span class="c0">2. This Chapter also lays down separate provisions regarding cooperation on animal welfare, &nbsp;antimicrobial resistance and sustainable food systems. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.3: Definitions &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of this Chapter, the following definitions apply: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c133"><span class="c0">(a) the definitions contained in Annex A of the SPS Agreement; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c884"><span class="c0">(b) the definitions adopted under the auspices of the Codex Alimentarius Commission (the &nbsp;&ldquo;Codex&rdquo;); &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c828"><span class="c0">(c) the definitions adopted under the auspices of the World Organisation for Animal Health (the &nbsp;&ldquo;OIE&rdquo;); and </span></p><p class="c808"><span class="c0">(d) the definitions adopted under the auspices of the International Plant Protection Convention &nbsp;(the &ldquo;IPPC&rdquo;). &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c449"><span class="c0">2. For the purposes of this Chapter: </span></p><p class="c629"><span class="c0">(a) &ldquo;import conditions&rdquo; means any SPS measures that are required to be fulfilled for the import of &nbsp;products; and</span></p><p class="c131"><span class="c0">42 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c174"><span class="c0">(b) &quot;protected zone&quot; for a specified regulated plant pest means an officially defined geographical &nbsp;area in which that pest is not established in spite of favourable conditions and its presence in &nbsp;other parts of the territory of the Party, and into which that pest is not allowed to be introduced. </span></p><p class="c315"><span class="c0">3. The Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures may adopt other &nbsp;definitions for the purposes of this Chapter, taking into consideration the glossaries and definitions of &nbsp;the relevant international organisations, such as the Codex, OIE and IPPC. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c339"><span class="c0">4. The definitions under the SPS Agreement prevail to the extent that there is an inconsistency &nbsp;between the definitions adopted by the Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary &nbsp;Measures or adopted under the auspices of the Codex, the OIE, the IPPC and the definitions under the &nbsp;SPS Agreement. In the event of an inconsistency between definitions adopted by the Trade Specialised &nbsp;Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures and the definitions set out in the Codex, OIE or &nbsp;IPPC, the definitions set out in the Codex, OIE or IPPC shall prevail. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.4: Rights and obligations &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c601"><span class="c0">The Parties reaffirm their rights and obligations under the SPS Agreement. This includes the right to &nbsp;adopt measures in accordance with Article 5(7) of the SPS Agreement. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article SPS.5: General principles </span></p><p class="c595"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall apply SPS measures for achieving their appropriate level of protection that &nbsp;are based on risk assessments in accordance with relevant provisions, including Article 5 of the SPS &nbsp;Agreement. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall not use SPS measures to create unjustified barriers to trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c580"><span class="c0">3. Regarding trade-related SPS procedures and approvals established under this Chapter, each &nbsp;Party shall ensure that these procedures and related SPS measures: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) are initiated and completed without undue delay; </span></p><p class="c652"><span class="c0">(b) do not include unnecessary, scientifically and technically unjustified or unduly burdensome &nbsp;information requests that might delay access to each other&rsquo;s markets; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c228"><span class="c0">(c) are not applied in a manner which would constitute arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination &nbsp;against the other Party&rsquo;s entire territory or parts of the other Party&rsquo;s territory where identical &nbsp;or similar SPS conditions exist; and </span></p><p class="c158"><span class="c0">(d) are proportionate to the risks identified and not more trade restrictive than necessary to &nbsp;achieve the importing Party&#39;s appropriate level of protection. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c796"><span class="c0">4. The Parties shall not use the procedures referred to in paragraph 3, or any requests for &nbsp;additional information, to delay access to their markets without scientific and technical justification. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c772"><span class="c0">5. Each Party shall ensure that any administrative procedure it requires concerning the import &nbsp;conditions on food safety, animal health or plant health is not more burdensome or trade restrictive &nbsp;than necessary to give the importing Party adequate confidence that these conditions are met. Each &nbsp;Party shall ensure that the negative effects on trade of any administrative procedures are kept to a &nbsp;minimum and that the clearance processes remain simple and expeditious while meeting the &nbsp;importing Party&rsquo;s conditions. </span></p><p class="c472"><span class="c0">43 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c56"><span class="c0">6. The importing Party shall not put in place any additional administrative system or procedure &nbsp;that unnecessarily hampers trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.6: Official certification </span></p><p class="c307"><span class="c0">1. Where the importing Party requires official certificates, the model certificates shall be: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c723"><span class="c0">(a) set in line with the principles as laid down in the international standards of the Codex, the &nbsp;IPPC and the OIE; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c815"><span class="c0">(b) applicable to imports from all parts of the territory of the exporting Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c680"><span class="c0">2. The Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures may agree on &nbsp;specific cases where the model certificates referred to in paragraph 1 would be established only &nbsp;for a part or parts of the territory of the exporting Party. The Parties shall promote the &nbsp;implementation of electronic certification and other technologies to facilitate trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c355"><span class="c0">Article SPS.7: Import conditions and procedures </span></p><p class="c402"><span class="c0">1. Without prejudice to the rights and obligations each Party has under the SPS Agreement and &nbsp;this Chapter, the import conditions of the importing Party shall apply to the entire territory of the &nbsp;exporting Party in a consistent manner. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c275"><span class="c0">2. The exporting Party shall ensure that products exported to the other Party, such as animals &nbsp;and animal products, plants and plant products, or other related objects, meet the SPS requirements &nbsp;of the importing Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c64"><span class="c0">3. The importing Party may require that imports of particular products are subject to &nbsp;authorisation. Such authorisation shall be granted where a request is made by the relevant competent &nbsp;authority of the exporting Party which objectively demonstrates, to the satisfaction of the importing &nbsp;Party, that the authorisation requirements of the importing Party are fulfilled. The relevant competent &nbsp;authority of the exporting Party may make a request for authorisation in respect of the entire territory &nbsp;of the exporting Party. The importing Party shall grant such requests on that basis, where they fulfil &nbsp;the authorisation requirements of the importing Party as set out in this paragraph. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c714"><span class="c0">4. The importing Party shall not introduce authorisation requirements which are additional to &nbsp;those which apply at the end of the transition period, unless the application of such requirements to &nbsp;further products is justified to mitigate a significant risk to human, animal or plant health. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c622"><span class="c0">5. The importing Party shall establish and communicate to the other Party import conditions for &nbsp;all products. The importing Party shall ensure that its import conditions are applied in a proportionate &nbsp;and non-discriminatory manner. </span></p><p class="c545"><span class="c0">6. Without prejudice to provisional measures under Article 5(7) of the SPS Agreement, for &nbsp;products, or other related objects, where a phytosanitary concern exists, the import conditions shall &nbsp;be restricted to measures to protect against regulated pests of the importing Party and shall be &nbsp;applicable to the entire territory of the exporting Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c640"><span class="c0">7. Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 and 3, in the case of import authorisation requests for a specific &nbsp;product, where the exporting Party has requested to be examined only for a part, or certain parts, of &nbsp;its territory (in the case of the Union, individual Member States), the importing Party shall promptly &nbsp;proceed to the examination of that request. Where the importing Party receives requests in respect &nbsp;of the specific product from more than one part of the exporting Party, or, where further requests are </span></p><p class="c384"><span class="c0">44 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c240"><span class="c0">received in respect of a product which has already been authorised, the importing Party shall expedite &nbsp;completion of the authorisation procedure, taking into account the identical or similar SPS regime &nbsp;applicable in the different parts of the exporting Party. </span></p><p class="c314"><span class="c0">8. Each Party shall ensure that all SPS control, inspection and approval procedures are initiated &nbsp;and completed without undue delay. Information requirements shall be limited to what is necessary &nbsp;for the approval process to take into account information already available in the importing Party, &nbsp;such as on the legislative framework and audit reports of the exporting Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c869"><span class="c0">9. Except in duly justified circumstances related to its level of protection, each Party shall provide &nbsp;a transition period between the publication of any changes to its approval procedures and their &nbsp;application to allow the other Party to become familiar with and adapt to such changes. Each Party &nbsp;shall not unduly prolong the approval process for applications submitted prior to publication of the &nbsp;changes. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">10. In relation to the processes set out in paragraphs 3 to 8, the following actions shall be taken: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c890"><span class="c0">(a) as soon as the importing Party has positively concluded its assessment, it shall promptly take all &nbsp;necessary legislative and administrative measures to allow trade to take place without undue &nbsp;delay; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c411"><span class="c0">(b) the exporting Party shall: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c530"><span class="c0">(i) provide all relevant information required by the importing Party; and (ii) give reasonable access to the importing Party for audit and other relevant procedures. </span></p><p class="c366"><span class="c0">(c) the importing party shall establish a list of regulated pests for products, or other related objects, &nbsp;where a phytosanitary concern exists. That list shall contain: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c427"><span class="c0">(i) the pests not known to occur within any part of its own territory; </span></p><p class="c438"><span class="c0">(ii) the pests known to occur within its own territory and under official control; </span></p><p class="c573"><span class="c0">(iii) the pests known to occur within parts of its own territory and for which pest free areas or protected zones are established; and </span></p><p class="c332"><span class="c0">(iv) non-quarantine pests known to occur within its own territory and under official control for specified planting material. </span></p><p class="c878"><span class="c0">11. The importing Party shall accept consignments without requiring that the importing Party &nbsp;verifies compliance of those consignments before their departure from the territory of the exporting &nbsp;Party. </span></p><p class="c509"><span class="c0">12. A Party may collect fees for the costs incurred to conduct specific SPS frontier checks, which &nbsp;should not exceed the recovery of the costs. </span></p><p class="c695"><span class="c0">13. The importing Party shall have the right to carry out import checks on products imported from &nbsp;the exporting Party for the purposes of ensuring compliance with its SPS import requirements. </span></p><p class="c185"><span class="c0">14. The import checks carried out on products imported from the exporting Party shall be based &nbsp;on the SPS risk associated with such importations. Import checks shall be carried out only to the extent </span></p><p class="c82"><span class="c0">45 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c451"><span class="c0">necessary to protect human, animal or plant life and health, without undue delay and with a minimum &nbsp;effect on trade between the Parties. </span></p><p class="c498"><span class="c0">15. Information on the proportion of products from the exporting Party checked at import shall &nbsp;be made available by the importing Party upon request of the exporting Party. </span></p><p class="c364"><span class="c0">16. If import checks reveal non-compliance with the relevant import conditions the action taken &nbsp;by the importing Party must be based on an assessment of the risk involved and not be more trade &nbsp;restrictive than required to achieve the Party&#39;s appropriate level of SPS protection. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.8 Lists of approved establishments </span></p><p class="c216"><span class="c0">1. Whenever justified, the importing Party may maintain a list of approved establishments &nbsp;meeting its import requirements as a condition to allow imports of animal products from these &nbsp;establishments. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c467"><span class="c0">2. Unless justified to mitigate a significant risk to human or animal health, lists of approved &nbsp;establishments shall only be required for the products for which they were required at the end of the &nbsp;transition period. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c503"><span class="c0">3. The exporting Party shall inform the importing Party of its list of establishments meeting the &nbsp;importing Party&rsquo;s conditions which shall be based on guarantees provided by the exporting Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c561"><span class="c0">4. Upon a request from the exporting Party, the importing Party shall approve establishments &nbsp;which are situated in the territory of the exporting Party, based on guarantees provided by the &nbsp;exporting Party, without prior inspection of individual establishments. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c743"><span class="c0">5. Unless the importing Party requests additional information and subject to guarantees being &nbsp;provided by the exporting party, the importing Party shall take the necessary legislative or &nbsp;administrative measures, in accordance with its applicable legal procedures, to allow imports from &nbsp;those establishments without undue delay. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c749"><span class="c0">6. The list of the approved establishments shall be made publicly available by the importing &nbsp;Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c146"><span class="c0">7. Where the importing Party decides to reject the request of the exporting Party to accept &nbsp;adding an establishment to the list of approved establishments, it shall inform the exporting Party &nbsp;without delay and shall submit a reply, including information about the non-conformities which led to &nbsp;the rejection of the establishment&rsquo;s approval. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.9: Transparency and exchange of information &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c752"><span class="c0">1.
