Each Party shall pursue transparency as regards SPS measures applicable to trade and shall &nbsp;for those purposes undertake the following actions: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c649"><span class="c0">(a) promptly communicate to the other Party any changes to its SPS measures and approval &nbsp;procedures, including changes that may affect its capacity to fulfil the SPS import requirements &nbsp;of the other Party for certain products; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(b) enhance mutual understanding of its SPS measures and their application; </span></p><p class="c98"><span class="c0">46 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c201"><span class="c0">(c) exchange information with the other Party on matters related to the development and application &nbsp;of SPS measures, including the progress on new available scientific evidence, that affect, or may &nbsp;affect, trade between the Parties with a view to minimising negative trade effects; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c495"><span class="c0">(d) upon request of the other Party, communicate the conditions that apply for the import of specific &nbsp;products within 20 working days; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c556"><span class="c0">(e) upon request of the other Party, communicate the state of play of the procedure for the &nbsp;authorisation of specific products within 20 working days; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c99"><span class="c0">(f) communicate to the other Party any significant change to the structure or organisation of a Party&#39;s &nbsp;competent authority; </span></p><p class="c147"><span class="c0">(g) on request, communicate the results of a Party&#39;s official control and a report that concerns the &nbsp;results of the control carried out; </span></p><p class="c489"><span class="c0">(h) on request, communicate the results of an import check provided for in case of a rejected or a non compliant consignment; and </span></p><p class="c76"><span class="c0">(i) on request, communicate, without undue delay, a risk assessment or scientific opinion produced &nbsp;by a Party that is relevant to this Chapter. </span></p><p class="c888"><span class="c0">2. Where a Party has made available the information in paragraph 1 via notification to the WTO&rsquo;s &nbsp;Central Registry of Notifications or to the relevant international standard-setting body, in accordance &nbsp;with its relevant rules, the requirements in paragraph 1, as they apply to that information, are fulfilled. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.10: Adaptation to regional conditions &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c421"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall recognise the concept of zoning including disease or pest-free areas, &nbsp;protected zones and areas of low disease or pest prevalence and shall apply it to the trade between &nbsp;the Parties, in accordance with the SPS Agreement, including the guidelines to further the practical &nbsp;implementation of Article 6 of the SPS Agreement (WTO/SPS Committee Decision G/SPS/48) and the &nbsp;relevant recommendations, standards and guidelines of the OIE and IPPC. The Trade Specialised &nbsp;Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures may define further details for these procedures, &nbsp;taking into account any relevant SPS Agreement, OIE and IPPC standards, guidelines or &nbsp;recommendations. </span></p><p class="c502"><span class="c0">2. The Parties may also agree to cooperate on the concept of compartmentalisation as referred &nbsp;to in Chapters 4.4 and 4.5 of the OIE Terrestrial Animal Health Code and Chapters 4.1 and 4.2 of the &nbsp;OIE Aquatic Animal Health Code</span><span class="c27">. </span></p><p class="c246"><span class="c0">3. When establishing or maintaining the zones referred to in paragraph 1, the Parties shall &nbsp;consider factors such as geographical location, ecosystems, epidemiological surveillance and the &nbsp;effectiveness of SPS controls. </span></p><p class="c696"><span class="c0">4. With regard to animals and animal products, when establishing or maintaining import &nbsp;conditions upon the request of the exporting Party, the importing Party shall recognise the disease free areas established by the exporting Party as a basis for consideration towards the determination &nbsp;of allowing or maintaining the import, without prejudice to paragraphs 8 and 9. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c54"><span class="c0">5. The exporting Party shall identify the parts of its territory referred to in paragraph 4 and, if &nbsp;requested, provide a full explanation and supporting data based on the OIE standards, or in other ways </span></p><p class="c328"><span class="c0">47 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c548"><span class="c0">established by the Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures, based on &nbsp;the knowledge acquired through experience of the exporting Party&rsquo;s relevant authorities. </span></p><p class="c560"><span class="c0">6. With regard to plants, plant products, and other related objects, when establishing or &nbsp;maintaining phytosanitary import conditions, on request of the exporting Party, the importing Party &nbsp;shall recognise the pest-free areas, pest-free places of production, pest-free production sites, areas of &nbsp;low pest prevalence and protected zones established by the exporting Party as a basis for &nbsp;consideration towards the determination to allow or maintain the import, without prejudice to &nbsp;paragraphs 8 and 9. </span></p><p class="c700"><span class="c0">7. The exporting Party shall identify its pest-free areas, pest-free places of production, pest-free &nbsp;production sites and areas of low pest prevalence or protected zones. If requested by the importing &nbsp;Party, the exporting Party shall provide a full explanation and supporting data based on the &nbsp;International Standards for Phytosanitary Measures developed under the IPPC, or in other ways &nbsp;established by the Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures, based on &nbsp;the knowledge acquired through experience of the exporting Party&#39;s relevant phytosanitary &nbsp;authorities. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c331"><span class="c0">8. The Parties shall recognise disease-free areas and protected zones which are in place at the &nbsp;end of the transition period. </span></p><p class="c657"><span class="c0">9. Paragraph 8 shall also apply to subsequent adaptations to the disease-free areas and &nbsp;protected zones (in the case of the United Kingdom pest-free areas), except in cases of significant &nbsp;changes in the disease or pest situations. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c267"><span class="c0">10. The Parties may carry out audits and verifications pursuant to Article 11 to implement &nbsp;paragraphs 4 to 9 of this Article. </span></p><p class="c688"><span class="c0">11. The Parties shall establish close cooperation with the objective of maintaining confidence in &nbsp;the procedures in relation to the establishment of disease- or pest-free areas, pest-free places of &nbsp;production, pest-free production sites and areas of low pest or disease prevalence and protected &nbsp;zones, with the aim to minimise trade disruption. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c816"><span class="c0">12. The importing Party shall base its own determination of the animal or plant health status of &nbsp;the exporting Party or parts thereof on the information provided by the exporting Party in accordance &nbsp;with the SPS Agreement, OIE and IPPC standards, and take into consideration any determination made &nbsp;by the exporting Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c79"><span class="c0">13. Where the importing Party does not accept the determination made by the exporting Party &nbsp;as referred to in paragraph 12 of this Article, the importing Party shall objectively justify and explain &nbsp;to the exporting Party the reasons for that rejection and, upon request, hold consultations, in &nbsp;accordance with Article SPS 12(2). </span></p><p class="c849"><span class="c0">14. Each Party shall ensure that the obligations set out in paragraphs 4 to 9, 12 and 13 are carried &nbsp;out without undue delay. The importing Party will expedite the recognition of the disease or pest &nbsp;status when the status has been recovered after an outbreak. </span></p><p class="c161"><span class="c0">15. Where a Party considers that a specific region has a special status with respect to a specific &nbsp;disease and which fulfils the criteria laid down in the OIE Terrestrial Animal Health Code Chapter 1.2 &nbsp;or the OIE Aquatic Animal Health Code Chapter 1.2, it may request recognition of this status. The &nbsp;importing Party may request additional guarantees in respect of imports of live animals and animal &nbsp;products appropriate to the agreed status.</span></p><p class="c395"><span class="c0">48 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article SPS.11: Audits and verifications &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c465"><span class="c0">1. The importing Party may carry out audits and verifications of the following: &nbsp;(a) all or part of the other Party&rsquo;s authorities&rsquo; inspection and certification system; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c206"><span class="c0">(b) the results of the controls carried out under the exporting Party&rsquo;s inspection and certification &nbsp;system. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c603"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall carry out those audits and verifications in accordance with the provisions of &nbsp;the SPS Agreement, taking into account the relevant international standards, guidelines and &nbsp;recommendations of the Codex Alimentarius, OIE or IPPC. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c731"><span class="c0">3. For the purposes of carrying out such audits and verifications, the importing Party may &nbsp;conduct audits and verifications by means of requests of information from the exporting Party or audit &nbsp;and verification visits to the exporting Party, which may include: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c85"><span class="c0">(a) an assessment of all or part of the responsible authorities&rsquo; total control programme, including, &nbsp;where appropriate, reviews of regulatory audit and inspection activities; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) on-the-spot checks; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c126"><span class="c0">(c) the collection of information and data to assess the causes of recurring or emerging problems &nbsp;in relation to exports of products. </span></p><p class="c802"><span class="c0">4. The importing Party shall share with the exporting Party the results and conclusions of the &nbsp;audits and verifications carried out pursuant to paragraph 1. The importing Party may make these &nbsp;results publicly available. </span></p><p class="c458"><span class="c0">5. Prior to the commencement of an audit or verification, the Parties shall discuss the objectives &nbsp;and scope of the audit or verification, the criteria or requirements against which the exporting Party &nbsp;will be assessed, and the itinerary and procedures for conducting the audit or verification which shall &nbsp;be laid down in an audit or verification plan. Unless otherwise agreed by the Parties, the importing &nbsp;Party shall provide the exporting Party with an audit or verification plan at least 30 days prior to the &nbsp;commencement of the audit or verification. </span></p><p class="c164"><span class="c0">6. The importing Party shall provide the exporting Party the opportunity to comment on the draft &nbsp;audit or verification report. The importing Party shall provide a final report in writing to the exporting &nbsp;Party normally within two months from the date of receipt of those comments. </span></p><p class="c761"><span class="c0">7. Each Party shall bear its own costs associated with such an audit or verification. &nbsp;Article SPS.12: Notification and consultation &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c497"><span class="c0">1. A Party shall notify the other Party without undue delay of: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(a) a significant change to pest or disease status; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) the emergence of a new animal disease; </span></p><p class="c809"><span class="c0">(c) a finding of epidemiological importance with respect to an animal disease; (d) a significant food safety issue identified by a Party; </span></p><p class="c26"><span class="c0">49 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c383"><span class="c0">(e) any additional measures beyond the basic requirements of their respective SPS measures taken to &nbsp;control or eradicate animal disease or protect human health, and any changes in preventive &nbsp;policies, including vaccination policies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c678"><span class="c0">(f) on request, the results of a Party&rsquo;s official control and a report that concerns the results of the &nbsp;control carried out; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(g) any significant changes to the functions of a system or database. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c420"><span class="c0">2. If a Party has a significant concern with respect to food safety, plant health, or animal health, &nbsp;or an SPS measure that the other Party has proposed or implemented, that Party may request &nbsp;technical consultations with the other Party. The requested Party should respond to the request &nbsp;without undue delay. Each Party shall endeavour to provide the information necessary to avoid a &nbsp;disruption to trade and, as the case may be, to reach a mutually acceptable solution. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c162"><span class="c0">3. Consultations referred to in paragraph 2 may be held via telephone conference, &nbsp;videoconference, or any other means of communication mutually agreed on by the Parties. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.13: Emergency measures &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c208"><span class="c0">1. If the importing Party considers that there is a serious risk to human, animal or plant life and &nbsp;health, it may take without prior notification the necessary measures for the protection of human, &nbsp;animal or plant life and health. For consignments that are in transit between the Parties, the importing &nbsp;Party shall consider the most suitable and proportionate solution to avoid unnecessary disruptions to &nbsp;trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c598"><span class="c0">2. The Party taking the measures shall notify the other Party of an emergency SPS measure as &nbsp;soon as possible after its decision to implement the measure and no later than 24 hours after the &nbsp;decision has been taken. If a Party requests technical consultations to address the emergency SPS &nbsp;measure, the technical consultations must be held within 10 days of the notification of the emergency &nbsp;SPS measure. The Parties shall consider any information provided through the technical consultations. These consultations shall be carried out in order to avoid unnecessary disruptions to trade. The Parties &nbsp;may consider options for the facilitation of the implementation or the replacement of the measures. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c84"><span class="c0">3. The importing Party shall consider, in a timely manner, information that was provided by the &nbsp;exporting Party when it makes its decision with respect to consignments that, at the time of adoption &nbsp;of the emergency SPS measure, are being transported between the Parties, in order to avoid &nbsp;unnecessary disruptions to trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c273"><span class="c0">4. The importing Party shall ensure that any emergency measure taken on the grounds referred &nbsp;to in paragraph 1 of this Article is not maintained without scientific evidence or, in cases where &nbsp;scientific evidence is insufficient, is adopted in accordance with Article 5(7) of the SPS Agreement. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article: SPS.14: Multilateral international fora &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c14"><span class="c0">The Parties agree to cooperate in multilateral international fora on the development of international &nbsp;standards, guidelines and recommendations in the areas under the scope of this Chapter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.15: Implementation and competent authorities </span></p><p class="c602"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of the implementation of this Chapter, each Party shall take all of the &nbsp;following into account: </span></p><p class="c376"><span class="c0">50 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c369"><span class="c0">(a) decisions of the WTO SPS Committee; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c346"><span class="c0">(b) the work of the relevant international standard setting bodies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c455"><span class="c0">(c) any knowledge and past experience it has of trading with the exporting Party; and (d) information provided by the other Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c439"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall, without delay, provide each other with a description of the competent &nbsp;authorities of the Parties for the implementation of this Chapter. The Parties shall notify each other &nbsp;of any significant change to these competent authorities. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c69"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall ensure that its competent authorities have the necessary resources to &nbsp;effectively implement this Chapter. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.16: Cooperation on animal welfare &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c49"><span class="c0">1. The Parties recognise that animals are sentient beings. They also recognise the connection &nbsp;between improved welfare of animals and sustainable food production systems. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c295"><span class="c0">2. The Parties undertake to cooperate in international fora to promote the development of the &nbsp;best possible animal welfare practices and their implementation. In particular, the Parties shall &nbsp;cooperate to reinforce and broaden the scope of the OIE animal welfare standards, as well as their &nbsp;implementation, with a focus on farmed animals. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c519"><span class="c0">3. The Parties shall exchange information, expertise and experiences in the field of animal &nbsp;welfare, particularly related to breeding, holding, handling, transportation and slaughter of food producing animals. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c687"><span class="c0">4. The Parties shall strengthen their cooperation on research in the area of animal welfare in &nbsp;relation to animal breeding and the treatment of animals on farms, during transport and at slaughter. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.17: Cooperation on antimicrobial resistance </span></p><p class="c408"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall provide a framework for dialogue and cooperation with a view to &nbsp;strengthening the fight against the development of anti-microbial resistance. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c814"><span class="c0">2. The Parties recognise that anti-microbial resistance is a serious threat to human and animal &nbsp;health. Misuse of anti-microbials in animal production, including non-therapeutic use, can contribute &nbsp;to anti-microbial resistance that may represent a risk to human life. The Parties recognise that the &nbsp;nature of the threat requires a transnational and One Health approach. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c43"><span class="c0">3. With a view to combating antimicrobial resistance, the Parties shall endeavour to cooperate &nbsp;internationally with regional or multilateral work programmes to reduce the unnecessary use of &nbsp;antibiotics in animal production and to work towards the cessation of the use of antibiotics as growth &nbsp;promotors internationally to combat antimicrobial resistance in line with the One Health approach, &nbsp;and in compliance with the Global Action Plan. </span></p><p class="c406"><span class="c0">4. The Parties shall collaborate in the development of international guidelines, standards, &nbsp;recommendations and actions in relevant international organisations aiming to promote the prudent &nbsp;and responsible use of antibiotics in animal husbandry and veterinary practices. </span></p><p class="c163"><span class="c0">51 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c419"><span class="c0">5. The dialogue referred to in paragraph 1 shall cover, </span><span class="c27">inter alia</span><span class="c0">: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c475"><span class="c0">(a) collaboration to follow up existing and future guidelines, standards, recommendations and &nbsp;actions developed in relevant international organisations and existing and future initiatives and &nbsp;national plans aiming to promote the prudent and responsible use of antibiotics and relating to &nbsp;animal production and veterinary practices; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c647"><span class="c0">(b) collaboration in the implementation of the recommendations of OIE, WHO and Codex, in &nbsp;particular CAC-RCP61/2005; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(c) the exchange of information on good farming practices; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(d) the promotion of research, innovation and development; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c514"><span class="c0">(e) the promotion of multidisciplinary approaches to combat antimicrobial resistance, including the &nbsp;One Health approach of the WHO, OIE and Codex Alimentarius. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SPS.18: Sustainable food systems &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c581"><span class="c0">Each Party shall encourage its food safety, animal and plant health services to cooperate with their &nbsp;counterparts in the other Party with the aim of promoting sustainable food production methods and &nbsp;food systems. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article SPS.19: Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c625"><span class="c0">The Trade Specialised Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures shall supervise the &nbsp;implementation and operation of this Chapter and have the following functions: </span></p><p class="c639"><span class="c0">(a) promptly clarifying and addressing, where possible, any issue raised by a Party relating to the &nbsp;development, adoption or application of sanitary and phytosanitary requirements, standards &nbsp;and recommendations under this Chapter or the SPS Agreement; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) discussing ongoing processes on the development of new regulations; </span></p><p class="c826"><span class="c0">(c) discussing as expeditiously as possible concerns expressed by a Party with regard to the SPS import &nbsp;conditions and procedures applied by the other Party; </span></p><p class="c187"><span class="c0">(d) regularly reviewing the Parties&rsquo; SPS measures, including certification requirements and border &nbsp;clearance processes, and their application, in order to facilitate trade between the Parties, in &nbsp;accordance with the principles, objectives and procedures set out in Article 5 of the SPS &nbsp;Agreement. Each Party shall identify any appropriate action it will take, including in relation to &nbsp;the frequency of identity and physical checks, taking into consideration the results of this review &nbsp;and based on the criteria laid down in ANNEX SPS-1: Criteria referred to in Article SPS.19.(d). </span></p><p class="c516"><span class="c0">(e) exchanging views, information, and experiences with respect to the cooperation activities on &nbsp;protecting animal welfare and the fight against antimicrobial resistance carried out under SPS. &nbsp;16 and 17; </span></p><p class="c546"><span class="c0">(f) on request of a Party, considering what constitutes a significant change in the disease or pest &nbsp;situation referred to in Article SPS 10(9); </span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(g) adopting decisions to:</span></p><p class="c811"><span class="c0">52 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c169"><span class="c0">(i) add definitions as referred to in Article SPS 3(3); </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(ii) define the specific cases referred to in Article SPS 6(2); </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(iii) define details for the procedures referred to in Article SPS 10(1); </span></p><p class="c202"><span class="c0">(iv) establish other ways to support the explanations referred to in Article SPS 10(5) and (7). </span></p><p class="c94"><span class="c0">Chapter 4: Technical barriers to trade </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article TBT.1: Objective &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c745"><span class="c0">The objective of this Chapter is to facilitate trade in goods between the Parties by preventing, &nbsp;identifying and eliminating unnecessary technical barriers to trade. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.2: Scope &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c730"><span class="c0">1. This Chapter applies to the preparation, adoption and application of all standards, technical &nbsp;regulations and conformity assessment procedures, which may affect trade in goods between the &nbsp;Parties. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. This Chapter does not apply to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c200"><span class="c0">(a) purchasing specifications prepared by governmental bodies for production or consumption &nbsp;requirements of such bodies; or </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) SPS measures that fall within scope of Chapter 3 [Sanitary and phytosanitary measures]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c673"><span class="c0">3. The Annexes to this Chapter apply, in respect of products within their scope, in addition to &nbsp;this Chapter. Any provision in an Annex to this Chapter that an international standard or body or &nbsp;organisation is to be considered or recognised as relevant, does not prevent a standard developed by &nbsp;any other body or organisation from being considered to be a relevant international standard pursuant &nbsp;to Article TBT.4 (4) and (5). </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.3: Relationship with the TBT Agreement &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c709"><span class="c0">1. Articles 2 to 9 of and Annexes 1 and 3 to the TBT Agreement are incorporated into and made &nbsp;part of this Agreement </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c627"><span class="c0">2. Terms referred to in this Chapter and in the Annexes to this Chapter shall have the same &nbsp;meaning as they have in the TBT Agreement. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.4: Technical regulations &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c285"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall carry out impact assessments of planned technical regulations in accordance &nbsp;with its respective rules and procedures. The rules and procedures referred to in this paragraph and &nbsp;in paragraph 8 may provide for exceptions. </span></p><p class="c398"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall assess the available regulatory and non-regulatory alternatives to the &nbsp;proposed technical regulation that may fulfil the Party&#39;s legitimate objectives, in accordance with &nbsp;Article 2.2 of the TBT Agreement. </span></p><p class="c665"><span class="c0">53 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c679"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall use relevant international standards as a basis for its technical regulations &nbsp;except when it can demonstrate that such international standards would be an ineffective or &nbsp;inappropriate means for the fulfilment of the legitimate objectives pursued. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c459"><span class="c0">4. International standards developed by the International Organization for Standardization (ISO), &nbsp;International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC), International Telecommunication Union (ITU) and &nbsp;Codex Alimentarius Commission (Codex) shall be the relevant international standards within the &nbsp;meaning of Article 2, Article 5 and Annex 3 of the TBT Agreement. </span></p><p class="c70"><span class="c0">5. A standard developed by other international organisations, could also be considered a &nbsp;relevant international standard within the meaning of Article 2, Article 5 and Annex 3 of the TBT &nbsp;Agreement, provided that: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) it has been developed by a standardising body which seeks to establish consensus either: </span></p><p class="c320"><span class="c0">(i) among national delegations of the participating WTO Members representing all the &nbsp;national standardising bodies in their territory that have adopted, or expect to adopt, &nbsp;standards for the subject matter to which the international standardisation activity &nbsp;relates, or, &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c843"><span class="c0">(ii) among governmental bodies of participating WTO Members, and, </span></p><p class="c698"><span class="c0">(b) it has been developed in accordance with the Decision of the WTO Committee on Technical &nbsp;Barriers to Trade on Principles for the Development of International Standards, Guides and &nbsp;Recommendations with relation to Articles 2, 5, and Annex 3 of the TBT Agreement.</span><span class="c805">4</span><span class="c71">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c522"><span class="c0">6. Where a Party does not use international standards as a basis for a technical regulation, on &nbsp;request of the other Party, it shall identify any substantial deviation from the relevant international &nbsp;standard, explain the reasons why such standards were judged inappropriate or ineffective for the &nbsp;objective pursued, and provide the scientific or technical evidence on which that assessment was &nbsp;based. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c707"><span class="c0">7. Each Party shall review its technical regulations to increase the convergence of those technical &nbsp;regulations with relevant international standards, taking into account, </span><span class="c27">inter alia</span><span class="c0">, any new &nbsp;developments in the relevant international standards or any changes in the circumstances that have &nbsp;given rise to divergence from any relevant international standards. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c606"><span class="c0">8. In accordance with its respective rules and procedures and without prejudice to Title X [Good &nbsp;Regulatory Practices and Regulatory Cooperation], when developing a major technical regulation &nbsp;which may have a significant effect on trade, each Party shall ensure that procedures exist that allow &nbsp;persons to express their opinion in a public consultation, except where urgent problems of safety, &nbsp;health, environment or national security arise or threaten to arise. Each Party shall allow persons of &nbsp;the other Party to participate in such consultations on terms that are no less favourable than those &nbsp;accorded to its own nationals, and shall make the results of those consultations public. </span></p><p class="c148"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c740"><span class="c81">4 </span><span class="c77">G/TBT/9, 13 November 2000, Annex 4.</span></p><p class="c217"><span class="c0">54 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article TBT.5: Standards &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c212"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall encourage the standardising bodies established within its territory, as well as &nbsp;the regional standardising bodies of which a Party or the standardising bodies established in its &nbsp;territory are members: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c101"><span class="c0">(a) to participate, within the limits of their resources, in the preparation of international standards &nbsp;by relevant international standardising bodies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c702"><span class="c0">(b) to use relevant international standards as a basis for the standards they develop, except where &nbsp;such international standards would be ineffective or inappropriate, for example because of an &nbsp;insufficient level of protection, fundamental climatic or geographical factors or fundamental &nbsp;technological problems; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(c) to avoid duplications of, or overlaps with, the work of international standardising bodies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c818"><span class="c0">(d) to review national and regional standards that are not based on relevant international &nbsp;standards at regular intervals, with a view to increasing the convergence of those standards &nbsp;with relevant international standards; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c109"><span class="c0">(e) to cooperate with the relevant standardising bodies of the other Party in international &nbsp;standardisation activities, including through cooperation in the international standardising &nbsp;bodies or at regional level; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c621"><span class="c0">(f) to foster bilateral cooperation with the standardising bodies of the other Party; and (g) to exchange information between standardising bodies. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c803"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall exchange information on: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(a) their respective use of standards in support of technical regulations; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c298"><span class="c0">(b) their respective standardisation processes, and the extent to which they use international, &nbsp;regional or sub-regional standards as a basis for their national standards. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c518"><span class="c0">3. Where standards are rendered mandatory in a draft technical regulation or conformity &nbsp;assessment procedure, through incorporation or reference, the transparency obligations set out in &nbsp;Article TBT.7 [Transparency] and in Articles 2 or 5 of the TBT Agreement shall apply. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c582"><span class="c0">Article TBT.6: Conformity assessment &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c819"><span class="c0">1. Article TBT.4 [Technical regulations] concerning the preparation, adoption and application of &nbsp;technical regulations shall also apply to conformity assessment procedures, </span><span class="c27">mutatis mutandis</span><span class="c0">. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c644"><span class="c0">2. Where a Party requires conformity assessment as a positive assurance that a product &nbsp;conforms with a technical regulation, it shall: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c158"><span class="c0">(a) select conformity assessment procedures that are proportionate to the risks involved, as &nbsp;determined on the basis of a risk-assessment; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c329"><span class="c0">(b) consider as proof of compliance with technical regulations the use of a supplier&rsquo;s declaration of &nbsp;conformity, i.e. a declaration of conformity issued by the manufacturer on the sole </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">55 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c167"><span class="c0">responsibility of the manufacturer without a mandatory third-party assessment, as assurance &nbsp;of conformity among the options for showing compliance with technical regulations; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c211"><span class="c0">(c) where requested by the other Party, provide information on the criteria used to select the &nbsp;conformity assessment procedures for specific products. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c387"><span class="c0">3. Where a Party requires third party conformity assessment as a positive assurance that a &nbsp;product conforms with a technical regulation and it has not reserved this task to a government &nbsp;authority as specified in paragraph 4, it shall: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c550"><span class="c0">(a) use accreditation, as appropriate, as a means to demonstrate technical competence to qualify &nbsp;conformity assessment bodies. Without prejudice to its right to establish requirements for &nbsp;conformity assessment bodies, each Party recognises the valuable role that accreditation &nbsp;operated with authority derived from government and on a non-commercial basis can play in &nbsp;the qualification of conformity assessment bodies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) use relevant international standards for accreditation and conformity assessment; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c441"><span class="c0">(c) encourage accreditation bodies and conformity assessment bodies located within its territory &nbsp;to join any relevant functioning international agreements or arrangements for harmonisation &nbsp;or facilitation of acceptance of conformity assessment results; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c799"><span class="c0">(d) if two or more conformity assessment bodies are authorised by a Party to carry out conformity &nbsp;assessment procedures required for placing a product on the market, ensure that economic &nbsp;operators have a choice amongst the conformity assessment bodies designated by the &nbsp;authorities of a Party for a particular product or set of products; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c104"><span class="c0">(e) ensure that conformity assessment bodies are independent of manufacturers, importers and &nbsp;economic operators in general and that there are no conflicts of interest between accreditation &nbsp;bodies and conformity assessment bodies; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c681"><span class="c0">(f) allow conformity assessment bodies to use subcontractors to perform testing or inspections in &nbsp;relation to the conformity assessment, including subcontractors located in the territory of the &nbsp;other Party, and may require subcontractors to meet the same requirements the conformity &nbsp;assessment body must meet to perform such testing or inspections itself; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c349"><span class="c0">(g) publish on a single website a list of the bodies that it has designated to perform such conformity &nbsp;assessment and the relevant information on the scope of designation of each such body. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c306"><span class="c0">4. Nothing in this Article shall preclude a Party from requiring that conformity assessment in &nbsp;relation to specific products is performed by its specified government authorities. If a Party requires &nbsp;that conformity assessment is performed by its specified government authorities, that Party shall: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c52"><span class="c0">(a) limit the conformity assessment fees to the approximate cost of the services rendered and, at &nbsp;the request of an applicant for conformity assessment, explain how any fees it imposes for that &nbsp;conformity assessment are limited to the approximate cost of services rendered; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(b) make publicly available the conformity assessment fees. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c23"><span class="c0">5. Notwithstanding paragraphs 2 to 4, each Party shall accept a supplier&rsquo;s declaration of &nbsp;conformity as proof of compliance with its technical regulations in those product areas where it does &nbsp;so on the date of entry into force of this Agreement.</span></p><p class="c328"><span class="c0">56 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c248"><span class="c0">6. Each Party shall publish and maintain a list of the product areas referred to in paragraph 5 for &nbsp;information purposes, together with the references to the applicable technical regulations. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c2"><span class="c0">7. Notwithstanding paragraph 5, either Party may introduce requirements for the mandatory &nbsp;third party testing or certification of the product areas referred to in that paragraph, provided that &nbsp;such requirements are justified on grounds of legitimate objectives and are proportionate to the &nbsp;purpose of giving the importing Party adequate confidence that products conform with the applicable &nbsp;technical regulations or standards, taking account of the risks that non-conformity would create. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c221"><span class="c0">8. A Party proposing to introduce the conformity assessment procedures referred to in &nbsp;paragraph 7 shall notify the other Party at an early stage and shall take the comments of the other &nbsp;Party into account in devising any such conformity assessment procedures. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.7: Transparency &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c861"><span class="c0">1. Except where urgent problems of safety, health, environmental protection or national security &nbsp;arise or threaten to arise, each Party shall allow the other Party to provide written comments on &nbsp;notified proposed technical regulations and conformity assessment procedures within a period of at &nbsp;least 60 days from the date of the transmission of the notification of such regulations or procedures &nbsp;to the WTO Central Registry of Notifications. A Party shall give positive consideration to a reasonable &nbsp;request to extend that comment period. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c469"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall provide the electronic version of the full notified text together with the &nbsp;notification. In the event that the notified text is not in one of the official WTO languages, the notifying Party shall provide a detailed and comprehensive description of the content of the measure in the &nbsp;WTO notification format. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c365"><span class="c0">3. If a Party receives written comments on its proposed technical regulation or conformity &nbsp;assessment procedure from the other Party, it shall: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c311"><span class="c0">(a) if requested by the other Party, discuss the written comments with the participation of its &nbsp;competent regulatory authority, at a time when they can be taken into account; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c136"><span class="c0">(b) reply in writing to the comments no later than the date of publication of the technical regulation &nbsp;or conformity assessment procedure. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c265"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall endeavour to publish on a website its responses to the comments it receives &nbsp;following the notification referred to in paragraph 1 no later than on the date of publication of the &nbsp;adopted technical regulation or conformity assessment procedure. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c246"><span class="c0">5. Each Party shall, where requested by the other Party, provide information regarding the &nbsp;objectives of, legal basis for and rationale for, any technical regulation or conformity assessment &nbsp;procedure that the Party has adopted or is proposing to adopt. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c507"><span class="c0">6. Each Party shall ensure that the technical regulations and conformity assessment procedures &nbsp;it has adopted are published on a website that is accessible free of charge. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c685"><span class="c0">7. Each Party shall provide information on the adoption and the entry into force of technical &nbsp;regulations or conformity assessment procedures and the adopted final texts through an addendum &nbsp;to the original notification to the WTO. </span></p><p class="c377"><span class="c0">57 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c493"><span class="c0">8. Each Party shall allow a reasonable interval between the publication of technical regulations &nbsp;and their entry into force, in order to allow time for the economic operators of the other Party to &nbsp;adapt. &lsquo;Reasonable interval&rsquo; means a period of at least six months, unless this would be ineffective in &nbsp;fulfilling the legitimate objectives pursued. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c527"><span class="c0">9. A Party shall give positive consideration to a reasonable request from the other Party received &nbsp;prior to the end of the comment period set out in paragraph 1 to extend the period of time between &nbsp;the adoption of the technical regulation and its entry into force, except where the delay would be &nbsp;ineffective in fulfilling the legitimate objectives pursued. </span></p><p class="c617"><span class="c0">10. Each Party shall ensure that the enquiry point established in accordance with Article 10 of the &nbsp;TBT Agreement provides information and answers in one of the official WTO languages to reasonable &nbsp;enquiries from the other Party or from interested persons of the other Party regarding adopted &nbsp;technical regulations and conformity assessment procedures. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.8: Marking and labelling &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c778"><span class="c0">1. The technical regulations of a Party may include or exclusively address mandatory marking or &nbsp;labelling requirements. In such cases, the principles of Article 2.2 of the TBT Agreement apply to these &nbsp;technical regulations. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c747"><span class="c0">2. Where a Party requires mandatory marking or labelling of products, all of the following &nbsp;conditions shall apply: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c93"><span class="c0">(a) it shall only require information which is relevant for consumers or users of the product or &nbsp;information that indicates that the product conforms to the mandatory technical requirements; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c728"><span class="c0">(b) it shall not require any prior approval, registration or certification of the labels or markings of &nbsp;products, nor any fee disbursement, as a precondition for placing on its market products that &nbsp;otherwise comply with its mandatory technical requirements unless it is necessary in view of &nbsp;legitimate objectives; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c756"><span class="c0">(c) where the Party requires the use of a unique identification number by economic operators, it &nbsp;shall issue such a number to the economic operators of the other Party without undue delay &nbsp;and on a non-discriminatory basis; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c41"><span class="c0">(d) unless the information listed in points (i), (ii) or (iii) would be misleading, contradictory or &nbsp;confusing in relation to the information that the importing Party requires with respect to the &nbsp;goods, the importing Party shall permit: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c114"><span class="c0">(i) information in other languages in addition to the language required in the importing &nbsp;Party of the goods; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c897"><span class="c0">(ii) internationally-accepted nomenclatures, pictograms, symbols or graphics; and &nbsp;(iii) additional information to that required in the importing Party of the goods; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c40"><span class="c0">(e) it shall accept that labelling, including supplementary labelling or corrections to labelling, take &nbsp;place in customs warehouses or other designated areas in the country of import as an &nbsp;alternative to labelling in the country of origin, unless such labelling is required to be carried &nbsp;out by approved persons for reasons of public health or safety; and</span></p><p class="c533"><span class="c0">58 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c510"><span class="c0">(f) unless it considers that legitimate objectives may be undermined, it shall endeavour to accept &nbsp;the use of non-permanent or detachable labels, or marking or labelling in the accompanying &nbsp;documentation, rather than requiring labels or marking to be physically attached to the product. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article TBT.9: Cooperation on market surveillance and non-food product safety and compliance &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c18"><span class="c0">1. The Parties recognise the importance of cooperation on market surveillance, compliance and &nbsp;the safety of non-food products for the facilitation of trade and for the protection of consumers and &nbsp;other users, and the importance of building mutual trust based on shared information. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c596"><span class="c0">2. To guarantee the independent and impartial functioning of market surveillance, the Parties &nbsp;shall ensure: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) the separation of market surveillance functions from conformity assessment functions; and </span></p><p class="c25"><span class="c0">(b) the absence of any interests that would affect the impartiality of market surveillance authorities &nbsp;in the performance of their control or supervision of economic operators. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c69"><span class="c0">3. The Parties shall cooperate and exchange information in the area of non-food product safety &nbsp;and compliance, which may include in particular the following: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) market surveillance and enforcement activities and measures; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) risk assessment methods and product testing; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) coordinated product recalls or other similar actions; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c75"><span class="c0">(d) scientific, technical and regulatory matters in order to improve non-food product safety and &nbsp;compliance; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(e) emerging issues of significant health and safety relevance; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(f) standardisation-related activities; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(g) exchanges of officials. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c719"><span class="c0">4. The Partnership Council shall use its best endeavours to establish in Annex TBT-XX, as soon as &nbsp;possible and preferably within six months of entry into force of this Agreement, an arrangement for &nbsp;the regular exchange of information between the Rapid Alert System for non-food products (RAPEX), &nbsp;or its successor, and the database relating to market surveillance and product safety established &nbsp;under the General Product Safety Regulations 2005, or its successor, in relation to the safety of non food products and related preventive, restrictive and corrective measures. </span></p><p class="c422"><span class="c0">The arrangement shall set out the modalities under which: </span></p><p class="c9"><span class="c0">(a) the Union is to provide the United Kingdom with selected information from its RAPEX alert system, &nbsp;or its successor, as referred to in Directive 2001/95/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council &nbsp;of 3 December 2001 on general product safety or its successor; </span></p><p class="c646"><span class="c0">(b) the United Kingdom is to provide the Union with selected information from its database relating &nbsp;to market surveillance and product safety established under the General Product Safety Regulations &nbsp;2005, or its successor; and</span></p><p class="c38"><span class="c0">59 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c312"><span class="c0">(c) the Parties are to inform each other of any follow-up actions and measures taken in response to &nbsp;the information exchanged. </span></p><p class="c692"><span class="c0">5. The Partnership Council may establish in Annex TBT-ZZ an arrangement on the regular &nbsp;exchange of information, including the exchange of information by electronic means, regarding &nbsp;measures taken on non-compliant non-food products, other than those covered by paragraph 4. </span></p><p class="c442"><span class="c0">6. Each Party shall use the information obtained pursuant to paragraphs 3, 4 and 5 for the sole &nbsp;purpose of protecting consumers, health, safety or the environment. </span></p><p class="c485"><span class="c0">7. Each Party shall treat the information obtained pursuant to paragraphs 3, 4 and 5 as &nbsp;confidential. </span></p><p class="c675"><span class="c0">8. The arrangements referred to in paragraphs 4 and 5 shall specify the type of information to &nbsp;be exchanged, the modalities for the exchange and the application of confidentiality and personal &nbsp;data protection rules. The Partnership Council shall have the power to adopt decisions in order to &nbsp;determine or amend the arrangements set out in Annexes TBT-XX and TBT-ZZ. </span></p><p class="c669"><span class="c0">9. For the purposes of this Article, &lsquo;market surveillance&rsquo; means activities conducted and &nbsp;measures taken by market surveillance and enforcement authorities, including activities conducted &nbsp;and measures taken in cooperation with economic operators, on the basis of procedures of a Party to &nbsp;enable that Party to monitor or address safety of products and their compliance with the requirements &nbsp;set out in its laws and regulations. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c67"><span class="c0">10. Each Party shall ensure that any measure taken by its market surveillance or enforcement &nbsp;authorities to withdraw or recall from its market or to prohibit or restrict the making available on its &nbsp;market of a product imported from the territory of the other Party, for reasons related to non compliance with the applicable legislation, is proportionate, states the exact grounds on which the &nbsp;measure is based and is communicated without delay to the relevant economic operator. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article TBT.10: Technical discussions &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c204"><span class="c0">1. If a Party considers that a draft or proposed technical regulation or conformity assessment &nbsp;procedure of the other Party might have a significant effect on trade between the Parties, it may &nbsp;request technical discussions on the matter. The request shall be made in writing to the other Party &nbsp;and shall identify: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) the measure at issue; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">(b) the provisions of this Chapter or of an Annex to this Chapter to which the concerns relate; and </span></p><p class="c8"><span class="c0">(c) the reasons for the request, including a description of the requesting Party&rsquo;s concerns regarding &nbsp;the measure. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c609"><span class="c0">2. A Party shall deliver its request to the contact point of the other Party designated pursuant to &nbsp;Article TBT.12 [Contact points]. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c160"><span class="c0">3. At the request of either Party, the Parties shall meet to discuss the concerns raised in the &nbsp;request, in person or via videoconference or teleconference, within 60 days of the date of the request &nbsp;and shall endeavour to resolve the matter as expeditiously as possible. If a requesting Party believes &nbsp;that the matter is urgent, it may request that any meeting take place within a shorter time frame. In &nbsp;such cases, the responding Party shall give positive consideration to such a request. </span></p><p class="c436"><span class="c0">60 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article TBT.11: Cooperation </span></p><p class="c226"><span class="c0">1. The Parties shall cooperate in the field of technical regulations, standards and conformity &nbsp;assessment procedures, where it is in their mutual interest, and without prejudice to the autonomy &nbsp;of their own respective decision-making and legal orders. The Trade Specialised Committee on &nbsp;Technical Barriers to Trade may exchange views with respect to the cooperation activities carried out &nbsp;under this Article or the Annexes to this Chapter. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c209"><span class="c0">2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, the Parties shall seek to identify, develop and promote &nbsp;cooperation activities of mutual interest. These activities may in particular relate to: </span></p><p class="c619"><span class="c0">(a) the exchange of information, experience and data related to technical regulations, standards &nbsp;and conformity assessment procedures; </span></p><p class="c373"><span class="c0">(b) ensuring efficient interaction and cooperation of their respective regulatory authorities at &nbsp;international, regional or national level; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c288"><span class="c0">(c) exchanging information, to the extent possible, about international agreements and &nbsp;arrangements regarding technical barriers to trade to which one or both Parties are party; and </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(d) establishment of or participation in trade facilitating initiatives. </span></p><p class="c764"><span class="c0">3. For the purposes of this Article and the provisions on cooperation under the Annexes to this &nbsp;Chapter, the European Commission shall act on behalf of the European Union. </span></p><p class="c210"><span class="c0">Article TBT.12: Contact Points </span></p><p class="c28"><span class="c0">1. Upon the entry into force of this Agreement, each Party shall designate a contact point for the &nbsp;implementation of this Chapter and shall notify the other Party of the contact details for the contact &nbsp;point, including information regarding the relevant officials. The Parties shall promptly notify each &nbsp;other of any change of those contact details. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c295"><span class="c0">2. The contact point shall provide any information or explanation requested by the contact point &nbsp;of the other Party in relation to the implementation of this Chapter within a reasonable period of time &nbsp;and, if possible, within 60 days of the date of receipt of the request. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article TBT.13: Trade Specialised Committee on Technical Barriers to Trade </span></p><p class="c483"><span class="c0">The Trade Specialised Committee on Technical Barriers to Trade shall supervise the implementation &nbsp;and operation of this Chapter and the Annexes to it and shall promptly clarify and address, where &nbsp;possible, any issue raised by a Party relating to the development, adoption or application of technical &nbsp;regulations, standards and conformity assessment procedures under this Chapter or the TBT &nbsp;Agreement. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c94"><span class="c0">Chapter 5: Customs and trade facilitation </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.1: Objective </span></p><p class="c10"><span class="c0">The objectives of this Chapter are:</span></p><p class="c61"><span class="c0">61 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c782"><span class="c0">(a) to reinforce cooperation between the Parties in the area of customs and trade facilitation and to &nbsp;support or maintain, where relevant, appropriate levels of compatibility of their customs &nbsp;legislation and practices with a view to ensuring that relevant legislation and procedures, as &nbsp;well as the administrative capacity of the relevant administrations, fulfil the objectives of &nbsp;promoting trade facilitation while ensuring effective customs controls and effective &nbsp;enforcement of customs legislation and trade related laws and regulations, the proper &nbsp;protection of security and safety of citizens and the respect of prohibitions and restrictions and &nbsp;financial interests of the Parties; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c250"><span class="c0">(b) to reinforce administrative cooperation between the Parties in the field of VAT and mutual &nbsp;assistance in claims related to taxes and duties; </span></p><p class="c594"><span class="c0">(c) to ensure that the legislation of each Party is non-discriminatory and that customs procedures are &nbsp;based upon the use of modern methods and effective controls to combat fraud and to promote &nbsp;legitimate trade; and </span></p><p class="c477"><span class="c0">(d) to ensure that legitimate public policy objectives, including in relation to security, safety and the &nbsp;fight against fraud are not compromised in any way. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.1a: Definitions </span></p><p class="c151"><span class="c0">For the purposes of this Chapter and ANNEX CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic Operators] and the &nbsp;Protocol on mutual administrative assistance in customs matters and the Protocol on administrative &nbsp;cooperation and combating fraud in the field of Value Added Tax and on mutual assistance for the &nbsp;recovery of claims relating to taxes and duties, the following definitions apply: </span></p><p class="c152"><span class="c0">(a) &ldquo;Agreement on Pre-shipment Inspection&rdquo; means the Agreement on Pre-shipment Inspection, &nbsp;contained in Annex 1A to the WTO Agreement; </span></p><p class="c55"><span class="c0">(b) &ldquo;ATA and Istanbul Conventions&rdquo; means the Customs Convention on the ATA Carnet for the &nbsp;Temporary Admission of Goods done in Brussels on 6 December 1961 and the Istanbul Convention on &nbsp;Temporary Admission done on 26 June 1990; </span></p><p class="c559"><span class="c0">(c) &ldquo;Common Transit Convention&rdquo; means the Convention of 20 May 1987 on a common transit &nbsp;procedure; </span></p><p class="c810"><span class="c0">(d) &ldquo;Customs Data Model of the WCO&rdquo; means the library of data components and electronic &nbsp;templates for the exchange of business data and compilation of international standards on data and &nbsp;information used in applying regulatory facilitation and controls in global trade, as published by the &nbsp;WCO Data Model Project Team from time to time; </span></p><p class="c145"><span class="c0">(e) &quot;customs legislation&quot; means any legal or regulatory provision applicable in the territory of &nbsp;either Party, governing the entry or import of goods, exit or export of goods, the transit of goods and &nbsp;the placing of goods under any other customs regime or procedure, including measures of prohibition, &nbsp;restriction and control; </span></p><p class="c234"><span class="c0">(f) &ldquo;information&rdquo; means any data, document, image, report, communication or authenticated &nbsp;copy, in any format, including in electronic format, whether or not processed or analysed;</span></p><p class="c742"><span class="c0">62 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c768"><span class="c0">(g) &ldquo;person&rdquo; means any person as defined in point (m) of Article OTH.1 [Definitions] of Title XVII &nbsp;[OTHER PROVISIONS]</span><span class="c134">5</span><span class="c0">; </span></p><p class="c73"><span class="c0">(h) &ldquo;SAFE Framework&rdquo; means the SAFE Framework of Standards to Secure and Facilitate Global &nbsp;Trade adopted at the June 2005 World Customs Organisation Session in Brussels and as updated from &nbsp;time to time; and </span></p><p class="c831"><span class="c0">(i) &ldquo;WTO Trade Facilitation Agreement&rdquo; means the Agreement on Trade Facilitation annexed to &nbsp;the Protocol Amending the WTO Agreement (decision of 27 November 2014). </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.2: Customs cooperation &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c222"><span class="c0">1. The relevant authorities of the Parties shall cooperate on customs matters to support the &nbsp;objectives set out in Article CUSTMS.1 [Objective], taking into account the resources of their &nbsp;respective authorities. For the purpose of this Title [Trade in goods], the Convention of 20 May 1987 &nbsp;on the Simplification of Formalities in Trade in Goods applies. </span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall develop cooperation, including in the following areas: </span></p><p class="c842"><span class="c0">(a) exchanging information concerning customs legislation, the implementation of customs &nbsp;legislation and customs procedures; particularly in the following areas: </span></p><p class="c308"><span class="c0">(i) the simplification and modernisation of customs procedures; </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(ii) the facilitation of transit movements and transhipment; </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(iii) relations with the business community; and </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(iv) supply chain security and risk management; </span></p><p class="c853"><span class="c0">(b) working together on the customs-related aspects of securing and facilitating the international &nbsp;trade supply chain in accordance with the SAFE Framework; </span></p><p class="c686"><span class="c0">(c) considering developing joint initiativesrelating to import, export and other customs procedures &nbsp;including technical assistance, as well as towards ensuring an effective service to the business &nbsp;community; </span></p><p class="c537"><span class="c0">(d) strengthening their cooperation in the field of customs in international organisations such as &nbsp;the WTO and the WCO, and exchanging information or holding discussions with a view to &nbsp;establishing where possible common positions in those international organisations and in &nbsp;UNCTAD, UNECE; </span></p><p class="c759"><span class="c0">(e) endeavouring to harmonise their data requirements for import, export and other customs &nbsp;procedures by implementing common standards and data elements in accordance with the &nbsp;Customs Data Model of the WCO; </span></p><p class="c597"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c763"><span class="c81">5</span><span class="c77">For greater certainty, it is understood that, in particular for the purposes of this Chapter, the notion of &ldquo;person&rdquo; &nbsp;includes any association of persons lacking the legal status of a legal person but recognized under applicable law &nbsp;as having the capacity to perform legal acts.</span></p><p class="c103"><span class="c0">63 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c524"><span class="c0">(f) strengthening their cooperation on risk management techniques, including sharing best &nbsp;practices, and, where appropriate, risk information and control results. Where relevant and &nbsp;appropriate, the Parties may also consider mutual recognition of risk management techniques, &nbsp;risk standards and controls and customs security measures; the Parties may also consider, &nbsp;where relevant and appropriate, the development of compatible risk criteria and standards, &nbsp;control measures and priority control areas; </span></p><p class="c786"><span class="c0">(g) establishing mutual recognition of Authorised Economic Operator programmes to secure and &nbsp;facilitate trade; </span></p><p class="c116"><span class="c0">(h) fostering cooperation between customs and other government authorities or agencies in &nbsp;relation to Authorised Economic Operator programmes, which may be achieved, inter alia, by &nbsp;agreeing on the highest standards, facilitating access to benefits and minimising unnecessary &nbsp;duplication; </span></p><p class="c154"><span class="c0">(i) enforcing intellectual property rights by customs authorities, including exchanging information &nbsp;and best practices in customs operations focusing in particular on intellectual property rights &nbsp;enforcement; </span></p><p class="c504"><span class="c0">(j) maintaining compatible customs procedures, where appropriate and practicable to do so, &nbsp;including the application of a single administrative document for customs declaration; and </span></p><p class="c452"><span class="c0">(k) exchanging, where relevant and appropriate and under arrangements to be agreed, certain &nbsp;categories of customs-related information between the customs authorities of the Parties &nbsp;through structured and recurrent communication, for the purposes of improving risk &nbsp;management and the effectiveness of customs controls, targeting goods at risk in terms of &nbsp;revenue collection or safety and security, and facilitating legitimate trade; such exchanges may &nbsp;include export and import declaration data on trade between the Parties, with the possibility of &nbsp;exploring, through pilot initiatives, the development of interoperable mechanisms to avoid &nbsp;duplication in the submission of such information. Exchanges under this point shall be without &nbsp;prejudice to exchanges of information that may take place between the Parties pursuant to the &nbsp;Protocol on mutual administrative assistance in customs matters. </span></p><p class="c758"><span class="c0">3. Without prejudice to other forms of cooperation envisaged in this Agreement, the customs &nbsp;authorities of the Parties shall provide each other with mutual administrative assistance in the matters &nbsp;covered by this Chapter in accordance with the Protocol on mutual administrative assistance in &nbsp;customs matters. </span></p><p class="c748"><span class="c0">4. Any exchange of information between the Parties under this Chapter shall be subject to the &nbsp;confidentiality and protection of information set out in Article 12 of the Protocol on mutual &nbsp;administrative assistance in customs matters [Information exchange and confidentiality], </span><span class="c27">mutatis &nbsp;mutandis</span><span class="c0">, as well as to any confidentiality requirements set out in the legislation of the Parties. </span></p><p class="c824"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.3: Customs and other trade related legislation and procedures 1. Each Party shall ensure that its customs provisions and procedures: </span></p><p class="c243"><span class="c0">(a) are consistent with international instruments and standards applicable in the area of customs &nbsp;and trade, including the WTO Trade Facilitation Agreement, the substantive elements of the &nbsp;Revised Kyoto Convention on the Simplification and Harmonisation of Customs Procedures, the &nbsp;International Convention on the Harmonised Commodity Description and Coding System, as &nbsp;well as the SAFE Framework and the Customs Data Model of the WCO;</span></p><p class="c395"><span class="c0">64 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c775"><span class="c0">(b) provide the protection and facilitation of legitimate trade taking into account the evolution of &nbsp;trade practices through effective enforcement including in case of breaches of its laws and &nbsp;regulations, duty evasion and smuggling and through ensuring compliance with legislative &nbsp;requirements; </span></p><p class="c155"><span class="c0">(c) are based on legislation that is proportionate and non-discriminatory, avoids unnecessary &nbsp;burdens on economic operators, provides for further facilitation for operators with high levels &nbsp;of compliance including favourable treatment with respect to customs controls prior to the &nbsp;release of goods, and ensures safeguards against fraud and illicit or damageable activities while &nbsp;ensuring a high level of protection of security and safety of citizens and the respect of &nbsp;prohibitions and restrictions and financial interests of the parties; and </span></p><p class="c338"><span class="c0">(d) contain rules that ensure that any penalty imposed for breaches of customs regulations or &nbsp;procedural requirements is proportionate and non-discriminatory and that the imposition of &nbsp;such penalties does not result in unjustified delays. </span></p><p class="c754"><span class="c0">Each Party should periodically review its legislation and customs procedures. Customs procedures &nbsp;should also be applied in a manner that is predictable, consistent and transparent. </span></p><p class="c881"><span class="c0">2. In order to improve working methods and to ensure non-discrimination, transparency, &nbsp;efficiency, integrity and the accountability of operations, each Party shall: </span></p><p class="c426"><span class="c0">(a) simplify and review requirements and formalities wherever possible with a view to ensuring the &nbsp;rapid release and clearance of goods; </span></p><p class="c200"><span class="c0">(b) work towards the further simplification and standardisation of the data and documentation &nbsp;required by customs and other agencies; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c820"><span class="c0">(c) promote coordination between all border agencies, both internally and across borders, to &nbsp;facilitate border-crossing processes and enhance control, taking into account joint border &nbsp;controls where feasible and appropriate. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.4: Release of goods </span></p><p class="c461"><span class="c0">1.
