Each Party shall adopt or maintain customs procedures that: </span></p><p class="c48"><span class="c0">(a) provide for the prompt release of goods within a period that is no longer than necessary to &nbsp;ensure compliance with its laws and regulations; </span></p><p class="c645"><span class="c0">(b) provide for advance electronic submission and processing of documentation and any other &nbsp;required information prior to the arrival of the goods, to enable the release of goods promptly &nbsp;upon arrival if no risk has been identified through risk analysis or if no random checks or other &nbsp;checks are to be performed; </span></p><p class="c508"><span class="c0">(c) provide for the possibility, where appropriate and if the necessary conditions are satisfied, of &nbsp;releasing goods for free circulation at the first point of arrival; and </span></p><p class="c838"><span class="c0">(d) allow for the release of goods prior to the final determination of customs duties, taxes, fees and &nbsp;charges, if such a determination is not done prior to, or upon arrival, or as rapidly as possible &nbsp;after arrival and provided that all other regulatory requirements have been met. </span></p><p class="c66"><span class="c0">65 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c357"><span class="c0">2. As a condition for such release, each Party may require a guarantee for any amount not yet &nbsp;determined in the form of a surety, a deposit or another appropriate instrument provided for in its &nbsp;laws and regulations. Such guarantee shall not be greater than the amount the Party requires to &nbsp;ensure payment of customs duties, taxes, fees and charges ultimately due for the goods covered by &nbsp;the guarantee. The guarantee shall be discharged when it is no longer required. </span></p><p class="c387"><span class="c0">3. The Parties shall ensure that the customs and other authorities responsible for border controls &nbsp;and procedures dealing with importation, exportation and transit of goods cooperate with one &nbsp;another and coordinate their activities in order to facilitate trade and expedite the release of goods. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.5: Simplified customs procedures </span></p><p class="c122"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall work towards simplification of its requirements and formalities for customs &nbsp;procedures in order to reduce the time and costs thereof for traders or operators, including small and &nbsp;medium-sized enterprises. </span></p><p class="c21"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall adopt or maintain measures allowing traders or operators fulfilling criteria specified in its laws and regulations to benefit from further simplification of customs procedures. Such &nbsp;measures may include </span><span class="c27">inter alia</span><span class="c0">: </span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(a) customs declarations containing a reduced set of data or supporting documents; </span></p><p class="c284"><span class="c0">(b) periodical customs declarations for the determination and payment of customs duties and taxes &nbsp;covering multiple imports within a given period after the release of those imported goods; </span></p><p class="c309"><span class="c0">(c) self-assessment of and the deferred payment of customs duties and taxes until after the release &nbsp;of those imported goods; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c528"><span class="c0">(d) the use of a guarantee with a reduced amount or a waiver from the obligation to provide a &nbsp;guarantee. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c450"><span class="c0">3. Where a Party chooses to adopt one of these measures, it will offer, where considered &nbsp;appropriate and practicable by that Party and in accordance with its laws and regulations, these &nbsp;simplifications to all traders who meet the relevant criteria. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.6: Transit and transhipment </span></p><p class="c408"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of Article GOODS.4a [Freedom of Transit], the Common Transit Convention &nbsp;shall apply. </span></p><p class="c304"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall ensure the facilitation and effective control of transhipment operations and &nbsp;transit movements through their respective territories. </span></p><p class="c790"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall promote and implement regional transit arrangements with a view to &nbsp;facilitating trade in compliance with the Common Transit Convention. </span></p><p class="c410"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall ensure cooperation and coordination between all concerned authorities and &nbsp;agencies in their respective territories in order to facilitate traffic in transit. </span></p><p class="c591"><span class="c0">5. Each Party shall allow goods intended for import to be moved within its territory under &nbsp;customs control from a customs office of entry to another customs office in its territory from where &nbsp;the goods would be released or cleared.</span></p><p class="c299"><span class="c0">66 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.7: Risk management </span></p><p class="c779"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall adopt or maintain a risk management system for customs controls with a view &nbsp;to reducing the likelihood and the impact of an event which would prevent the correct application of &nbsp;customs legislation, compromise the financial interest of the Parties or pose a threat to the security &nbsp;and safety of the Parties and their residents, to human, animal or plant health, to the environment or &nbsp;to consumers. </span></p><p class="c171"><span class="c0">2. Customs controls, other than random checks, shall primarily be based on risk analysis using &nbsp;electronic data-processing techniques. </span></p><p class="c407"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall design and apply risk management in such a manner as to avoid arbitrary or &nbsp;unjustifiable discrimination, or disguised restrictions to international trade. </span></p><p class="c613"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall concentrate customs controls and other relevant border controls on high-risk &nbsp;consignments and shall expedite the release of low-risk consignments. Each Party may also select &nbsp;consignments for such controls on a random basis as part of its risk management. </span></p><p class="c86"><span class="c0">5. Each Party shall base risk management on the assessment of risk through appropriate &nbsp;selectivity criteria. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.8: Post-clearance audit </span></p><p class="c430"><span class="c0">1. With a view to expediting the release of goods, each Party shall adopt or maintain post clearance audit to ensure compliance with customs and other related laws and regulations. </span></p><p class="c894"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall select persons and consignments for post-clearance audits in a risk-based &nbsp;manner, which may include using appropriate selectivity criteria. Each Party shall conduct post clearance audits in a transparent manner. Where a person is involved in the audit process and &nbsp;conclusive results have been achieved, the Party shall notify the person whose record is audited of &nbsp;the results, the person&rsquo;s rights and obligations and the reasons for the results, without delay. </span></p><p class="c813"><span class="c0">3. The information obtained in post-clearance audits may be used in further administrative or &nbsp;judicial proceedings. </span></p><p class="c389"><span class="c0">4. The Parties shall, wherever practicable, use the results of post-clearance audit for risk &nbsp;management purposes. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.9: Authorised Economic Operators </span></p><p class="c628"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall maintain a partnership programme for operators who meet the specified &nbsp;criteria in Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic Operators]. </span></p><p class="c362"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall recognise their respective programmes for Authorised Economic Operators &nbsp;in accordance with Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic Operators]. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.10: Publication and availability of information </span></p><p class="c249"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall ensure that its customs legislation and other trade-related laws and &nbsp;regulations, as well as its general administrative procedures and relevant information of general &nbsp;application that relate to trade, are published and readily available to any interested person in an &nbsp;easily accessible manner, including, as appropriate, through the Internet.</span></p><p class="c626"><span class="c0">67 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c88"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall promptly publish new legislation and general procedures related to customs &nbsp;and trade facilitation issues as early as possible prior to the entry into force of any such legislation or &nbsp;procedures, and shall promptly publish any changes to and interpretations of such legislation and &nbsp;procedures. Such publication shall include: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) relevant notices of administrative nature; </span></p><p class="c656"><span class="c0">(b) importation, exportation and transit procedures (including port, airport, and other entry-point &nbsp;procedures) and required forms and documents; </span></p><p class="c487"><span class="c0">(c) applied rates of duty and taxes of any kind imposed on or in connection with importation or &nbsp;exportation; </span></p><p class="c125"><span class="c0">(d) fees and charges imposed by or for governmental agencies on or in connection with &nbsp;importation, exportation or transit; </span></p><p class="c342"><span class="c0">(e) rules for the classification or valuation of products for customs purposes; (f) laws, regulations and administrative rulings of general application relating to rules of origin; (g) import, export or transit restrictions or prohibitions; </span></p><p class="c807"><span class="c0">(h) penalty provisions against breaches of import, export or transit formalities; (i) appeal procedures; </span></p><p class="c135"><span class="c0">(j) agreements or parts thereof with any country or countries relating to importation, exportation &nbsp;or transit; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(k) procedures relating to the administration of tariff quotas; </span></p><p class="c443"><span class="c0">(l) hours of operation and operating procedures for customs offices at ports and border crossing &nbsp;points; and </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(m) points of contact for information enquiries. </span></p><p class="c833"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall ensure there is a reasonable time period between the publication of new or &nbsp;amended legislation, procedures and fees or charges and their entry into force. </span></p><p class="c325"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall make the following available through the internet: </span></p><p class="c830"><span class="c0">(a) a description of its importation, exportation and transit procedures, including appeal &nbsp;procedures, informing of the practical steps needed to import and export, and for transit; </span></p><p class="c468"><span class="c0">(b) the forms and documents required for importation into, exportation from, or transit through &nbsp;the territory of that Party; and </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(c) contact information regarding enquiry points. </span></p><p class="c412"><span class="c0">Each party shall ensure that the descriptions, forms, documents and information referred to in points &nbsp;(a), (b) and (c) of the first subparagraph are kept up to date.</span></p><p class="c400"><span class="c0">68 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c337"><span class="c0">5. Each Party shall establish or maintain one or more enquiry points to answer enquiries of &nbsp;governments, traders and other interested parties regarding customs and other trade-related matters &nbsp;within a reasonable time. The Parties shall not require the payment of a fee for answering enquiries. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.11: Advance rulings </span></p><p class="c571"><span class="c0">1. Each Party, through its customs authorities, shall issue advance rulings upon application by &nbsp;economic operators setting forth the treatment to be accorded to the goods concerned. Such rulings &nbsp;shall be issued in writing or in electronic format in a time bound manner and shall contain all necessary &nbsp;information in accordance with the legislation of the issuing Party. </span></p><p class="c194"><span class="c0">2. Advance rulings shall be valid for a period of at least three years from the starting date of their &nbsp;validity unless the ruling no longer conforms to the law or the facts or circumstances supporting the &nbsp;original ruling have changed. </span></p><p class="c874"><span class="c0">3. A Party may refuse to issue an advance ruling if the question raised in the application is the &nbsp;subject of an administrative or judicial review, or if the application does not relate to any intended &nbsp;use of the advance ruling or any intended use of a customs procedure. If a Party declines to issue an &nbsp;advance ruling, it shall promptly notify the applicant in writing, setting out the relevant facts and the &nbsp;basis for its decision. </span></p><p class="c325"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall publish, at least: </span></p><p class="c316"><span class="c0">(a) the requirements for applying for an advance ruling, including the information to be provided &nbsp;and the format; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) the time period by which it will issue an advance ruling; and </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) the length of time for which the advance ruling is valid. </span></p><p class="c137"><span class="c0">5. If a Party revokes, modifies, invalidates or annuls an advance ruling, it shall provide written &nbsp;notice to the applicant setting out the relevant facts and the basis for its decision. A Party shall only &nbsp;revoke, modify, invalidate or annul an advance ruling with retroactive effect if the ruling was based &nbsp;on incomplete, incorrect, false or misleading information. </span></p><p class="c444"><span class="c0">6. An advance ruling issued by a Party shall be binding on that Party in respect of the applicant &nbsp;that sought it. The Party may provide that the advance ruling is binding on the applicant. </span></p><p class="c870"><span class="c0">7. Each Party shall provide, at the written request of the holder, a review of an advance ruling or of a &nbsp;decision to revoke, modify or invalidate an advance ruling. </span></p><p class="c871"><span class="c0">8. Each Party shall make publicly available information on advance rulings, taking into account the &nbsp;need to protect personal and commercially confidential information. </span></p><p class="c117"><span class="c0">9. Advance rulings shall be issued with regard to: </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(a) the tariff classification of goods; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) the origin of goods; and </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) any other matter the Parties may agree upon.</span></p><p class="c287"><span class="c0">69 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.12: Customs brokers </span></p><p class="c36"><span class="c0">The customs provisions and procedures of a Party shall not require the mandatory use of customs &nbsp;brokers or other agents. Each Party shall publish its measures on the use of customs brokers. Each &nbsp;Party shall apply transparent, non-discriminatory and proportionate rules if and when licensing &nbsp;customs brokers. </span></p><p class="c31"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.13: Pre-shipment inspections </span></p><p class="c825"><span class="c0">A Party shall not require the mandatory use of pre-shipment inspections as defined in the WTO &nbsp;Agreement on Pre-shipment Inspection, or any other inspection activity performed at destination, by &nbsp;private companies, before customs clearance. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.14: Review and appeal </span></p><p class="c83"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall provide effective, prompt, non-discriminatory and easily accessible &nbsp;procedures that guarantee the right of appeal against administrative actions, rulings and decisions of &nbsp;customs or other competent authorities that affect the import or export of goods or goods in transit. </span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. The procedures referred to in paragraph 1 shall include: </span></p><p class="c289"><span class="c0">(a) an administrative appeal to or review by an administrative authority higher than or independent &nbsp;of the official or office that issued the decision; and </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(b) a judicial appeal or review of the decision. </span></p><p class="c466"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall ensure that, in cases where the decision on appeal or review under point (a) &nbsp;of paragraph 2 is not given within the time period provided for in its laws and regulations or is not &nbsp;given without undue delay, the petitioner has the right to further administrative or judicial appeal or &nbsp;review or any other recourse to judicial authority in accordance with that Party&rsquo;s laws and regulations. </span></p><p class="c188"><span class="c0">4. Each Party shall ensure that the petitioner is provided with the reasons for the administrative &nbsp;decision so as to enable the petitioner to have recourse to appeal or review procedures where &nbsp;necessary. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.15: Relations with the business community </span></p><p class="c130"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall hold timely and regular consultations with trade representatives on legislative &nbsp;proposals and general procedures related to customs and trade facilitation issues. To that end, &nbsp;appropriate consultation between administrations and the business community shall be maintained &nbsp;by each Party. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c877"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall ensure that its customs and related requirements and procedures continue &nbsp;to meet the needs of the trading community, follow best practices, and restrict trade as little as &nbsp;possible. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.16: Temporary admission </span></p><p class="c812"><span class="c0">1. For the purposes of this Article, &lsquo;temporary admission&rsquo; means the customs procedure under &nbsp;which certain goods, including means of transport, can be brought into a customs territory with &nbsp;conditional relief from the payment of import duties and taxes and without the application of import &nbsp;prohibitions or restrictions of an economic character, on the condition that the goods are imported </span></p><p class="c626"><span class="c0">70 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c193"><span class="c0">for a specific purpose and are intended for re-exportation within a specified period without having &nbsp;undergone any change except normal depreciation due to the use made of those goods. </span></p><p class="c123"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall grant temporary admission, with total conditional relief from import duties &nbsp;and taxes and without application of import restrictions or prohibitions of economic character, as &nbsp;provided for in its laws and regulations, to the following types of goods: </span></p><p class="c684"><span class="c0">(a) goods for display or use at exhibitions, fairs, meetings or similar events (goods intended for &nbsp;display or demonstration at an event; goods intended for use in connection with the display of &nbsp;foreign products at an event; equipment including interpretation equipment, sound and image &nbsp;recording apparatus and films of an educational, scientific or cultural character intended for use &nbsp;at international meetings, conferences or congresses); products obtained incidentally during &nbsp;the event from temporarily imported goods, as a result of the demonstration of displayed &nbsp;machinery or apparatus; </span></p><p class="c372"><span class="c0">(b) professional equipment (equipment for the press, for sound or television broadcasting which is &nbsp;necessary for representatives of the press, of broadcasting or television organisations visiting &nbsp;the territory of another country for purposes of reporting, in order to transmit or record &nbsp;material for specified programmes; cinematographic equipment necessary for a person visiting &nbsp;the territory of another country in order to make a specified film or films; any other equipment &nbsp;necessary for the exercise of the calling, trade or profession of a person visiting the territory of &nbsp;another country to perform a specified task, insofar as it is not to be used for the industrial &nbsp;manufacture or packaging of goods or (except in the case of hand tools) for the exploitation of &nbsp;natural resources, for the construction, repair or maintenance of buildings or for earth moving &nbsp;and like projects; ancillary apparatus for the equipment mentioned above, and accessories &nbsp;therefor); component parts imported for repair of professional equipment temporarily &nbsp;admitted; </span></p><p class="c186"><span class="c0">(c) goods imported in connection with a commercial operation but whose importation does not in &nbsp;itself constitute a commercial operation (packings which are imported filled for re-exportation &nbsp;empty or filled, or are imported empty for re-exportation filled; containers, whether or not filled &nbsp;with goods, and accessories and equipment for temporarily admitted containers, which are &nbsp;either imported with a container to be re-exported separately or with another container, or are &nbsp;imported separately to be re-exported with a container and component parts intended for the &nbsp;repair of containers granted temporary admission; pallets; samples; advertising films; other &nbsp;goods imported in connection with a commercial operation); </span></p><p class="c51"><span class="c0">(d) goods imported in connection with a manufacturing operation (matrices, blocks, plates, moulds, &nbsp;drawings, plans, models and other similar articles; measuring, controlling and checking &nbsp;instruments and other similar articles; special tools and instruments, imported for use during a &nbsp;manufacturing process); replacement means of production (instruments, apparatus and &nbsp;machines made available to a customer by a supplier or repairer, pending the delivery or repair &nbsp;of similar goods); </span></p><p class="c350"><span class="c0">(e) goods imported exclusively for educational, scientific or cultural purposes (scientific equipment, &nbsp;pedagogic material, welfare material for seafarers, and any other goods imported in connection &nbsp;with educational, scientific or cultural activities); spare parts for scientific equipment and &nbsp;pedagogic material which has been granted temporary admission; tools specially designed for &nbsp;the maintenance, checking, gauging or repair of such equipment;</span></p><p class="c218"><span class="c0">71 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c893"><span class="c0">(f) personal effects (all articles, new or used, which a traveller may reasonably require for his or &nbsp;her personal use during the journey, taking into account all the circumstances of the journey, &nbsp;but excluding any goods imported for commercial purposes); goods imported for sports &nbsp;purposes (sports requisites and other articles for use by travellers in sports contests or &nbsp;demonstrations or for training in the territory of temporary admission); </span></p><p class="c777"><span class="c0">(g) tourist publicity material (goods imported for the purpose of encouraging the public to visit &nbsp;another foreign country, in particular in order to attend cultural, religious, touristic, sporting or &nbsp;professional meetings or demonstrations held there); </span></p><p class="c264"><span class="c0">(h) goods imported for humanitarian purposes (medical, surgical and laboratory equipment and &nbsp;relief consignments, such as vehicles and other means of transport, blankets, tents, &nbsp;prefabricated houses or other goods of prime necessity, forwarded as aid to those affected by &nbsp;natural disaster and similar catastrophes); and </span></p><p class="c547"><span class="c0">(i) animals imported for specific purposes (dressage, training, breeding, shoeing or weighing, &nbsp;veterinary treatment, testing (for example, with a view to purchase), participation in shows, &nbsp;exhibitions, contests, competitions or demonstrations, entertainment (circus animals, etc.), &nbsp;touring (including pet animals of travellers), exercise of function (police dogs or horses; detector &nbsp;dogs, dogs for the blind, etc.), rescue operations, transhumance or grazing, performance of &nbsp;work or transport, medical purposes (delivery of snake poison, etc.). </span></p><p class="c238"><span class="c0">3. Each Party shall, for the temporary admission of the goods referred to in paragraph 2 and &nbsp;regardless of their origin, accept a carnet as prescribed for the purposes of the ATA and Istanbul &nbsp;Conventions issued in the other Party, endorsed there and guaranteed by an association forming part &nbsp;of the international guarantee chain, certified by the competent authorities and valid in the customs &nbsp;territory of the importing Party. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS 17. Single window </span></p><p class="c767"><span class="c0">Each Party shall endeavour to establish a single window that enables traders to submit documentation &nbsp;or data required for importation, exportation, or transit of goods through a single entry point to the &nbsp;participating authorities or agencies. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS 18. Facilitation of roll-on, roll-off traffic </span></p><p class="c578"><span class="c0">1. In recognition of the high volume of sea-crossings and, in particular, the high volume of roll &nbsp;on, roll off traffic between their respective customsterritories, the Parties agree to cooperate in order &nbsp;to facilitate such traffic as well as other alternative modes of traffic. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c35"><span class="c0">2. The Parties acknowledge: </span></p><p class="c177"><span class="c0">(a) the right of each Party to adopt trade facilitating customs formalities and procedures for traffic &nbsp;between the Parties within their respective legal frameworks; and </span></p><p class="c875"><span class="c0">(b) the right of ports, port authorities and operators to act, within the legal orders of their &nbsp;respective Parties, in accordance with their rules and their operating and business models. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c353"><span class="c0">3. To this effect the Parties:</span></p><p class="c798"><span class="c0">72 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c201"><span class="c0">(a) shall adopt or maintain procedures allowing for the submission of import documentation and &nbsp;other required information, including manifests, in order to begin processing prior to the arrival &nbsp;of goods with a view to expediting the release of goods upon arrival; and </span></p><p class="c541"><span class="c0">(b) undertake to facilitate the use by operators of the transit procedure, including simplifications &nbsp;of the transit procedure as provided for under the Common Transit Convention. </span></p><p class="c370"><span class="c0">4. The Parties agree to encourage cooperation between their respective customs authorities on &nbsp;bilateral sea-crossing routes, and to exchange information on the functioning of ports handling traffic &nbsp;between them and on the applicable rules and procedures. They will make public, and promote &nbsp;knowledge by operators of, information on the measures they have in place and the processes &nbsp;established by ports to facilitate such traffic. </span></p><p class="c534"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.19: Administrative cooperation in VAT and mutual assistance for recovery of taxes &nbsp;and duties </span></p><p class="c220"><span class="c0">The competent authorities of the Parties shall cooperate with each other to ensure compliance with &nbsp;VAT legislation and in recovering claims relating to taxes and duties in accordance with the Protocol &nbsp;on administrative cooperation and combating fraud in the field of Value Added Tax and on mutual &nbsp;assistance for the recovery of claims relating to taxes and duties. </span></p><p class="c766"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS. 20: Trade Specialised Committee on Customs Cooperation and Rules of Origin &nbsp;1. The Trade Specialised Committee on Customs Cooperation and Rules of Origin shall: &nbsp;(a) hold regular consultations; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c363"><span class="c0">(b) in relation to the review of the provisions of the Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic &nbsp;Operators]: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c17"><span class="c0">(i) jointly validate programme members to identify strengths and weaknesses in &nbsp;implementing Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic Operators]; and </span></p><p class="c308"><span class="c0">(ii) exchange views on data to be shared and treatment of operators. </span></p><p class="c661"><span class="c0">2. The Trade Specialised Committee on Customs Cooperation and Rules of Origin may adopt &nbsp;decisions or recommendations: </span></p><p class="c380"><span class="c0">(a) on the exchange of customs-related information, on mutual recognition of risk management &nbsp;techniques, risk standards and controls, customs security measures, on advanced rulings, on &nbsp;common approaches to customs valuation and on other issues related to the implementation &nbsp;of this Chapter; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c834"><span class="c0">(b) on the arrangements relating to the automatic exchange of information as referred to in Article &nbsp;10 [Automatic exchange of information] of the Protocol on mutual administrative assistance in &nbsp;customs matters, and on other issues relating to the implementation of that Protocol; </span></p><p class="c525"><span class="c0">(c) on any issues relating to the implementation of the Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic &nbsp;Operators]; and </span></p><p class="c865"><span class="c0">(d) on the procedures for the consultation established in Article ORIG.26 [Denial of preferential &nbsp;tariff treatment] on any technical or administrative matters relating to the implementation of </span></p><p class="c299"><span class="c0">73 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c892"><span class="c0">Chapter 2 [Rules of Origin] of this Title, including on interpretative notes aimed at ensuring the &nbsp;uniform administration of the rules of origin. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article CUSTMS.21: Amendments </span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0">1. The Partnership Council may amend: </span></p><p class="c463"><span class="c0">(a) Annex CUSTMS-1 [Authorised Economic Operators], the Protocol on mutual administrative &nbsp;assistance in customs matters and the list of goods set out in paragraph 2 of CUSTMS.16 &nbsp;[Temporary admission]; and </span></p><p class="c262"><span class="c0">(b) the Protocol on administrative cooperation and combating fraud in the field of Value Added Tax &nbsp;and on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to taxes and duties. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c715"><span class="c0">2. The Trade Specialised Committee on Administrative Cooperation in VAT and recovery of taxes &nbsp;and duties may amend the value referred to in Article 33(4) of the Protocol on administrative &nbsp;cooperation and combating fraud in the field of Value Added Tax and on mutual assistance for the &nbsp;recovery of claims relating to taxes and duties. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c27">TITLE II: SERVICES AND INVESTMENT </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Chapter 1: General provisions </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.1.1: Objective and scope </span></p><p class="c506"><span class="c0">1. The Parties affirm their commitment to establish a favourable climate for the development of &nbsp;trade and investment between them. </span></p><p class="c677"><span class="c0">2. The Parties reaffirm the right to regulate within their territories to achieve legitimate policy &nbsp;objectives, such as: the protection of public health; social services; public education; safety; the &nbsp;environment, including climate change; public morals; social or consumer protection; privacy and data &nbsp;protection or the promotion and protection of cultural diversity. </span></p><p class="c615"><span class="c0">3. This Title does not apply to measures affecting natural persons of a Party seeking access to &nbsp;the employment market of the other Party or to measures regarding nationality, citizenship, residence &nbsp;or employment on a permanent basis. </span></p><p class="c260"><span class="c0">4. This Title shall not prevent a Party from applying measures to regulate the entry of natural &nbsp;persons into, or their temporary stay in, its territory, including those measures necessary to protect &nbsp;the integrity of its borders and to ensure the orderly movement of natural persons across them, &nbsp;provided that such measures are not applied in such a manner as to nullify or impair the benefits &nbsp;accruing to the other Party under the terms of this Title. The sole fact of requiring a visa for natural &nbsp;persons of certain countries and not for those of others shall not be regarded as nullifying or impairing &nbsp;benefits under this Title. </span></p><p class="c353"><span class="c0">5. This Title does not apply to: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(a) air services or related services in support of air services</span><span class="c134">6</span><span class="c0">, other than: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c274"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c478"><span class="c81">6 </span><span class="c77">Air services or related services in support of air services include, but are not limited to, the following </span></p><p class="c217"><span class="c0">74 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c169"><span class="c0">(i) aircraft repair and maintenance services; </span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(ii) computer reservation system services; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c144"><span class="c0">(iii) ground handling services; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c635"><span class="c0">(iv) the following services provided using a manned aircraft, subject to compliance with the &nbsp;Parties respective laws and regulations governing the admission of aircrafts to, &nbsp;departure from and operation within, their territory: aerial fire-fighting; flight training; &nbsp;spraying; surveying; mapping; photography; and other airborne agricultural, industrial &nbsp;and inspection services; and </span></p><p class="c308"><span class="c0">(v) the selling and marketing of air transport services; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) audio-visual services; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(c) national maritime cabotage</span><span class="c134">7</span><span class="c0">; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(d) inland waterways transport. </span></p><p class="c397"><span class="c0">6. This Title does not apply to any measure of a Party with respect to public procurement of a &nbsp;good or service purchased for governmental purposes, and not with a view to commercial resale or &nbsp;with a view to use in the supply of a good or service for commercial sale, whether or not that &nbsp;procurement is &lsquo;covered procurement&rsquo; within the meaning of Article PPROC.2 [Incorporation of &nbsp;certain provisions of the GPA and covered procurement]. </span></p><p class="c268"><span class="c0">7. Except for Article SERVIN.2.6 [Performance requirements], this Title does not apply to &nbsp;subsidies or grants provided by the Parties, including government-supported loans, guarantees and &nbsp;insurance. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.1.2: Definitions </span></p><p class="c303"><span class="c0">For the purposes of this Title: </span></p><p class="c616"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c142"><span class="c77">services: air transportation; services provided by using an aircraft whose primary purpose is not the &nbsp;transportation of goods or passengers, such as aerial fire-fighting, flight training, sightseeing, spraying, &nbsp;surveying, mapping, photography, parachute jumping, glider towing, helicopter-lift for logging and &nbsp;construction, and other airborne agricultural, industrial and inspection services; the rental of aircraft with &nbsp;crew; and airport operation services. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c293"><span class="c81">7 </span><span class="c77">National maritime cabotage covers: for the Union, without prejudice to the scope of activities which may &nbsp;be considered as cabotage under the relevant national legislation, transportation of passengers or goods &nbsp;between a port or point located in a Member State and another port or point located in that same Member State, including on its continental shelf, as provided for in the United Nations Convention on the &nbsp;Law of the Sea, done in Montego Bay, Jamaica, on 10 December 1982, and traffic originating and &nbsp;terminating in the same port or point located in a Member State; for the United Kingdom, transportation &nbsp;of passengers or goods between a port or point located in the United Kingdom and another port or point &nbsp;located in the United Kingdom, including on its continental shelf, as provided for in the United Nations &nbsp;Convention on the Law of the Sea, done in Montego Bay, Jamaica, on 10 December 1982, and traffic &nbsp;originating and terminating in the same port or point located in the United Kingdom.</span></p><p class="c529"><span class="c0">75 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c201"><span class="c0">(a) &quot;activities performed in the exercise of governmental authority&quot; means activities which are &nbsp;performed, including services which are supplied, neither on a commercial basis nor in &nbsp;competition with one or more economic operators</span><span class="c134">8</span><span class="c0">; </span></p><p class="c774"><span class="c0">(b) &quot;aircraft repair and maintenance services&quot; means such activities when undertaken on an aircraft &nbsp;or a part thereof while it is withdrawn from service and does not include so-called line &nbsp;maintenance; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c251"><span class="c0">(c) &quot;computer reservation system services&quot; means services provided by computerised systems that &nbsp;contain information about air carriers&#39; schedules, availability, fares and fare rules, through &nbsp;which reservations can be made or tickets may be issued; </span></p><p class="c241"><span class="c0">(d) &quot;covered enterprise&quot; means an enterprise in the territory of a Party established in accordance &nbsp;with point (h) by an investor of the other Party, in accordance with the applicable law, existing &nbsp;on the date of entry into force of this Agreement or established thereafter; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(e) &quot;cross-border trade in services&quot; means the supply of a service: </span></p><p class="c74"><span class="c0">(i) from the territory of a Party into the territory of the other Party; or </span></p><p class="c297"><span class="c0">(ii) in the territory of a Party to the service consumer of the other Party; </span></p><p class="c572"><span class="c0">(f) &quot;economic activity&quot; means any activity of an industrial, commercial or professional character or &nbsp;activities of craftsmen, including the supply of services, except for activities performed in the &nbsp;exercise of governmental authority; </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(g) &quot;enterprise&quot; means a legal person or a branch or a representative office of a legal person; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c575"><span class="c0">(h) &quot;establishment&quot; means the setting up or the acquisition of a legal person, including through &nbsp;capital participation, or the creation of a branch or representative office in the territory of a &nbsp;Party, with a view to creating or maintaining lasting economic links; </span></p><p class="c294"><span class="c0">(i) &quot;ground handling services&quot; means the supply at an airport, on a fee or contract basis, of the &nbsp;following services: airline representation, administration and supervision; passenger handling; &nbsp;baggage handling; ramp services; catering; air cargo and mail handling; fuelling of an aircraft; &nbsp;aircraft servicing and cleaning; surface transport; and flight operations, crew administration and &nbsp;flight planning; ground handling services do not include: self-handling; security; aircraft repair &nbsp;and maintenance; or management or operation of essential centralised airport infrastructure, &nbsp;such as de-icing facilities, fuel distribution systems, baggage handling systems and fixed intra &nbsp;airport transport systems; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c649"><span class="c0">(j) &quot;investor of a Party&quot; means a natural or legal person of a Party that seeks to establish, is &nbsp;establishing or has established an enterprise in accordance with point (h) in the territory of the &nbsp;other Party; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(k) &quot;legal person of a Party&quot;</span><span class="c134">9 </span><span class="c0">means: </span></p><p class="c868"><span class="c693">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c231"><span class="c81">8</span><span class="c77">For greater certainty, the term &quot;activities performed in the exercise of governmental authority&quot; when &nbsp;used in relation to measures of a Party affecting the supply of services, includes &quot;services supplied in the &nbsp;exercise of governmental authority&quot; as defined in point (p) of Article SERVIN.1.2 [Definitions]. </span><span class="c81">9</span><span class="c77">For greater certainty, the shipping companies referred to in this point are only considered as legal persons </span></p><p class="c26"><span class="c0">76 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c169"><span class="c0">(i) for the Union: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c515"><span class="c0">(A) a legal person constituted or organised under the law of the Union or at least &nbsp;one of its Member States and engaged, in the territory of the Union, in &nbsp;substantive business operations, understood by the Union, in line with its &nbsp;notification of the Treaty establishing the European Community to the WTO &nbsp;(WT/REG39/1), as equivalent to the concept of &quot;effective and continuous link&quot; &nbsp;with the economy of a Member State enshrined in Article 54 of the Treaty on &nbsp;the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU); and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c755"><span class="c0">(B) shipping companies established outside the Union, and controlled by natural &nbsp;persons of a Member State, whose vessels are registered in, and fly the flag &nbsp;of, a Member State; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c857"><span class="c0">(ii) for the United Kingdom: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c347"><span class="c0">(A) a legal person constituted or organised under the law of the United Kingdom &nbsp;and engaged in substantive business operations in the territory of the United &nbsp;Kingdom; and &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c536"><span class="c0">(B) shipping companies established outside the United Kingdom and controlled &nbsp;by natural persons of the United Kingdom, whose vessels are registered in, &nbsp;and fly the flag of, the United Kingdom; </span></p><p class="c844"><span class="c0">(l) &quot;operation&quot; means the conduct, management, maintenance, use, enjoyment, or sale or other &nbsp;form of disposal of an enterprise; </span></p><p class="c219"><span class="c0">(m) &quot;professional qualifications&quot; means qualifications attested by evidence of formal qualification, &nbsp;professional experience, or other attestation of competence; </span></p><p class="c848"><span class="c0">(n) &quot;selling and marketing of air transport services&quot; means opportunities for the air carrier &nbsp;concerned to sell and market freely its air transport services including all aspects of marketing &nbsp;such as market research, advertising and distribution, but not including the pricing of air &nbsp;transport services nor the applicable conditions; </span></p><p class="c499"><span class="c0">(o) &quot;service&quot; means any service in any sector except services supplied in the exercise of &nbsp;governmental authority; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c592"><span class="c0">(p) &quot;services supplied in the exercise of governmental authority&quot; means any service which is &nbsp;supplied neither on a commercial basis, nor in competition with one or more service suppliers; </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">(q) &quot;service supplier&quot; means any natural or legal person that seeks to supply or supplies a service; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c488"><span class="c0">(r) &quot;service supplier of a Party&quot; means a natural or legal person of a Party that seeks to supply or &nbsp;supplies a service. </span></p><p class="c549"><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c852"><span class="c77">of a Party with respect to their activities relating to the supply of maritime transport services. </span></p><p class="c521"><span class="c0">77 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.1.3: Denial of benefits </span></p><p class="c300"><span class="c0">1. A Party may deny the benefits of this Title and Title IV [Capital movements, payments, &nbsp;transfers and temporary safeguard measures] of this Heading to an investor or service supplier of the &nbsp;other Party, or to a covered enterprise, if the denying Party adopts or maintains measures related to &nbsp;the maintenance of international peace and security, including the protection of human rights, which: </span></p><p class="c280"><span class="c0">(a) prohibit transactions with that investor, service supplier or covered enterprise; or </span></p><p class="c317"><span class="c0">(b) would be violated or circumvented if the benefits of this Title and Title IV [Capital movements, &nbsp;payments, transfers and temporary safeguard measures] of this Heading were accorded to that &nbsp;investor, service supplier or covered enterprise, including where the measures prohibit transactions &nbsp;with a natural or legal person which owns or controls any of them. </span></p><p class="c557"><span class="c0">2. For greater certainty, paragraph 1 is applicable to Title IV [Capital movements, payments, &nbsp;transfers and temporary safeguard measures] of this Heading to the extent that it relates to services &nbsp;or investment with respect to which a Party has denied the benefits of this Title. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.1.4: Review </span></p><p class="c505"><span class="c0">1. With a view to introducing possible improvements to the provisions of this Title, and &nbsp;consistent with their commitments under international agreements, the Parties shall review their legal &nbsp;framework relating to trade in services and investment, including this Agreement, in accordance with &nbsp;Article FINPROV.3 [Review]. </span></p><p class="c773"><span class="c0">2. The Parties shall endeavour, where appropriate, to review the non-conforming measures and &nbsp;reservations set out in Annex SERVIN-1 [Existing measures], Annex SERVIN-2 [Future measures], Annex &nbsp;SERVIN-3 [Business visitors for establishment purposes, intra-corporate transferees and short-term &nbsp;business visitors] and Annex SERVIN-4 [Contractual service suppliers and independent professionals] &nbsp;and the activities for short term business visitors set out in Annex SERVIN-3 [Business visitors for &nbsp;establishment purposes, intra-corporate transferees and short-term business visitors], with a view to &nbsp;agreeing to possible improvements in their mutual interest. </span></p><p class="c183"><span class="c0">3. This Article shall not apply with respect to financial services. </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Chapter 2: Investment liberalisation </span></p><p class="c107"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.1: Scope </span></p><p class="c885"><span class="c0">This Chapter applies to measures of a Party affecting the establishment of an enterprise to perform &nbsp;economic activities and the operation of such an enterprise by: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) investors of the other Party; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) covered enterprises; and </span></p><p class="c276"><span class="c0">(c) for the purposes of Article SERVIN.2.6 [Performance requirements], any enterprise in the &nbsp;territory of the Party which adopts or maintains the measure.</span></p><p class="c247"><span class="c0">78 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.2: Market access </span></p><p class="c682"><span class="c0">A Party shall not adopt or maintain, with regard to establishment of an enterprise by an investor of &nbsp;the other Party or by a covered enterprise, or operation of a covered enterprise, either on the basis &nbsp;of its entire territory or on the basis of a territorial sub-division, measures that: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) impose limitations on: </span></p><p class="c214"><span class="c0">(i) the number of enterprises that may carry out a specific economic activity, whether in &nbsp;the form of numerical quotas, monopolies, exclusive rights or the requirement of an &nbsp;economic needs test; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c588"><span class="c0">(ii) the total value of transactions or assets in the form of numerical quotas or the &nbsp;requirement of an economic needs test; &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c429"><span class="c0">(iii) the total number of operations or on the total quantity of output expressed in terms of &nbsp;designated numerical units in the form of quotas or the requirement of an economic &nbsp;needs test;</span><span class="c134">10 11</span><span class="c532">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c791"><span class="c0">(iv) the participation of foreign capital in terms of maximum percentage limit on foreign &nbsp;shareholding or the total value of individual or aggregate foreign investment; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c746"><span class="c0">(v) the total number of natural persons that may be employed in a particular sector or that &nbsp;an enterprise may employ and who are necessary for, and directly related to, the &nbsp;performance of an economic activity, in the form of numerical quotas or the &nbsp;requirement of an economic needs test; or </span></p><p class="c289"><span class="c0">(b) restrict or require specific types of legal entity or joint venture through which an investor of the &nbsp;other Party may perform an economic activity. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.3: National treatment </span></p><p class="c87"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall accord to investors of the other Party and to covered enterprises treatment &nbsp;no less favourable than that it accords, in like situations, to its own investors and to their enterprises, &nbsp;with respect to their establishment and operation in its territory. </span></p><p class="c189"><span class="c0">2. The treatment accorded by a Party under paragraph 1 means: </span></p><p class="c348"><span class="c0">(a) with respect to a regional or local level of government of the United Kingdom, treatment no &nbsp;less favourable than the most favourable treatment accorded, in like situations, by that level of &nbsp;government to investors of the United Kingdom and to their enterprises in its territory; and </span></p><p class="c823"><span class="c0">(b) with respect to a government of, or in, a Member State, treatment no less favourable than the &nbsp;most favourable treatment accorded, in like situations, by that government to investors of that &nbsp;Member State and to their enterprises in its territory. </span></p><p class="c258"><span class="c693">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="c378"><span class="c81">10 </span><span class="c77">Points (a) (i) to (iii) of Article SERVIN.2.2 [Market access] do not cover measures taken in order to limit &nbsp;the production of an agricultural or fishery product. </span></p><p class="c153"><span class="c81">11 </span><span class="c77">Point (a)(iii) of Article SERVIN.2.2 [Market access] does not cover measures by a Party which limit inputs &nbsp;for the supply of services.</span></p><p class="c789"><span class="c0">79 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p><p class="c15"><span class="c16">This document has been agreed between the European Union and the United Kingdom and is provided for information only. &nbsp;No rights may be derived from it until the date of application. The numbering of the articles is provisional. &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c50"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.4: Most favoured nation treatment </span></p><p class="c882"><span class="c0">1. Each Party shall accord to investors of the other Party and to covered enterprises treatment &nbsp;no less favourable than that it accords, in like situations, to investors of a third country and to their &nbsp;enterprises, with respect to establishment in its territory. </span></p><p class="c387"><span class="c0">2. Each Party shall accord to investors of the other Party and to covered enterprises treatment &nbsp;no less favourable than that it accords, in like situations, to investors of a third country and to their &nbsp;enterprises, with respect to operation in its territory. </span></p><p class="c171"><span class="c0">3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 shall not be construed as obliging a Party to extend to investors of the &nbsp;other Party or to covered enterprises the benefit of any treatment resulting from: &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c543"><span class="c0">(a) an international agreement for the avoidance of double taxation or other international &nbsp;agreement or arrangement relating wholly or mainly to taxation; or &nbsp;</span></p><p class="c106"><span class="c0">(b) measures providing for recognition, including the recognition of the standards or criteria for the &nbsp;authorisation, licencing, or certification of a natural person or enterprise to carry out an &nbsp;economic activity, or the recognition of prudential measures as referred to in paragraph 3 of &nbsp;the GATS Annex on Financial Services. </span></p><p class="c729"><span class="c0">4. For greater certainty, the &ldquo;treatment&rdquo; referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2 does not include &nbsp;investor-to-state dispute settlement procedures provided for in other international agreements. </span></p><p class="c238"><span class="c0">5. For greater certainty, the existence of substantive provisions in other international &nbsp;agreements concluded by a Party with a third country, or the mere formal transposition of those &nbsp;provisions into domestic law to the extent that it is necessary in order to incorporate them into the &nbsp;domestic legal order, do not in themselves constitute the &ldquo;treatment&rdquo; referred to in paragraphs 1 and &nbsp;2. Measures of a Party pursuant to those provisions may constitute such treatment and thus give rise &nbsp;to a breach of this Article. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.5: Senior management and boards of directors </span></p><p class="c511"><span class="c0">A Party shall not require a covered enterprise to appoint individuals of any particular nationality as &nbsp;executives, managers or members of boards of directors. </span></p><p class="c45"><span class="c0">Article SERVIN.2.6: Performance requirements </span></p><p class="c141"><span class="c0">1. A Party shall not impose or enforce any requirement, or enforce any commitment or &nbsp;undertaking, in connection with the establishment or operation of any enterprise in its territory: </span></p><p class="c4"><span class="c0">(a) to export a given level or percentage of goods or services; </span></p><p class="c42"><span class="c0">(b) to achieve a given level or percentage of domestic content; </span></p><p class="c736"><span class="c0">(c) to purchase, use or accord a preference to goods produced or services provided in its territory &nbsp;or to purchase goods or services from natural or legal persons or any other entities in its &nbsp;territory; </span></p><p class="c839"><span class="c0">(d) to relate in any way the volume or value of imports to the volume or value of exports or to the &nbsp;amount of foreign exchange inflows associated with such enterprise;</span></p><p class="c636"><span class="c0">80 </span></p><p class="c6"><span class="c3">24.12.2020 </span></p></body></html>
